801 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Madlener v. Finley


No. 86-1278


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 796; 515 N.E.2d 697; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3305; 113 Ill. Dec. 712



September 24, 1987  
September 24, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her lawsuit that was filed against defendant clerk of a court that alleged he breached his fiduciary duty when he failed to deposit plaintiff's funds in an interest bearing account.


OVERVIEW: The litigant had filed a lawsuit against the clerk of a court that alleged he breached his fiduciary duty when he failed to deposit her funds in an interest bearing account. The trial court had dismissed the litigant's lawsuit, and she appealed. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the lawsuit, and remanded for further determination. The court agreed with the litigant that the clerk of a court, as a public official, was a fiduciary who owed a duty to protect and foster the interests of those individuals who had placed their trust and confidence in him when they deposited the funds. The court remanded for a determination of whether there were financial institutions that could accommodate the needs of the clerk of a court with a demand account that also paid interest. However, the court denied the litigant retrospective relief in the form of restitution that were based upon principles of equity and good conscience.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the litigants lawsuit that was filed against the clerk of a court that alleged he breached his fiduciary duty when he failed to deposit her funds in an interest bearing account. The court remanded for further determination on this issue.

 

802 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re No Name


No. 3-87-0206


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


160 Ill. App. 3d 613; 513 N.E.2d 1185; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3150; 112 Ill. Dec. 576; 14 Media L. Rep. 1883



September 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Iroquois County; the Hon. Dwight McGrew, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Iroquois County (Illinois), which denied its request to vacate an order that prevented it from publishing the name of a juvenile that was accused of murder and banned it from the courtroom for future proceedings in the matter pursuant to the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701-20(6) (1985). Appellee, the state attorney general, responded.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the newspaper contended that the trial court's orders were unconstitutional because they violated its First Amendment right to publish information that had already entered the public domain and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701-20(6) (1985) was unconstitutional on its face and as applied by the trial court. The attorney general filed motions to dismiss the newspaper's appeal for want of jurisdiction and for failure to file a complete record on appeal. Those motions were taken with the appeal. Specifically, the attorney general argued that the court was without jurisdiction to entertain the instant appeal under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1), 107 Ill.2d.R. 307(a)(1), because the matter was not an injunctive action in any way, shape, or form. The attorney general contended that the trial court's order to the press not to use the name of the minor in reporting on the court hearing was strictly administrative in nature and designed to protect the minor's safety. The court agreed. The substance of the orders were administrative in nature and derived from the inherent authority of the trial court to control the proceedings and, thus, ancillary to the Juvenile Court Act.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the newspaper's appeal for lack of jurisdiction.

 

803 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re E.G.


Nos. 87-1791, 87-2065 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 765; 515 N.E.2d 286; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3303; 113 Ill. Dec. 477



September 23, 1987  
September 23, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended May 24, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harry B. Aron, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part; affirmed in part and modified in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a minor who had refused blood transfusions on the ground that it violated her religious beliefs, appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found, in appellee state's suit under the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701--1 et seq., that she was medically neglected and, while finding that she was mature and had arrived at her decision independently, adjudged her a ward of the court.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the finding of medical neglect did not violate the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The Abused and Neglected Child Reporting Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2051 et seq. (1985), excepted certain religion-based refusals of medical treatment from the class of cases physicians were required to report as constituting neglect. However, there was no such exception in the Juvenile Court Act. Since no member of any other faith would have been entitled to an exemption from a finding of medical neglect under the Juvenile Court Act simply because of his religious beliefs, there was no equal protection violation. Further, the Juvenile Court Act did not violate the minor's free exercise rights under the First Amendment because the state had a significant interest in protecting immature minors. However, the trial court found that the minor had made a mature decision to follow her religious beliefs. This finding obviated any state interest in protecting immature minors. In the absence of such an interest, the minor could not be prevented from exercising a constitutional right solely because of her minority.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order appointing a temporary custodian for the minor. It ordered the minor to be partially emancipated, and granted her the right to accept or refuse transfusions.

 

804 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sykes


No. 85-3697


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 623; 515 N.E.2d 253; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3291; 113 Ill. Dec. 444



September 22, 1987  
September 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth L. Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of aggravated kidnapping and unlawful restraint. He was sentenced in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on the aggravated kidnapping charge to an extended term of imprisonment of 30 years. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed a 10-year-old child, and proceeded to take her through alleys and down a street, until she yelled for held and ran off. In reversing defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping, the court held that "secret confinement" the gist of kidnapping, had to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt. Since the victim simply was not confined or enclosed within any place or any thing and at no time was the victim "concealed, hidden, or not made public" during the entire incident, the state failed to prove that the victim was "secretly confined." Defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping had to be reversed. In light of strong similarities between the two offenses, evidence of a similar crime was properly admitted when the jury was instructed that the evidence was received solely on the issue of the defendant's identification, intent, motive, and design. It was not necessary to conduct a mini-trial of the prior incident in order to establish sufficient acts from which defendant's identity, intent and motive and design in the incident might be inferred, and for the sake of economy of judicial time, the court advised against such detailed evidence of other offenses.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping and the cause was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on the unlawful restraint conviction.

 

805 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hastings


No. 85-3574


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 714; 515 N.E.2d 260; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3299; 113 Ill. Dec. 451



September 22, 1987  
September 22, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Urso, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: A witness gave a statement to the police that he observed defendant urge the codefendant to shoot the victim. At trial the witness recanted his statement. The state impeached its own witness with prior inconsistent statements. Defendant was subsequently convicted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the state's impeachment of its own witness by the use of his out-of-court statements was proper under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 238 because the witness' testimony at trial was damaging to the state's case; (2) the witness' prior inconsistent statements were admissible as substantive evidence because the state met the four requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1 (1985); and (3) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1 (1985) was constitutional because the legislature was empowered to enact rules of evidence and that rule did not conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 238.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

806 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 2-86-0916


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


160 Ill. App. 3d 750; 513 N.E.2d 1154; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3169; 112 Ill. Dec. 545



September 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which convicted it of four counts of obscenity for selling obscene magazines in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20a(1) (1985).


OVERVIEW: A police officer purchased four magazines from defendant's store. The trial court convicted defendant of four counts of obscenity. Defendant argued on appeal that the Illinois obscenity statute was unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, and overbroad. He further argued that the trial court erred in prohibiting defendant from asking a question on voir dire about the jurors' beliefs on obscenity, in refusing to admit into evidence adult use ordinances from other communities within Illinois, and in failing to give to two of defendant's proposed jury instructions. The court affirmed. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(b) (1985), as amended, followed the federal obscenity guidelines and was not unconstitutionally vague, indefinite, or overbroad. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing defendant's proposed voir dire question because the question was aimed at indoctrinating the jury into believing that the regulation of obscenity was comparable to regulating a citizen's entry of adult bookstores. The ordinances were properly excluded because they did not constitute evidence of the statewide community standard for sexually explicit material.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on four counts of obscenity for selling obscene magazines.

Gavery v. County of Lake


No. 2-86-1202


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


160 Ill. App. 3d 761; 513 N.E.2d 1127; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3170; 112 Ill. Dec. 518



September 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that dismissed his libel action against defendants, county and official.


OVERVIEW: The doctor instituted a libel action against the county and the official, who was the county's personnel director, based upon a letter circulated by the official to county employees informing them that they could no longer obtain services from the doctor under the county's HMO due to numerous complaints made by employees about the doctor. The trial court dismissed the complaint on the ground that the action was barred by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1-101 et seq. (1985). The court affirmed. The court held that the official was entitled to immunity under the Act because his action in writing and circulating the letter was discretionary rather than ministerial in nature. The court also rejected the doctor's contentions that the Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the doctor's libel action against the county and the official.

 

808 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Geneva v. Metropolitan Airport Auth.


No. 2-87-0526


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


161 Ill. App. 3d 419; 514 N.E.2d 476; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3268; 112 Ill. Dec. 813



September 16, 1987  
September 16, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Michael J. Colwell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipal airport corporation appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied its motion to transfer venue of plaintiff city's complaint alleging that amendments to the act creating the municipal corporation were unconstitutional. The trial court held that the interests of judicial economy mandated that it was not required to follow Ill. Code Civ. P., 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-103(a).


OVERVIEW: The municipal corporation's principal office was in Du Page County. The municipal corporation filed a motion to transfer venue to Du Page County. The court reversed the order of the trial court denying the motion to transfer. The court held that because the municipal corporation was a public governmental corporation and was a defendant, Ill. Code Civ. P., 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-103 limited venue to the county in which its principal office was located, with the exception that in actions to recover damages to real estate venue could have been in the county where the real estate was located. The court found that the city requested equitable relief and did not seek to recover damages to real estate. The court held that the action had to be brought in Du Page County, the county in which the municipal corporation had its principal office, because there were no exceptions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which denied the municipal corporation's motion to transfer venue of the city's claims for equitable relief from alleged unconstitutional amendments to the act that created the municipal corporation.

 

809 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Robinson


No. 3-86-0648


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


160 Ill. App. 3d 366; 513 N.E.2d 603; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3112; 112 Ill. Dec. 189



September 14, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 15, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief, finding that there were no issues rising to a constitutional level. A jury convicted petitioner of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Prior to sentencing, petitioner filed a pro se motion to have his court-appointed attorney replaced. Petitioner argued that he had received ineffective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal. The trial court appointed counsel to represent petitioner. The court-appointed counsel later filed a motion to withdraw, stating that he had found no constitutional issues suitable for post-conviction relief. Following a hearing on counsel's petition, the trial court allowed the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Petitioner's allegation regarding the trial court's refusal to rule on a motion in limine was barred by the doctrine of res judicata, and his allegations concerning ineffective assistance of counsel were not supported by a clear and substantial showing. Thus, the trial court correctly determined that petitioner had not shown that his allegations of error rose to a constitutional level; thus, an evidentiary hearing was not warranted. The trial court properly allowed the counsel's motion to withdraw. Also, it was not error to assign the petition to a judge other than the one who presided over his trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the petition for post-conviction relief.

 

810 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Small v. Kusper


No. 87-0587


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


161 Ill. App. 3d 42; 513 N.E.2d 1108; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3214; 112 Ill. Dec. 499



September 14, 1987  
September 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action against defendant county clerk alleging that the requirement found in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. Para. 5--30, 6--67, and 7--43 (1985) that each primary voter disclose his party affiliation was unconstitutional because such requirement violated the right to privacy guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: The voters filed suit against the county clerk, alleging that the requirement found in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 5--30, 6--67, and 7--43 that each voter was required to disclose his party affiliation before voting in a primary election was unconstitutional because the requirement violated the constitutional right to privacy guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The trial court granted the clerk's motion to dismiss, holding that the right to privacy under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 did not encompass party affiliation. The voters appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that one's party affiliation did not constitute a privacy right under Ill. Const. art. 1, § 6. The prohibition against disclosing matters of a personal nature properly referred to the type of information contained in banking records and collected by credit associations, income tax services, and investigative institutions. The only public declaration that a voter was called upon to make was to choose which party primary to participate in. The imposition on the voter was minimal. Whatever burden was suffered by the voter was outweighed by the state's compelling interest in preventing election fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the voters' case against the county clerk, claiming that the statutory requirement that voters were required to disclose their party affiliation violated the right to privacy.

 

811 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bailey


No. 84-0809


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


164 Ill. App. 3d 555; 517 N.E.2d 570; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3594; 115 Ill. Dec. 159



September 11, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas R. Fitzgerald, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for murder and sentenced him to imprisonment for his natural life pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b), (a)(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed two people during a robbery. A witness saw him leaving the crime scene. The witness knew defendant. After his arrest and indictment, defendant was put in a lineup, although he did not have an attorney present. The police did not make a sustained effort to determine whether defendant had an attorney or to find an attorney for the lineup. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the identification. After a hearing, the trial court overruled the suppression motion. The trial court convicted defendant for murder. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in not suppressing his post-indictment lineup, the evidence did not prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and the mandatory life sentence was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that, although defendant was denied his constitutional rights and the trial judge misconstrued defendant's argument, the in-court identification had an independent source, and the lineup violation was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the challenge to the mandatory life imprisonment provision was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his sentence of life imprisonment.

 

812 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davidson


No. 5-85-0211


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


160 Ill. App. 3d 99; 514 N.E.2d 17; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3077; 112 Ill. Dec. 621



September 9, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Charles J. Romani, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information with and convicted in the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) of murder under the accountability theory, solicitation to commit murder and conspiracy to commit murder. The defendant was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 30 years for murder and 20 years for solicitation. The defendant appealed her sentence and conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the court erred in many respects, especially in convicting her for the offenses of conspiracy and solicitation where the state failed to sufficiently prove them. The state's evidence showed that the defendant was involved in an affair with her co-conspirator, that they had planned the murder of the defendant's husband, and that the co-conspirator killed the defendant's husband. The court held that the defendant's convictions for conspiracy and solicitation had to be vacated. The court noted that § 8-5 of the Criminal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-5 (1979), provided that no person was to be convicted of both the inchoate and the principal offense, and the committee comments to that section clearly stated that the provision applied to conspiracy and solicitation. The court held that the statute required that a conviction for conspiracy to commit murder was to be vacated where the defendant had also been convicted of murder. The court further held that statute applied to the solicitation conviction as well.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the defendant's convictions and sentences for conspiracy and solicitation, but affirmed the defendant's conviction and sentence for murder.

 

813 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Winfield


No. 85-3737


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


160 Ill. App. 3d 983; 513 N.E.2d 1032; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3196; 112 Ill. Dec. 423



September 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Howard M. Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for aggravated criminal sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and appealed. The court held that the trial judge had not rendered legally inconsistent verdicts. The court determined that the phrases "sexual intercourse" and "placed his penis on the sex organ" were immaterial to the charge and mere surplusage in the indictment. The court held that the victim's preliminary hearing testimony satisfied the statutory requirements for admissibility as direct evidence at trial because it conflicted with her trial testimony, she was subject to cross-examination on her prior statements, and the prior statements were made under oath. The court found no conflict between Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 238, 87 Ill. 2d 238, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, § 115-10.1 (1985) that rendered the latter unconstitutional. The court held that the testimony of a nurse was admissible as an exception to the hearsay rule because the statements were made for the purpose of medical treatment and diagnosis. The court ruled that the trial judge properly denied defendant's motion for a continuance to substitute counsel and that the state was not required to prove that defendant was over a particular age to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

 

814 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Carson Pirie Scott & Co. v. Department of Employment Sec.


No. 85-3359


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


164 Ill. App. 3d 530; 518 N.E.2d 161; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3592; 115 Ill. Dec. 636



August 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 22, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Employment Security, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judicial review to appellee employer under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 578 (1981) and set aside the department director's denial of the employer's application for cancellation of benefit wage charges. The employer cross-appealed the lower court's denial of an award of reasonable expenses of litigation.


OVERVIEW: An employer applied for revision of its benefit wages statement sent from the state Department of Employment Security and requested cancellation of certain charges. A hearing was held on the matter, but the state refused to cancel some charges. The employer sought judicial review, and the lower court determined that the charges should be cancelled. The employer moved for an award of expenses and attorney fees, but the motion was denied. The Department of Employment Security appealed the judgment of the lower court, and the employer cross-appealed the denial of his motion for expenses and attorney fees. On review, the court interpreted § 1508 of the Unemployment Insurance Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 578 (1981) and found that the statute provided standing for judicial review only to those employers who were entitled to, but did not receive, notice of the findings or determinations of the Department of Employment Security. The court found that in this case the employer was actually granted a hearing to which it was not entitled because of deficiencies in its application for revision and that it could not show that it was prejudiced in that process.


OUTCOME: The court held that the employer did not have standing to avail itself of review of its application for cancellation of benefit charges. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and dismissed the employer's cross-appeal for an award of reasonable expenses of litigation, including attorney fees.

 

815 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Murphy


No. 84-1443


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


160 Ill. App. 3d 781; 513 N.E.2d 904; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3172; 112 Ill. Dec. 295



August 26, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 14, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of deviate sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping after finding him competent to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with deviate sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping, he was assigned to a psychiatric unit. His attorney failed to obtain psychiatric records for use at a competency hearing and at trial. Defendant was convicted after a bench trial, and he appealed. The court reversed, holding that defendant received ineffective assistance of counsel because defendant's assignment to the psychiatric unit, coupled with other circumstances of the case, imposed a duty to investigate and discover the records. Due to the attorney's failure to investigate, the outcome of the fitness hearing was compromised and defendant did not assert an insanity defense at trial. The trial court did not abuse its discretion during the fitness hearing by finding the prosecution's witness more credible, but it did err by contravening Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104 --11(c) and imposing the burden of proving competency on defendant. The trial court did abuse its discretion by its finding on the day of trial that defendant was fit to stand trial when that finding was based on the court's own observation and lack of suggestion by defense counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that defendant was fit to stand trial and the judgment of conviction. The cause was remanded for a new fitness hearing.

Owens v. Manor Health Care Corp.


No. 4-87-0084


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


159 Ill. App. 3d 684; 512 N.E.2d 820; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3011; 111 Ill. Dec. 431



August 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which granted appellee nursing home's motion to dismiss appellant's action alleging that her ward was injured due to appellee's negligence on the grounds that appellant failed to attach a health care professional's report to the complaint as required by Ill. Code Civ. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Appellant guardian brought an action against appellee nursing home alleging that appellant's ward, while in appellee's care, was injured due to the negligence of appellee. The lower court granted appellee's motion to dismiss appellant's action. Upon appeal, the court reversed, holding that appellee was not engaged in a healing art with respect to this particular patient. The patient was not in a condition whereby he was being medically treated to restore him to a normal physical or mental state. Thus, the court concluded that the complaint sounded in ordinary negligence, rather than in healing art malpractice under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1985) as alleged by appellee, and compliance with the strict pleading requirements of para. 2-622 was not required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of appellant guardian's action alleging that her ward was injured while in appellee nursing home's care due to appellee's negligence because appellee was not engaged in a healing art with respect to the ward, the action sounded in ordinary negligence, and strict compliance with pleading requirements for actions sounding in healing art malpractice was not required.

 

817 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


Nos. 2-86-0563, 2-86-0577 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


160 Ill. App. 3d 315; 513 N.E.2d 468; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3106; 112 Ill. Dec. 54



August 24, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 5, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decisions of the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of obscenity in two cases.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obscenity in two separate cases for selling magazines that contained photographs of a sexual nature. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that: (1) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38 para. 11-20(b) (1987), which defined material which was obscene, was constitutional despite the fact that it did not define the term "prurient interest;" (2) the trial court did not err in refusing to admit an adult use ordinance into evidence; (3) the giving of a jury instruction that contained language that the jury could consider the material in question in light of their collective observations in life was a harmless error; and (4) the combining in each case of multiple charges of obscenity with general verdicts of guilty or not guilty followed by special interrogatory in reference to the obscenity of each magazine was proper because, although special interrogatories were not favored in criminal cases, their use actually benefitted defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of obscenity in two cases.

 

818 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cannady


No. 85-1587


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


159 Ill. App. 3d 1086; 513 N.E.2d 118; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3063; 111 Ill. Dec. 872



August 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas R. Fitzgerald, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful restraint, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and armed robbery. The circuit court sentenced defendant as an habitual criminal under the Habitual Criminal Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B--1 et seq. (1983). Defendant argued that the provisions of Act under which he was sentenced were unlawfully amended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that an examination of the legislative history revealed that the essential constitutional procedural prerequisites for the passage of bills under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) were not followed in the enactment of this amendment. The court affirmed and held that defendant waived this issue on review because he did not raise any objection at his sentencing hearing or in his post-trial motion that the amendment to the Act was unconstitutional. The court found that even if the issue was properly preserved for appeal, the legislative procedure was properly adhered to in passing the amendment. Defendant also alleged that his sentence of life imprisonment must have been reversed because the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of two prior convictions that contained the elements of a Class X felony as required by the Act. The court held that the state's petition set forth a prima facie case to sentence defendant as an habitual offender by fulfilling the requirements of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and held that defendant did not raise any objection at his sentencing hearing or in his post-trial motion that a statutory amendment was unconstitutional and thus waived the issue on review. The court affirmed defendant's sentence of life imprisonment.

 

819 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stice


No. 5-86-0035


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


160 Ill. App. 3d 132; 513 N.E.2d 463; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3081; 112 Ill. Dec. 49



August 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County; the Hon. E. C. Eberspacher, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty pleas to the crimes of rape, attempted aggravated kidnapping, and attempted criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to rape, attempted aggravated kidnapping, and attempted criminal sexual assault, however, he later filed a motion to withdraw his guilty pleas. The trial court denied the motion, and on appeal, the court upheld the trial court's order. The court held that because defendant failed to raise, in his motion to withdraw his pleas, the issue of the adequacy of the trial court's admonitions, the issue was deemed waived. The court further held that the prosecutor's recitation of the offenses in the language of the charges did establish that defendant committed acts constituting the offenses, so a factual basis for defendant's guilty pleas was established. The court also held that defendant had waived his right to challenge the voluntariness of his confession, which formed the basis of his guilty pleas. Finally, the court held that it was of no consequence that defendant's decision to plead guilty was influenced by the prospect of the admission of his confession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty pleas.

People v. Frisby

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of home invasion in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-11(a)(2) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of home invasion in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-11(a)(2) (1983). On appeal, he claimed that the State failed to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt in failing to establish two elements of the offense of home invasion, namely: (A) that defendant knowingly entered a dwelling, and (B) that defendant knew or had reason to know that one or more persons were present in the building. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the building that defendant invaded was a dwelling as defined by state law, in that it was used and intended to be used as a home and residence. Defendant also claimed that the State failed to establish his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt where the in-court identifications of defendant were unconstitutionally unreliable. The court concluded that the evidence in the record supported a reasonable inference that the witnesses had a sufficient opportunity to observe defendant before he was in police custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

821 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Naiditch v. Shaf Home Builders, Inc.


No. 2-86-0884


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


160 Ill. App. 3d 245; 512 N.E.2d 1027; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3099; 111 Ill. Dec. 486



August 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant home builders sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found in favor of plaintiff homebuyer in a breach of contract and breach of an implied warranty of habitability case and awarded actual damages and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The homebuyer purchased a new home from the builder that allegedly contained structural damages when built. The trial court found that the breach was wilful and wanton and awarded punitive damages. On appeal, the majority made it clear that there must be actual physical injury or actual damage to property to recover under a tort theory. Neither physical injury nor actual damage was proved. Where the construction defects did not cause physical injuries or damage to other property, tort liability could not be imposed on a builder for a breach of contract. Further, the essence of the implied warranties was that the builder was responsible for correcting any defects. Here, the builder was not allowed to respond to his obligation because he was not given an opportunity to correct the problem. The evidence was insufficient to support the trial court's decision to incorporate the corrections of the problems with the air-conditioning system into the judgment. On cross-appeal, an action for conversion was not the appropriate method of obtaining title to real property alleged to be wrongfully held pursuant to a contract provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.

People v. Carlyle


No. 86-1420


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


159 Ill. App. 3d 964; 513 N.E.2d 61; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3048; 111 Ill. Dec. 815



August 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert J. Sulski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced him to three years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced to three years' imprisonment. On appeal, defendant contended that he was denied a fair trial by repeated references to his arrest record. The State argued that because defendant made no objection to the testimony at issue and raised no issue concerning it in his post-trial motion, his assertion of error was considered waived unless it constituted plain error under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(a). The court agreed that the issue had been waived and concluded that the plain error exception to the waiver rule was not applicable. Next, defendant argued that the sentence imposed was arbitrary and capricious because the more serious offense of theft of a motor vehicle carried a lesser penalty. The court found the issue was waived because it was raised for the first time on appeal. The court also found the argument was without merit. The court examined the legislative history and concluded that the three-year sentence imposed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(b) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced him to three years' imprisonment.

 

823 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kaltsas v. North Chicago


No. 2-86-0568


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


160 Ill. App. 3d 302; 513 N.E.2d 438; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3104; 112 Ill. Dec. 24



August 12, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, residents of an unincorporated area, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint against defendant neighboring cities that refused to consent to the incorporation of the residents' village under § 2-3-5a of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1985).


OVERVIEW: After the cities refused to consent to the incorporation of the village, the residents brought an action against the cities alleging that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1985) deprived them of their constitutionally protected right to vote and diminished their property values in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The circuit court entered an order dismissing the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. On appeal, the court affirmed the order, holding that (1) because the legislature had broad power to regulate municipal boundaries, the residents could not assert an infringement of a fundamental right, and the state was not required to show a compelling state interest in justifying the consent requirement of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1985); (2) the residents had no claim for a violation of equal protection or substantive due process because there was no dispute that § 2-3-5a had a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose; and (3) in the absence of a fundamental right, procedural due process did not require a hearing on the issue of the cities' consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the residents' complaint against the cities that refused to consent to the incorporation of the residents' village.

People v. Winchel


No. 83-1247


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


159 Ill. App. 3d 892; 512 N.E.2d 1298; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3043; 111 Ill. Dec. 661



August 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Richard J. Petrarca, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, along with another man, was indicted for the murders of two individuals. Following a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), convicted defendant and sentenced him to natural life in prison. The other man was tried by a bench trial and was acquitted. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering two persons and sentenced to natural life in prison. Defendant contended the evidence was insufficient, alleged hearsay testimony was erroneously allowed, and his sentence was erroneous. Defendant also asserted seven different claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that (1) defendant, having failed to show or allege that the state knowingly used false testimony at his trial, was not entitled to a new trial, (2) defendant's statements on the night of the murders and his arrest were volunteered and properly admitted at trial, (3) there was no reasonable probability that the result of the trial would have been different had defense counsel used a different strategy or interviewed additional witnesses, and (4) the legislative history of the sentencing statute made clear that the legislature intended to make a mandatory natural life sentence of the controlling sentencing provision for those convicted of multiple murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of murder and sentencing him to natural life in prison was affirmed.

 

825 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gindorf


No. 2-86-0147


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


159 Ill. App. 3d 647; 512 N.E.2d 770; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3008; 111 Ill. Dec. 381



August 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Bernard F. Drew, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted her of six counts of murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1), (2) (1985). She was found guilty but mentally ill of two counts of murder and was sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1), (2) (1985), for causing her two children to ingest an overdose of sleeping pills. She was found guilty but mentally ill of two counts and was sentenced to life imprisonment. On appeal she questioned, inter alia, whether the evidence established that she was legally sane when she committed the offenses. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that there was a presumption that all persons were sane, and in order to raise the affirmative defense of insanity, defendant had to prove insanity at the time of the offense by a preponderance of the evidence. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3-2(b), 6-2(e) (1985). The trial court specifically found the experts' opinions less credible than the lay witness evidence on sanity, listing its reasons, before determining that she did not sustain her burden. Although defendant was depressed, she knew her conduct was wrong and refused to conform her conduct to the requirements of the law. Defendant did not have a history of mental disease, nor did she exhibit qualities of an insane person to those who came in contact with her daily before the incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

826 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cameron


No. 85-690


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


159 Ill. App. 3d 870; 513 N.E.2d 34; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3039; 111 Ill. Dec. 788



August 7, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1987. As Amended January 29, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert Sulski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the state's motion to dismiss the defendant's pro se petition for post-conviction relief following the trial court's conviction of the defendant of murder, armed robbery, and attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: The defendant and a co-defendant were convicted of murder, armed robbery, and attempted murder. The defendant filed a post-conviction petition for relief, contending that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at trial because the same attorney represented both him and a co-defendant when their defenses were inconsistent and antagonistic and that the defendant's trial attorney had a conflict of interest. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded with instructions, and held that it was necessary to remand the cause for an evidentiary hearing on the constitutional issue as to whether the defendant received effective assistance of counsel at trial. There was a possible conflict of interest in the joint representation at trial. By making an Anders motion to withdraw, defendant's appellate counsel did not raise the questions of severance or conflict of interest. At the defendant's post-conviction hearing, the defendant's counsel did not argue the possible ineffectiveness of either the trial or appellate counsel. The defendant's trial counsel asserted that he could not adequately cross-examine witnesses and that the state employed a guilt by association strategy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which granted the state's motion to dismiss the defendant's pro se petition for post-conviction relief following the trial court's conviction of the defendant of murder, armed robbery, and attempted murder, and remanded the case with instructions that the trial court appoint counsel other than the public defender to represent the defendant at an evidentiary hearing on his post-conviction petition.

People v. Treece


No. 3-85-0457


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


159 Ill. App. 3d 397; 511 N.E.2d 1361; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2978; 111 Ill. Dec. 66



August 4, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Angelo F. Pistilli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and affirmed as modified in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, armed robbery, aggravated criminal sexual assault, home invasion, and aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the state's use of peremptory challenges to remove black members of the venire violated his constitutional rights to have a jury drawn from a fair cross-section of the community and that the state's use of peremptory challenges to remove young persons under the age of 30 violated his constitutional rights. Defendant further argued that the trial court erred by allowing the state's motion, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 413(a)(vii), for the taking of hair, blood, and saliva samples from him without complying with constitutional requirements. The court held that the jury selection did not violate defendant's constitutional rights because defendant was not black and was, therefore, not a member of a cognizable racial group that was discriminated against by the state's peremptory challenges. The court found that the use of peremptory challenges to exclude jurors under the age of 30 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VI because people under the age of 30 did not qualify as a distinctive group. The court held that the samples were properly obtained under the trial judge's authority because the judge's authority was equivalent to a search warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, as modified in part, because defendant's contentions were without merit.

People v. Smith


Nos. 85-1884, 85-1903 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


159 Ill. App. 3d 156; 512 N.E.2d 71; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2950; 111 Ill. Dec. 167



August 3, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Roger J. Kiley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1985) and who was sentenced to a certain term of imprisonment, sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4 -103 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1985) and was sentenced to a certain term of imprisonment. On review, defendant argued that because possession of a stolen motor vehicle was a lesser included offense of theft of a motor vehicle, it was unconstitutional for the former to be punishable more severely than the latter. The court found that the amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1985), by imposing a more severe penalty for possession of a stolen motor vehicle than that imposed for felony theft, demonstrated a legislative intent that possession of a stolen motor vehicle be considered as a separate, more serious offense and not as a lesser included offense of theft. It was reasoned that the legislature could properly make such an evaluation. Thus, the court concluded that defendant's argument that the statute provided a disproportionately more serious sentence for a lesser included offense than provided for the greater offense was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentencing him to a certain term. Additionally, the court granted the State's request that defendant be assessed $ 50 as costs for the appeal.

Nos. 4-86-0821, 4-87-0039 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1009 (1985). The action sought damages due to the alleged negligent medical care and treatment rendered to the patient by defendants.


OVERVIEW: In 1984, plaintiffs filed a complaint seeking damages for personal injuries suffered by the patient and for the husband's loss of consortium due to defendants' alleged medical malpractice. Over the next two years, the parties engaged in extensive discovery. Beginning in July 1986, the circuit court issued several discovery rulings adverse to plaintiffs, and it denied the hospital's summary judgment motion. The case was set for trial in late 1986. Waukegan Port Dist. v. Petitioners of Proposed Vill. of Beach Park (In re Proposed Incorporation of Vill. of Beach Park)


No. 2-86-0784


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


158 Ill. App. 3d 207; 511 N.E.2d 858; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2830; 110 Ill. Dec. 681



July 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Wallace B. Dunn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a port district and a city, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed their objections to appellee petitioner's application to incorporate a village and denied their motions to intervene in the incorporation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The petitioners sought to incorporate a village which would contain less than 7,500 residents by the procedures established in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 2-3-5a (1985). Appellants, neighboring municipalities, objected to the petition and sought to intervene in the proceedings, but both motions were denied. Appellants claimed that para. 2-3-5a was unconstitutional because it denied them of due process. The court affirmed and held that although para. 2-3-5a provided for the consent of neighboring municipalities in the incorporation villages and cities exceeding 7,500 residents or cities with less than 7,500 residents, it did not violate appellants' due process rights. The court held that because appellants were municipal corporation, they could not seek the protection of the due process clause against the state. Additionally, the court found that an adverse party could only file a quo warranto action after the incorporation was approved by the electors of the proposed village, but not before the electors voted on the incorporation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision but remanded to submit the proposition to the electors.

In re Summary Suspension of Driver's License of Trainor


No. 4-86-0565


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


156 Ill. App. 3d 918; 510 N.E.2d 614; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2650; 109 Ill. Dec. 746



July 13, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County; the Hon. Charles E. Glennon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which denied his petition to rescind his statutory summary driver's license suspension imposed for refusing to take a breath test after being arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a car accident. When police arrived, they found that defendant smelled of alcohol. Defendant was placed under arrest for driving under the influence. Defendant refused to take a breath test. Defendant therefore received a statutory summary suspension of his driver's license. The lower court found the requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118.1(b) (1985) relative to implied consent had been met and denied defendant's motion to rescind. Defendant argued on appeal that the suspension had to be rescinded for failure to hold the implied-consent hearing within the statutorily mandated 30 days. The court agreed and reversed. The 30-day time period was mandatory under para. 2-118.1(b). This time period was the legislature's determination of what constituted a prompt hearing for due process requirements. Failure to hold the hearing within the required 30 days violated defendant's due process rights. The only appropriate remedy was to require the rescission of his suspension. The court held that para. 2-118.1(b) was constitutional and that it was not applicable to the lower court's power to stay pending appeal from a para. 2-118.1 hearing order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's petition to rescind summary suspension of defendant's driver's license.

People v. Abdennabi


Nos. 85-1365, 85-1410 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 979; 511 N.E.2d 719; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2796; 110 Ill. Dec. 542



July 6, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James J. Heyda, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and co-defendant sought review of judgments from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of conspiracy to commit aggravated arson, conspiracy to commit arson, attempted aggravated arson, and attempted arson. Defendant was also convicted of solicitation to commit aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant leased the bottom floor of a building, out of which he ran a grocery store. Defendant with co-defendant present told the witness his plan to burn down his store and offered the witness money to act as a lookout. On the night in question, defendant again offered the witness money to act as a lookout and told the witness to call him to wake him up and after the call, to open the side burglar gates on the store. The witness informed the arson unit of what was to occur. Upon review, the court found that the facts indicated defendants intended to attempt to commit arson beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the evidence indicated that defendants had a conspiratorial agreement to commit arson. The failure of the State to disclose a letter that recommended an award for the witness because he provided the police information that led to defendants' arrest was not a violation of the Brady rule. It did not deprive defendants of a fair trial and the witness was cross-examined at length about the possibility of receiving an award at trial. The court agreed that defendants' convictions for aggravated arson had to be reversed because the aggravated arson statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant and co-defendant's convictions for conspiracy to commit arson and attempted arson. The court reversed defendant and co-defendant's convictions for conspiracy to commit aggravated arson, attempted aggravated arson, and defendant's conviction for solicitation to commit aggravated arson. The court remanded the action for resentencing.

Cooper v. River Forest Firemen's Pension Bd.


No. 85-1083


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 944; 510 N.E.2d 1222; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2792; 110 Ill. Dec. 191



July 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pension board sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled that appellee employee was entitled to receive a pension based on the salary of a firefighter of the employee's rank as of the day that he elected to permanently retire rather than as of the date that he began receiving a disability pension.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a firefighter, was granted a disability pension in 1973. At the time, he was 47 years old and had over 21 years of active service. The employee elected to permanently retire from the fire department on January 1, 1982. The board ruled that the employee would be paid a pension based on the salary of a firefighter of his rank in 1973, the year he went on disability, rather than 1982, the year of his retirement. The employee sought review by the trial court, which ruled that the employee was entitled to receive his pension based on the salary of a firefighter of his rank at the time of his permanent retirement. The board sought review and the court affirmed. The court noted that the version of the Illinois Pension Act in effect at the time the action was commenced stated that the pension was to be computed based on the rank held by the employee on the date of his election to retire, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 4-113 (1985). The court rejected the board's claim that this section did not apply because the employee was not "in service" as of his retirement date, ruling that a firefighter who received disability benefits should be considered an in-service employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that the pension board was required to award the employee a pension based on what his salary would have been on the date that he elected to retire.

 

835 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dotson v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 86-0799


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 1036; 510 N.E.2d 1208; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2800; 110 Ill. Dec. 177



June 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert S. Porter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded damages to a decedent's estate for her wrongful death, permitted plaintiff father to recover for the wrongful death of his illegitimate son, and awarded damages to plaintiff injured party. The company admitted liability for the injuries and death that resulted from an explosion of a gas dryer that its employed repaired.


OVERVIEW: The court found that plaintiff husband could not separate a claim for loss of material services from a claim for loss of consortium in decedent's wrongful death action. The court concluded that it was reversible error to allow evidence of the quality of the husband's marriage to the decedent (material services) because the husband withdrew his claim for loss of consortium; therefore, this evidence was irrelevant to the issue of the amount of damages. Furthermore, the court found that evidence of his remarriage would have been properly admissible to limit his recovery for lost material services to actual loss. The court found that the failure to adequately apprise the jury of the fact of the husband's remarriage and the identity of his new spouse necessitated a new trial. The court found that to allow the mothers of illegitimate children to recover for their wrongful deaths while denying that right to their fathers constituted invidious gender-based discrimination that denied the equal protection of the laws. U.S. Const. amend. XIV; Ill. Const. art. I, § 18 (1970). Thus, the court found that the father was entitled to recover for his illegitimate son's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

836 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mau v. North American Asbestos Corp.


No. 4-86-0696


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


156 Ill. App. 3d 926; 509 N.E.2d 1112; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2651; 109 Ill. Dec. 273



June 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Luther H. Dearborn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's widow appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which held her in contempt for her failure to produce a list of witnesses before the trial of her wrongful death claim against defendant asbestos manufacturer. The widow argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1003(c) (1985) protected such matters from disclosure and that the list was privileged.


OVERVIEW: The widow filed a wrongful death action against the asbestos manufacturer. The circuit court ordered the widow to file a list of witnesses, including names and addresses, for use in voir dire. The circuit court also ordered that the list would be binding on the parties' presentations at trial. When the widow refused to comply, the circuit court held her in contempt, imposed a fine, and held that the trial would not proceed until the list was furnished. On appeal, the widow argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1003(c) (1985) provided that a party was not required to produce the names or addresses of witnesses. She also cited Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 201(b)(2), which provided that matters privileged at trial were also privileged during discovery, 87 Ill. 2d R. 201(b)(2). The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1003(c) (1985) applied only to discovery, not to trials. Moreover, a witness list was not "work product" privileged during discovery or at trial. Although the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in holding the widow in contempt, its order constituted an abuse of discretion because its scope was overbroad. The court vacated the order and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court held that the circuit court did not err when it found the widow in contempt for refusal to produce the witness list at trial. However, the court also held that the circuit court abused its discretion when it ordered that the widow could not call any witnesses not listed nor out of the listed order without its permission. The court vacated the contempt order and remanded the action.

 

837 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGeorge


No. 4-86-0332


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


156 Ill. App. 3d 860; 510 N.E.2d 1032; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2647; 110 Ill. Dec. 1



June 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Jerry L. Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, and vacated in part and remanded, sentence vacated, and cause remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Police officers purchased bondage magazines from defendant in an adult bookstore. The court reversed the obscenity conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded the cause for a new trial. The trial court erred in instructing the jury to use a state community standard in considering the magazines' value. The erroneous instruction was not harmless error because a rational juror, if properly instructed, could have accepted the expert witness' testimony and concluded that the materials had some limited value, either as an aid in achieving marital balance or as a safety valve to prevent criminal behavior. The jury instruction may have prompted the jury to discount the expert testimony and determine that the materials had value to the scientific community but no value to the jurors' community. The evidence failed to establish defendant possessed a book sold by another employee. The court rejected defendant's contention that the materials depicting ultimate sex acts, lewd exhibition of the genitals, and sexual violence were not obscene as a matter of law. In sentencing defendant, the trial court's creation of a class of disfavored offenders, adult bookstore employees, was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction for obscenity, vacated the sentence imposed, and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

838 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brandon


No. 86-0085


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 835; 510 N.E.2d 1005; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2776; 109 Ill. Dec. 937



June 22, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 13, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of attempted residential burglary under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38l, para. 8 -4, 19 -3 (1983), and sentenced him to nine years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion during voir dire and that it erred by not appointing independent counsel for his pro se motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court rejected both of defendant's contentions and affirmed the conviction. First, the court held that the trial court properly refused to ask prospective jurors whether they would be prejudiced against defendant because of his prior felony convictions. The proffered question was clearly covered by the jury instruction on the limitation of felony convictions in Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions, Crim. No. 3.13 (2d ed.), which was given to the jury at the end of the case. Second, the court held that defendant was not entitled to a new trial based on ineffective assistance of counsel because 1) defendant waived his claim to ineffective assistance of counsel pursuant to Ill. Code of Crim. P. § 116 -1, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 116 -1 (1985), 2) the allegations were unsworn, and 3) regardless, it was not manifestly erroneous for the trial court to determine that defendant's claim was spurious and to refuse to appoint new counsel for defendant's pro se motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Lake Louise Improv. Asso. v. Multimedia Cablevision of Oak Lawn, Inc.


No. 86-1941


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 713; 510 N.E.2d 982; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2760; 109 Ill. Dec. 914



June 19, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cable company appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff association a preliminary injunction that restrained the cable company from installing cable television facilities on the commonly owned property of the association in the association's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The association brought a declaratory judgment action concerning installation of cable television equipment by the cable company. The trial court issued a preliminary injunction restraining the cable company from installing cable television equipment on the association's property. The trial court predicated the preliminary injunction on a finding that the Illinois Cable Access Statute (Act), Ill. Rev.
