On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the trial court's finding was overly broad and if allowed to stand, could have affected the validity of other Illinois municipal franchises. The court did not rule on the constitutionality of the statute, but based its holding on the preliminary determination that the purpose of the proposed taking was a public rather than the private.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of a preliminary injunction.

 

840 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Board of Trustees


No. 86-2011


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 158; 510 N.E.2d 87; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2691; 109 Ill. Dec. 466



June 15, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board appealed from the rulings of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reviewed the board's action in terminating the pension benefits of plaintiff retiree, and held that the retiree was entitled to a refund of his pension contributions without setoff. The retiree cross-appealed the termination of his benefits after his conviction of a job-related felony, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 13 -- 221 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The retiree received benefits for years. The board summarily terminated the benefits upon conviction. On appeal, the court held that the trial court only had jurisdiction over the questions of law and of fact presented by the administrative record, and no new or additional issues could be framed by the pleadings, so that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 3 -- 110 (1985) precluded the trial court from considering the issues of a refund or setoff. The court held that the felony forfeiture statute served a valid public purpose by discouraging job-related criminal conduct by public employees and held that any contractual rights of the retiree, who began his employment after the statute was effective, were subject to the statute. The court then held that the retiree had a constitutionally protected property interest in his benefits, so that due process required that he be given reasonable notice and an opportunity to be heard prior to the termination. The court found that due process did not require a full plenary hearing and that the board could receive a copy of the conviction as prima facie evidence, but held that the retiree must be given an opportunity to raise relevant issues.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court that reviewed the board action. The court remanded the cause to the board for further proceedings in accordance with the retiree's due process rights.

 

841 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sweeney v. Citicorp Person-to-Person Fin. Ctr., Inc.


No. 86-1972


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 47; 510 N.E.2d 93; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2677; 109 Ill. Dec. 472



June 15, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon the motion of defendant lenders, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) certified two questions for appeal after the trial court denied the lenders' motion to dismiss a usury suit filed by plaintiff borrower.


OVERVIEW: A borrower obtained two loans, each from a different lender, at interest rates of 17.99 percent and 12.49 percent respectively. Both loans were secured by a second mortgage on the borrower's residence. The borrower filed usury claims against the lenders, who filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss. The court reversed and remanded for an order granting the lenders' motion to dismiss. The court rejected the borrower's argument that the unlawfulness of a loan had to be determined by the applicable law at the time the loan was made. There was no usury in the absence of a law limiting the rate of interest, and a particular rate of interest was illegal only if it exceeded the statutory limit applicable in the particular case. The borrower in fact was simply seeking a windfall, rather than protection from a usurious loan. The court thus applied the rule that the right to a remedy should be determined on the basis of the law at the time the suit was brought and judgment rendered. At the time the borrower filed suit, the state legislature had amended the Interest Act to exclude from the usury statute all loans secured by real estate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied the lenders' motion to dismiss, and the court remanded for the entry of an order granting the lenders' motion to dismiss a borrower's usury action. Because the court's answer to the first certified question disposed of the appeal, the court did not reach the second question.

Beverly Bank v. County of Cook


No. 85-3684


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 601; 510 N.E.2d 941; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2746; 109 Ill. Dec. 873



June 10, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, bank and company, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was entered in favor of defendants, county and others, in plaintiffs' action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief when the county denied plaintiffs' requested zoning relief for the development of a sanitary land fill.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought declaratory and injunctive relief when the county denied plaintiffs the requested zoning relief for the development of a sanitary landfill. Plaintiffs appealed from the trial court's findings that state law did not preempt the county's zoning authority as a home rule unit, and that the county was not estopped from exercising its zoning authority. The court found no express preemption in the Reclamation Act enacted under Ill. Const. Art. VII, § 6 (1970), so as to limit or deny the power of a home rule unit. The held that there was concurrent jurisdiction over sanitary landfill sites on the state under the Reclamation Act and on home rule units. Plaintiffs had to comply with both state and county regulations. The trial court correctly found that the county zoning ordinance at issue was not preempted by the Reclamation Act. The county's failure to object to the issuance of a mining permit to the company's owner was only nonaction and not a positive act. Estoppel would have been improper because the company's owner had failed to show a justified reliance on any conduct by the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which was entered in favor of defendants.

Decatur v. Waste Hauling, Inc.


No. 4-86-0754


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


156 Ill. App. 3d 630; 509 N.E.2d 716; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2612; 109 Ill. Dec. 55



June 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. James A. Hendrian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a waste hauling corporation, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant under a Decatur, Illinois, ordinance which prohibited refuse haulers in plaintiff city from collecting garbage at residences outside the district to which they had been assigned.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it created an irrational distinction between "residential" and "commercial" refuse pick-up accounts and because it acted to deprive defendant of a vested property interest. Further, defendant asserted that the trial court erred in striking its affirmative defenses although they had previously been addressed in ruling on defendant's motion to dismiss the ordinance prosecution. The city defended the classification on grounds it worked to limit the numbers of large, heavy garbage trucks present in primarily residential neighborhoods. By limiting the number of refuse haulers in such areas, the city continued, it was limiting congestion, noise, and damage to residential streets which were not built to withstand heavy truck traffic. The court held that the city had advanced valid reasons for the ordinance at issue. Likewise, the classification of "residential" property created by the ordinance was rationally related to promoting the public interest in limiting noise, congestion, and street damage in primarily residential neighborhoods.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for removing refuse from a district outside its license boundaries.

Lyon v. Hasbro Industries, Inc.


No. 4-86-0742


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


156 Ill. App. 3d 649; 509 N.E.2d 702; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2616; 109 Ill. Dec. 41



June 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. George S. Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant filed suit against defendant ambulance service for negligence after an ambulance broke down. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) dismissed one count for failure to comply with Ill. Code Civ. P. 2-622, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.110, para. 2-622 (1985). The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant swallowed a small toy peg and was taken to the hospital in a life-threatening situation. The ambulance service was called to transport the claimant to a larger hospital. The ambulance broke down six blocks from the hospital and the claimant suffered a cardiac arrest. The claimant, through his mother, filed suit against the ambulance service. The ambulance service filed a motion to dismiss one count against the ambulance service for failure to file a certificate and written report as provided in Ill. Code Civ. P. 2-622, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.110, para. 2-622 (1985), which was granted by the trial court in its entirety. On appeal, the court held that (1) the term "healing art malpractice" was broad in scope, (2) the allegation that the ambulance service failed to adequately equip the ambulance was a claim that asserted healing art malpractice and the claimant's failure to provide a certificate was grounds for dismissal, and (3) the claimant would be allowed to replead his allegations of failure to mechanically maintain the ambulance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the part of the count that alleged failure to adequately equip the ambulance with necessary and precautionary equipment. The court remanded with directions that the claimant be given 30 days to replead allegations of negligent transportation due to failure to have mechanically maintained the ambulance.

 

845 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Carpenter v. Kozubowski


No. 85-0552


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


157 Ill. App. 3d 127; 509 N.E.2d 1309; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2688; 109 Ill. Dec. 297



June 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters commenced an action against defendant city commissioners to contest a local option election that resulted in the prohibition of the retail sale of liquor in the voters' precinct. The voters sought review of the order of the Circuit of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the voters' action for failure file their complaint within the 10-day statutory period provided by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 182 (1983).


OVERVIEW: The voters' complaint was filed within 30 days of the election results, but more than 10 days after the election canvass. The complaint alleged that the liquor question was improperly placed on the ballot and that the vote count was inaccurate. The voters contended that the question of jurisdiction should be resolved pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 23-25 (1983), which permitted 30 days to challenge election results. The court held that the challenge to the election results was timely, but that the challenge to the validity of the election was untimely. The court reasoned that the voters' complaint concerned irregularities pertaining to the validity of the election and to the election results. The court held that para. 23-25 applied to the voters' challenge of the election results, that the voters' claim was made within 30 days of the election, and that the voters' claim regarding the election results was timely. The court held, however, that the challenge to the validity of the election was untimely because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 182 (1983) required those challenges to be brought within 10 days of the election canvass.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment dismissing the voters' challenge to the validity of the election. The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment dismissing the challenge to the election results and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Ortiz


No. 2-86-0166


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


155 Ill. App. 3d 786; 508 N.E.2d 490; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2489; 108 Ill. Dec. 329



May 18, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 16, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute was unconstitutional, the jury was not properly instructed, and that the admission of evidence relating to defendant's prior conviction was error. The court affirmed. The court found that a mental state of either intent, knowledge, or recklessness could have been implied for offenses involving sexual penetration, and the statute did not punish innocent conduct or set up an unconstitutional anomaly between the lesser and greater offenses. The court also found that an examination of approved jury instructions relating to sex offenses demonstrated that instructions defining general intent offenses did not need to set forth a specific mental state, and thus, the trial court did not err in failing to sua sponte instruct the jury as to defendant's mental state. The court determined that there had been no objection to either the testimony relating to defendant's prior conviction or to the prosecutor alluding to it in argument, and defendant had introduced the prior conviction as part of his trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault was affirmed.

Jordan v. Officer


No. 5-87-0251


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


155 Ill. App. 3d 874; 508 N.E.2d 1077; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2501; 108 Ill. Dec. 500



May 15, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. C. Glenn Stephens, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff losing candidates to contest the results of a primary election, defendant winning candidate appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which postponed a consolidated election and denied his motion to reconsider.


OVERVIEW: The losing candidates contested the election results on the ground that voters in the primary election had also signed the nominating petitions for independent candidates and argued that the trial court's order postponing the election was not appealable under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1). In vacating the order and remanding the matter, the court held that the order was appealable as a restraint on the winning candidate that was essentially injunctive in character. The trial court had no authority to enjoin an election unless injunctive relief was necessary to prevent a waste of public funds by the holding of an election under an unconstitutional election statute or any election called in violation of the constitution. This case did not involve that exception. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 2A-1.1(b), electors were guaranteed a right to vote by a certain date; interference with that right was not justified.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Morgan v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 3-86-0839


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


155 Ill. App. 3d 611; 508 N.E.2d 762; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2462; 108 Ill. Dec. 451



May 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. Robert W. Castendyck, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Illinois Racing Board (board) and stewards, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which held that plaintiff horse trainer was entitled to a preliminary injunction against defendants that prevented defendants from excluding the trainer from all racetracks under the supervision of the board.


OVERVIEW: The trainer was accused of racing a horse following illegal surgery on the horse. The stewards suspended the trainer for one year and excluded him from all racetracks under the supervision of the board. About four months later, the trainer obtained a temporary restraining order against defendants. He subsequently obtained a preliminary injunction that was to remain in effect until he exhausted all of his administrative remedies. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment after modifying the preliminary injunction. The court held that the initial temporary restraining order was an improper interference with defendants' duties. However, because the trainer's exclusion from racetracks deprived him of his only means of making a living, the trainer had a due process property right to a reasonably prompt hearing under the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 37-1 et seq. (1985). Because the board never reviewed the stewards' action, the lower court properly entered a temporary injunction against defendants. However, the court held that the injunction was to be modified such that it expired after any decision rendered by the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which held that the trainer was entitled to a preliminary injunction against defendants to prevent them from enforcing a suspension that excluded the trainer from racetracks. However, the lower court's preliminary injunction was modified such that it expired after the board rendered a decision. The court remanded the action.

 

849 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Tribune Co. v. Downers Grove


No. 2-85-1049


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


155 Ill. App. 3d 265; 508 N.E.2d 439; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2427; 108 Ill. Dec. 278; 14 Media L. Rep. 1273



May 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which awarded summary judgment to plaintiff newspaper in the newspaper's declaratory judgment action. The newspaper claimed that the village's door-to-door commercial solicitation ordinance violated the federal and state constitutional guarantees of freedom of speech, press, due process, and equal protection of the law.


OVERVIEW: Police officers of the village advised newspaper employees, who were conducting door-to-door sales of subscriptions to the newspaper in the village, that a commercial solicitation permit was required for them to do so. The salesmen were also advised that the ordinance prohibited any solicitation activity at premises that were posted with "No Solicitation" signs. The newspaper sought a declaration that the ordinance violated constitutional guarantees of freedom of speech, press, due process, and equal protection of the law as applied to the conduct of the newspaper when it solicited newspaper subscriptions in the village. The trial court permanently enjoined the village and its employees from subjecting the newspaper to the commercial solicitation regulations of its ordinance, and the village appealed. The court affirmed. The court agreed with the village that there was a distinction in the degree of first amendment protection afforded commercial and noncommercial speech, but ruled that the newspaper's right to freedom of speech and the press was no less than that of the other organizations against which the commercial solicitation restrictions were not applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that awarded summary judgment to the newspaper and permanently enjoined the village and its employees from subjecting the newspaper to the commercial solicitation regulations of its ordinance.

 

850 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Bashwiner


Nos. 85-0401, 85-3054 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


155 Ill. App. 3d 531; 508 N.E.2d 419; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2454; 108 Ill. Dec. 258



May 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Richard H. Jorzak, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in 85 -- 3054; reversed and remanded in 85 -- 0401.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ex-husband and respondent ex-wife challenged two rulings from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment in one action that the ex-husband pay the ex-wife's attorney fees to oppose a preliminary injunction; in the second action, the circuit court dismissed the ex-wife's petition for attorney fees incurred in the ex-wife's opposition to the ex-husband's motion to vacate the dissolution judgment.


OVERVIEW: The parties continued litigation after the dissolution as disputes erupted over the ex-wife's proposed removal of the couples' children to Washington, D.C. The ex-husband filed motions to vacate the dissolution judgment and for preliminary injunction. The ex-wife sought attorney fees for those actions. The trial court dismissed as untimely the ex-wife's petition as to the motion to vacate the dissolution judgment but granted the ex-wife's petition as to the injunctive orders. Both parties appealed, and the court affirmed the judgment that granted attorney fees to the ex-wife and reversed the judgment that dismissed the ex-wife's petition for attorney fees in the other action. The court held that the ex-wife, who successfully obtained a dissolution of the preliminary injunction, was entitled to damages and that the judgment amount was reasonable. The ex-wife properly waited for a decision on the appeal on the motion to vacate the dissolution judgment to file her petition for attorney fees, at which time the ex-wife would know the exact amount of the fees. This avoided piecemeal litigation. The trial court had jurisdiction of the case and erred in dismissing the ex-wife's petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted attorney fees to the ex-wife and reversed the judgment that dismissed attorney fees for the ex-wife in the second action. The ex-wife, as the successful party, was entitled to attorney fees in both actions, and the ex-wife was justified in waiting until there was a decision in the appeal of the order vacating the dissolution judgment.

 

851 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Health Clubs, Inc. v. Picur


No. 86-0894


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


155 Ill. App. 3d 482; 508 N.E.2d 742; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2451; 108 Ill. Dec. 431



May 7, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George A. Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and its officials appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying their motion to dismiss plaintiff health club and dues-paying member's suit challenging the constitutionality of an amendment to the Chicago Amusement Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Code § 104-1 et seq. (1984), and enjoining enforcement of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, health club and a dues-paying member, sued defendants, city and its officials, challenging the constitutionality of a city amusement tax ordinance amendment that included health and racquetball clubs. The trial court denied the city's motion to dismiss, declared the tax unconstitutional, and enjoined enforcement of the ordinance. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the amendment was constitutional and that the complaint should have been dismissed. Without deciding whether the amusement tax was an occupation tax, the court held that it did not violate the constitutional home rule provision, Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e) (1970), because the legislature authorized the city to tax amusements. The court also held that the amendment was neither constitutionally overbroad nor void for vagueness. The amendment did not violate equal protection under the federal or state constitution or have an extraterritorial governmental effect in violation of the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the city's motion to dismiss the health club's suit challenging the constitutionality of an amusement tax ordinance amendment, and enjoining its enforcement.

People v. Campos

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

May 6, 1987, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lake County (Illinois), convicting him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Defendant appealed, arguing that he was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the determination of the credibility of witnesses was left to the trier of fact. Further, the court held that the determination of the trier of fact was not set aside on review unless so palpably contrary to the evidence or so unreasonable, improbable, or unsatisfactory as to cause a reasonable doubt as to the guilt of the accused. Also, the court found that the trial judge properly determined the evidence sufficient to convict defendant. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that substantial corroboration existed to support the victim's contentions in the testimony of the arresting officers.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed and remanded with instructions to vacate the sentence.

People v. Bainter


No. 5-85-0733


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


154 Ill. App. 3d 1026; 507 N.E.2d 1309; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2389; 107 Ill. Dec. 940

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. William B. Starnes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1985) for an order that would have modified his previously imposed state court sentence by providing that it be served concurrently with another sentence subsequently imposed in a federal court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to armed robbery and was sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment by a state court. Thereafter, defendant pleaded guilty to transferring a firearm in interstate commerce without paying a transfer tax, in violation of 28 U.S.C.S. § 5861(e), and was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment, which a United States district court ordered to be served consecutively to the 15-year sentence imposed in the state court. Defendant filed a motion, pursuant to Ill. Rev. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed, contending that § 5-8-4(a) conferred upon the trial court the discretion to make defendant's state-imposed sentence run concurrently with the federal court sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1985) was an unconstitutional attempt to revest jurisdiction in the circuit court for further consideration of issues in a criminal case after the case was finally concluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied defendant's motion for an order that would have modified his previously imposed state court sentence.

In re Driver's License of Trainor


No. 4-86-0565


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2026



April 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Circuit Court County of Livingston No. 861872A, Honorable Charles E. Glennon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent driver challenged the judgment of Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which denied the driver's request under the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 118.1 (1985), for rescission of the statutory summary suspension of his driver's license. The driver had refused to take the breath test after being arrested for driving under the influence (DUI) in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.


OVERVIEW: The driver sought review of the trial court's judgment denying his motion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 118.1 for the court's rescission of the statutory summary suspension of his driver's license after his DUI arrest. The driver contended that there was insufficient evidence to support his arrest, that the suspension should have been rescinded after the court's failure to review his review petition within the 30-day period mandated in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118.1, and that the prosecution failed to prove that the driver had been advised of the consequences of his refusal to participate in the mandatory breath test. The court on appeal reversed the trial court's decision based on its determination that (1) the prosecution met ifs burden of proving the driver's DUI violation by a preponderance of evidence; (2) the trial court failed to comply with the due process requirements of para. 2-118.1, and its failure to do so required rescission of the driver's license suspension; and (3) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(c) required the arresting officer to advise defendant that a refusal to submit to the breath test would result in a license suspension.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the driver's motion to rescind his mandatory license suspension and remanded the matter. The court directed the trial court to rescind the driver's suspension.

 

855 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wright


No. 4-86-0513


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


154 Ill. App. 3d 962; 507 N.E.2d 926; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2380; 107 Ill. Dec. 773



April 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. John L. Davis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the denial of his petition for post-conviction relief by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in granting the State's motion to dismiss the petition without holding an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated criminal sexual assault and was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment. Almost one year later, defendant filed his petition for relief alleging that his plea was involuntary and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed. Defendant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing as a matter of right. In order to obtain an evidentiary hearing, defendant had to make a substantial showing of a constitutional violation. The record negated both allegations of constitutional error. The trial court found defendant made a knowing and voluntary plea. The trial court inquired whether defendant understood the plea, and whether he had been forced into the plea. The trial court also specifically asked defendant if his attorney pressured him to accept the plea agreement, to which defendant responded "no." The trial court's admonitions pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402 were thorough, and the record made at the time defendant entered his plea negated his claims of constitutional error; therefore, the trial court did not err in dismissing the petition without an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hardee's Food Systems, Inc. v. Human Rights Com.


No. 5-86-0202


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


155 Ill. App. 3d 173; 507 N.E.2d 1300; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2414; 107 Ill. Dec. 931



April 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer petitioned for review of an order of the Illinois Human Rights Commission (commission), which found that appellee employee had been discriminated against because of his race when he was discharged.


OVERVIEW: The court dismissed the petition for review. The court found that it was without authority to proceed with the review because the jurisdiction of the court to review the order of the commission was not properly invoked. The court determined that the transfer by the circuit court was improper as such a transfer was not sanctioned under state civil practice law, the state supreme court rules, or the Administrative Review Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 (1983). The court also determined that the transfer by the circuit court was invalid because it lacked subject matter jurisdiction to take any action with respect to direct administrative review in the appellate court, including any authority to transfer the cause to the appellate court. The court concluded that, as the circuit court was without subject matter jurisdiction at the time the complaint was filed, it therefore lacked the authority to transfer the complaint erroneously brought before it to the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The petition for review of the order finding that the employer had discriminated against the employee because of his race, was dismissed.

Bradford Exchange A.G. v. Department of Revenue


Nos. 86-1036, 86-2277 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


155 Ill. App. 3d 674; 508 N.E.2d 316; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2471; 108 Ill. Dec. 155



April 23, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the taxpayer's request to recover $ 510,900 in taxes, interest, and penalties it paid under protest to defendant state tax department under the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 440 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the occupation tax was unconstitutional, that it violated the United States-Swiss tax treaty, and that it violated the foreign commerce clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part, holding that: (1) the goods were not "in transit" within the meaning of the import-export clause merely because they were in the process of entering the state of their destination at the time the tax was imposed; (2) the tax did not fall on the goods themselves, but rather on the privilege of engaging in the business of selling goods at retail in the state as measured by the gross receipts of the sales; (3) the tax was a permissible, nondiscriminatory exaction applied without regard to the foreign origin of the goods; (4) the tax did not divert federal revenues to the state; (5) the tax did not discriminate against Swiss citizens residing in the United States by taxing them more heavily than United States citizens; however, (6) the trial court's finding that the tax was constitutional should have been applied prospectively rather than retroactively, negating imposition of interest and penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the judgment holding imposition of retailer occupation tax on the taxpayer was constitutional; reversed that portion awarding to the tax department the taxes, interest, and penalties paid under protest; and remanded the cause for resolution of the discrepancy in the amount of taxes, interest, and penalties actually paid.

Inland Steel Mortg. Acceptance Corp. v. Carlson


No. 2-86-0782


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


154 Ill. App. 3d 890; 507 N.E.2d 213; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2373; 107 Ill. Dec. 549



April 17, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 19, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. S. Bruce Scidmore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant Illinois Environmental Protection Agency's (IEPA) motion to dismiss the developer's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The developer owned a tract of land that fell within two sewage treatment regions. The developer sought approval from an IEPA commission to connect to the most convenient system. At the request of the town where the other system was located, the commission refused to consider the issue. The developer brought a declaratory judgment action requesting in count I that the use of void system boundaries be found unconstitutional, in count II that the refusal to consider the issue without an agreement with all towns involved be held unconstitutional, and in count III that the IEPA's use of the boundary that bisected its tract be found unconstitutional. The circuit court granted the IEPA's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court noted that all three counts failed because the developer did not exhaust administrative remedies. An exception to the exhaustion rule existed if an agency rule or order was being challenged on its face as not being authorized by statute, but none of the three counts fell within the exception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Holder


No. 3-85-0651


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


153 Ill. App. 3d 884; 506 N.E.2d 407; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2231; 106 Ill. Dec. 700



March 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and felony murder and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with two accomplices, entered the garage of a victim and shot him twice, killing him. Defendant and the men then stole money from the victim's wallet and searched his home for more money. On appeal, defendant argued that the State's use of peremptory challenges to exclude all black jurors from the jury violated his constitutional rights to equal protection and trial by an impartial jury drawn from a fair cross-section of the community. In affirming the conviction, the court ruled that defendant had waived his challenge since he had failed to raise the issue in any of his post-trial motions. The court ruled that Batson, which allowed a defendant to establish a prima facie case of racial discrimination based on the prosecution's use of peremptory challenges to strike members of the defendant's race from the jury venire, did apply to defendant's case. However, determinations of discrimination were findings of fact for a trial court. Because defendant did not present the question to the trial court, the challenge was waived. A prior consistent statement was admissible because it was used to show a recent fabrication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.

People v. Griffith


No. 2-86-0218


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


153 Ill. App. 3d 856; 506 N.E.2d 430; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2229; 106 Ill. Dec. 723



March 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Ronald Mehling, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which continued a statutory summary suspension of defendant's driving privileges for failure to submit to a breathalyzer pursuant to § 11 -- 501.1 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para.11 -- 501.1 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing his request for a hearing date other than the arraignment date, in placing the burden of proof on defendant in the suspension hearing, and in failing to properly consider the testimony of four witnesses. Defendant further argued that the mandatory summary suspension unconstitutionally deprived him of a property interest. The court disagreed. The decision to hold the rescission hearing on the afternoon of the same day that defendant filed his petition was not contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2 -- 118.1(b). Furthermore, in effect the trial court allowed defendant a later opportunity to be heard when defendant examined all four witnesses who were with him on the night of the arrest. The allocation of the burden of proof on defendant was proper. The findings of the trial court regarding the testimony would not be overturned because they were not manifestly against the weight of evidence. Use of a driver's license was not a fundamental interest. Therefore, the statute under which the suspension was effected was constitutional because it had a rational relationship to the state's interest in public safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Munday


No. 2-85-0967


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


153 Ill. App. 3d 910; 506 N.E.2d 445; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2236; 106 Ill. Dec. 738



March 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Edward Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a long criminal record and was charged with armed robbery, aggravated battery, and armed violence. Defendant agreed to plead guilty to armed robbery, and the state agreed to drop the rest of the charges against him. At the hearing upon defendant's guilty plea defendant and his attorney stated that there were no undisclosed agreements and that the agreement on the plea did not include any agreements pertaining to the sentence defendant would receive. At the sentencing hearing, the state recommended that defendant be imprisoned for 60 years and both defendant and his attorney stated that it was their understanding that the state would only recommend a 20-year sentence. The lower court denied defendant's request for post-conviction relief without a hearing, and the court reversed. The court held that substantially erroneous information concerning a sentence provided by defendant's attorney was below the level of competence required of criminal defense attorneys. The court ruled that if the ineffective assistance of defendant's counsel was relied upon by defendant, then defendant's guilty plea was not intelligently and voluntarily entered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which held that defendant was not entitled to post-conviction relief or a hearing on his petition for post-conviction relief. The matter was remanded to the lower court for a hearing on defendant's post-conviction petition.

Clark Oil & Refining Corp. v. Johnson


No. 84-0279


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


154 Ill. App. 3d 773; 506 N.E.2d 1362; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2362; 107 Ill. Dec. 307



March 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the validity of a use tax assessment against the taxpayer in its tax protest action against defendants, the Director of the Department of Revenue of the State of Illinois and the State Treasurer of the State of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was engaged in the oil refining business. Under protest, the taxpayer paid use taxes that were assessed on its use of certain "refinery fuels," which were by-products of the oil refining process. The trial court found that the taxpayer was entitled to a return of a portion of the tax because of a computation error. However, the trial court otherwise upheld the assessment, and the taxpayer appealed. The court held that the Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.1 et seq. (1981), was not unconstitutionally vague as applied. The court concluded that the Department had the authority to implement the measure of use tax prescribed by the legislature. The court further held that the Department's allocation of the selling price on the basis of relative volume was reasonable. The court rejected the alternative methods of calculation preferred by the taxpayer. The court also rejected the taxpayer's contention that the Department's construction of the Act was discriminatory and violative of equal protection. The fact that the taxpayer raised the price of its premium products to cover the crude oil cost did not prove that the taxpayer was subjected to double taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

People ex rel. Todd v. Harvey


No. 85-2962


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


154 Ill. App. 3d 296; 507 N.E.2d 110; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2300; 107 Ill. Dec. 446



March 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Richard S. Kelly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In interlocutory appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), brought pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, appellant father challenged denial of his motion to dismiss a paternity action that appellee State filed on behalf of the mother of child.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue on appeal was the manner in which the Illinois Parentage Act (IPA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, par. 2501 et seq. (1985), was to be applied to paternity actions filed prior to its effective date. Based on the IPA provisions, the father contended that the action, brought almost five years after the birth of the child, was barred by the two-year limitation on actions brought on behalf of any person other than the child. In an action on behalf of the mother, the State sought to hold the father liable for the support of the child as well as the mother's reasonable expenses arising from her pregnancy. The father moved to dismiss based on the statute of limitations contained in the newly enacted IPA. The trial court denied the motion because the complaint was filed prior to the effective date of the IPA. The court affirmed the order denying the father's motion to dismiss, but not on the grounds advanced by the trial court. The court held that the action could also be fairly construed as one brought on behalf of the child within the meaning of the IPA and thus would be barred only if brought later than two years after the child reached the age of majority.


OUTCOME: The order denying the father's motion to dismiss was affirmed.

 

864 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kickapoo Invest., Inc. v. Hartigan


No. 4-86-0368


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


153 Ill. App. 3d 785; 506 N.E.2d 365; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2217; 106 Ill. Dec. 658



March 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a county treasurer and his son-in-law, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which denied them relief in their action seeking a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 4.1 (1985), which barred county officials and their employees and certain of their relatives from participating in county tax sales, violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were the principal shareholders of a corporation that purchased delinquent taxes at various sales. Para 4.1 prohibited plaintiffs from participating in the tax sales. The State argued that para. 4.1 was constitutional because it was related to the legitimate interest of preserving fair competition. In reversing the trial court's judgment that found the statute constitutional, the court ruled that the classification scheme of para. 4.1 went too far, thus violating the Equal Protection Clause. Assuming arguendo that the State had propounded legitimate purposes for the statute, the court ruled that the classifications it created did not rationally relate to promoting State interests. By the terms of the statute, a part-time custodian in one county courthouse was prohibited from participating in another county's tax sales. Such a sweeping classification bore no relationship to protecting the integrity, or perceived integrity, of real estate tax sales in Illinois. The category of persons precluded from buying at tax sales had to be limited to those reasonably viewed as having access to information that might put them at an unfair advantage in buying delinquent taxes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

865 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Pahlke


Nos. 84-2015, 85-0074, 85-2246 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


154 Ill. App. 3d 256; 507 N.E.2d 71; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2295; 107 Ill. Dec. 407



March 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Monica D. Reynolds, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded the wife maintenance and child support, directed that the husband pay the major portion of the wife's and children's attorney's fees, and awarded the wife prospective attorney fees for the defense of the instant appeal.


OVERVIEW: The husband challenged the award of prospective and retroactive attorney's fees, child support, and maintenance to his wife. On appeal, the court affirmed the award. The court found that there was sufficient evidence that the husband's sale of the marital home was a sham transaction. The court also found that the husband had an 18-year earnings history, while the wife only had a 6-month earning history. Thus, the court concluded that the wife was not on equal footing with the husband. The court reasoned that the almost 20-year duration of the marriage warranted a substantial division of the marital assets to the wife. The court noted that the husband's child support payments were only 30 percent of his net pay and were below the minimum amounts set by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.40, para. 504 (1983). The court further determined that the attorney's fees incurred were necessitated by the husband's attempt to set aside the sham transaction finding. Lastly, the court held that the trial court had authority to award the wife prospective attorney's fees to defend the instant appeal where her financial resources were limited and the husband was in a financial position to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the wife.

People v. Jackson


No. 85-2919


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


154 Ill. App. 3d 241; 507 N.E.2d 38; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2293; 107 Ill. Dec. 374



March 17, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to an extended term of 60 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised as issues on review whether the circuit court erred in admitting in evidence a weapon not used in the murder, he was proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, the extended term sentence of 60 years was excessive, and extended terms were unconstitutional. The court found that when the revolver was first referred to in police testimony, defendant did not object until 16 questions were asked and answered concerning the weapon during the direct examination of the officer. Any prejudice which may have resulted from the admission of defendant's pistol was minimized by witnesses who were examined and cross-examined concerning this weapon at all times, making it clear to the jury that it could not have been the murder weapon. The court also found that none of the points presented by defendant undermined the eyewitness identification which was premised on three separate opportunities to observe defendant The court did not abuse its discretion where it examined all the facts of the case and the sentencing report, and determined that defendant's conduct was at a level of brutality and heinousness which warranted the severe punishment imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence where there was no merit in defendant's appeal in view of the record.

 

867 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lekas


Nos. 84-0873, 84-0970 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


155 Ill. App. 3d 391; 508 N.E.2d 221; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2442; 108 Ill. Dec. 60



March 17, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 19, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in 84 -- 0873; Affirmed in part, and reversed and vacated in part in 84 -- 0970.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and codefendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that entered convictions of murder, armed robbery, and aggravated arson for both defendant and codefendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and codefendant were tried together and convicted of murder, armed robbery, and aggravated arson for allegedly murdering a woman, stealing valuable coins, and setting fire to a house. The parties had separate counsel and each made motions for severance, which were denied. The trial court indicated that if codefendant testified, it would sever the case. Codefendant testified and the trial court denied defendant's motions to sever. On appeal, the court reversed the defendant's convictions and remanded his case for a new trial. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error by not granting defendant's motion to sever because defendant was prejudiced by the joint trial because of the adverse testimony of codefendant, which directly contradicted defendant's testimony. However, the court held that the joint trial did not require the reversal of defendant's convictions. The court found that defendant was not prejudiced by the testimony of codefendant. The court reversed both parties' convictions for aggravated arson because the aggravated arson statute was invalid. The court also held that the police had gained new information before codefendant was questioned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded his case for a new trial, reversed codefendant's conviction for aggravated arson, and affirmed codefendant's convictions of murder and armed robbery.

People v. McGhee


No. 85-2438


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


154 Ill. App. 3d 232; 507 N.E.2d 33; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2292; 107 Ill. Dec. 369



March 17, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Stephen A. Schiller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a 16-year-old juvenile, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which tried him as an adult and convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile, was tried as an adult and convicted of the murder. Defendant sought a reversal on the ground that his confession was obtained and admitted in evidence in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court concluded that the information that the officers had was not sufficient to obtain a warrant for the arrest; therefore, it was not sufficient to justify their unilateral conduct. The court held that the taking of defendant from his home was an arrest or a seizure which was made without probable clause. The court found, based on the totality of the circumstances, that defendant's confession was not voluntary. The court considered defendant's age, length of interrogation, lack of sleep, failure by the authorities to properly notify defendant's parents or a youth officer, refusal to permit his mother to see him at the police station prior to the time that he made any inculpatory statements, and lack of probable cause.


OUTCOME: A lower court order convicting defendant for murder was reversed and remanded.

Board of Trustees v. Washburn


No. 86-890


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


153 Ill. App. 3d 482; 505 N.E.2d 1209; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2187; 106 Ill. Dec. 418



March 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Charles Freeman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Director of the Illinois Department of Insurance (director) sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judgment in favor of plaintiff pension fund board of trustees (board) in its action for declaratory judgment that the director did not have authority to review individual board decisions under the Illinois Pension Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 1-101 et seq. (1985).


OVERVIEW: The director was examining the board's pension fund when it discovered that the board had not made retroactive payment of retirement benefits in a retiree's case after his pension was adjusted. The director order the board to do so, but it refused to do so because it did not believe it had the statutory authority. The board then filed for declaratory relief, and the trial court granted summary judgment in the board's favor finding that the director did not have jurisdiction to review the board's decisions. On appeal, the court affirmed. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 3-148, the court found that the Administrative Review Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 3-101 et seq. (1985), was the only method for review of decisions under the Pension Code. The court found that the director could examine the board's financial transactions and fiscal policies under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 22-502, but it did find any authority for the director to examine the board's administrative decisions. The court concluded that the board's administrative decisions were reviewable solely in the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the board in its action to determine that the director did not have authority to review the board's decisions.

Rackow v. Human Rights Com.


No. 85-0986


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


152 Ill. App. 3d 1046; 504 N.E.2d 1344; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2122; 105 Ill. Dec. 826



February 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs individuals and corporation sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which affirmed the decisions of defendant Illinois Human Rights Commission that found that plaintiffs violated Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 3-104(A) (1981) by refusing to lease an apartment to defendant individual because he would have had one or more of his children who were less than 14 years old residing with him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant individual completed a written application for a two-bedroom apartment for his two children and him, but plaintiffs had a policy under which no children were permitted in one-bedroom units and only one child under the age of five years was permitted in two-bedroom units. The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that affirmed the decisions of the Human Rights Commission because 1) there was no evidence to support plaintiffs' contention that the finding of the Human Rights Commission was against the manifest weight of the evidence or that it acted arbitrarily in clear abuse of its discretion; 2) a statute was not rendered unconstitutionally vague merely because a hypothetical situation could be conjured up which placed the meaning of some terms of the statute in question; 3) a statute was presumed valid and the burden was on the party challenging the statute to establish its constitutional invalidity; and 4) plaintiffs failed to meet their burden to establish the unconstitutional nature of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 3-104 (1981).


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court that affirmed the decisions of the Human Rights Commission in favor of defendant individual was affirmed.

Koontz v. Pepsico, Inc.


No. 86-1441


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


153 Ill. App. 3d 152; 505 N.E.2d 1126; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2145; 106 Ill. Dec. 335



February 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured workers appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant alleged guarantor's motion to dismiss the workers' complaint. The workers had filed a declaratory judgment action concerning the enforcement of a guaranty agreement whereby the guarantor allegedly assumed the obligation to pay all workers' compensation awards on behalf of the bankrupt employer.


OVERVIEW: The workers filed workers' compensation claims against their employer. Before the Industrial Commission considered the claims, the employer, which was a wholly owned subsidiary of the guarantor, filed a voluntary petition in bankruptcy. Subsequently, the guarantor divested the employer. The workers then filed claims in the trial court against the guarantor for enforcement of an alleged guaranty agreement. The trial court concluded that the issues raised in the workers' request for declaratory relief could have been addressed in their workers' compensation claims before the Industrial Commission. Thus, the trial court granted the guarantor's motion to dismiss on the basis that the workers' failed to exhaust their remedies under the Workers' Compensation Act. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.4(g) (1983) of the Act, the Industrial Commission had the authority and jurisdiction to review and interpret the alleged guaranty agreement to determine who was legally bound to pay the workers' claims. Thus, the workers were required to exhaust their remedies with the Industrial Commission before seeking relief in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

872 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Easley


No. 5-86-0409


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


152 Ill. App. 3d 839; 505 N.E.2d 11; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2090; 105 Ill. Dec. 885



February 20, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clay County; the Hon. Robert F. A. Stocke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Circuit Court of Clay County (Illinois), which revoked his probation that was previously granted after he was convicted of aggravated assault, reckless conduct, and unlawful use of weapons. On appeal, defendant contended that he should have been resentenced by the original sentencing judge according to § 5 -- 6 -- 4(h) of the Unif. Code Corr., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 6 -- 4(h) (1985).


OVERVIEW: According to § 5 -- 4 -- 1(b) of the Unif. Code Corr., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 4 -- 1(b) (1985), the judge who presided at the trial or the judge who accepted the plea of guilty had to impose sentence unless he was no longer sitting as a judge in that court. The State argued that § 5 -- 4 -- 1(b) was violative of the separation of powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970). On appeal by defendant, the court agreed with the State. The court found that § 5 -- 4 -- 1(b) conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21, which addressed the trial court's administrative responsibilities and which provided that the chief judge of each circuit could enter general orders in the exercise of his general administrative authority. Since there was an encroachment on the trial court's administrative responsibilities, § 5 -- 4 -- 1(b) of the Unif. Code Corr., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 4 -- 1(b) (1985), was unconstitutional. The court further found that defendant waived, by failing to allege in his motion to vacate sentence, any issue as to whether the judge who revoked defendant's probation was familiar with the factual basis of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

People v. Day

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


152 Ill. App. 3d 416; 504 N.E.2d 979; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2039; 105 Ill. Dec. 694

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted armed robbery and murder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced him to a term of 40 to 65 years. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and defendant filed a habeas corpus petition that was denied. Defendant then filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief that was dismissed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in not granting him an evidentiary hearing upon his petition or in failing to require the state to answer, or both, based on the allegations contained in his petition alleging the incompetency of the public defender who represented him in his initial trial. The court reversed the lower court and found that the lower court did not follow the post-conviction procedures of the amended Act in effect when its final order was entered, but instead rendered its decision based on the law in effect at the time the petition was filed. The court held it was obvious that the lower court did not make a determination, within 30 days after the effective date of the Act, as to whether defendant's pending petition was frivolous or patently without merit. The court remanded the cause for a hearing under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's grant of a dismissal of the state's petition to dismiss defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, and remanded with directions.

People v. Garvin


No. 85-979


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


152 Ill. App. 3d 438; 504 N.E.2d 948; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2041; 105 Ill. Dec. 663



February 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis J. Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his post-conviction petition. He appealed his conviction on two counts of attempted murder and a count of aggravated battery. His attorney filed an Anders brief seeking leave to withdraw as counsel after finding no meritorious issues but requested that the aggravated-battery conviction be vacated as cumulative. Defendant filed a pro se brief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that § 122 -- 2.1 of the Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 -- 2.1 (1985), which allowed for dismissal of frivolous or patently meritless petitions before appointment of counsel, conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c), 103 Ill. 2d R. 651(c), and violated the separation of powers. He claimed that Rule 651(c) impliedly granted a right to counsel to indigent post-conviction petitioners. On appeal, the court found that the rule specifically concerned appeals from post-conviction proceedings and provided that upon the timely filing of a post-conviction notice of appeal by a petitioner found by the court to be indigent, a transcript of the record of the post-conviction proceedings must be prepared and filed with the court to which the appeal was taken and counsel on appeal must be appointed, both without cost to the petitioner. The court noted that the rule did not direct appointment of counsel for post-conviction petitions prior to the appellate stage; that was done by § 122 -- 4 of the Code if the petition was not been found patently without merit or frivolous. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 -- 4 (1985). The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the circuit court of the petition of defendant as without merit.

County of Cook v. Chicago Magnet Wire Corp.


No. 85-2949


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


152 Ill. App. 3d 726; 504 N.E.2d 904; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2072; 105 Ill. Dec. 619



February 10, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Rene Goier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted defendant company's motion to dismiss citations issued against it by the county for the company's violation of an antiodor ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The company operated a wire-coating plant within the county, and the county issued nine citations to the company for its alleged violation of an antiodor ordinance. The trial court granted the company's motion to dismiss the citations on the grounds that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and that the county was guilty of laches because of its delay in prosecution after the action was commenced. The court reversed and remanded that judgment. The court held that dismissal on the basis of laches was erroneous where any delays in the prosecution of the matter had not prejudiced the company. It also ruled that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague where the terms used therein were either sufficiently defined or had commonly accepted and understood definitions. Finally, the court concluded that the county had validly exercised its home rule powers when it enacted the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment granting the company's motion to dismiss the county's citations against it for violation of an antiodor ordinance.

People v. Owens


No. 3-86-0044


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


151 Ill. App. 3d 1043; 504 N.E.2d 186; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 1974; 105 Ill. Dec. 317



February 4, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. Conway L. Spanton and the Hon. David DeDoncker, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for the offense of retail theft under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16A-3(a) (1985), by the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of retail theft under para. 16A-3(a) following a consolidated jury trial with his codefendant wife. Defendant was sentenced to a two-year term of imprisonment. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed, finding that the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction for retail theft under an accountability theory. Defendant drove to the store and waited in his car while his wife functioned as a lookout and two other women stuffed merchandise into bags. The jury disbelieved defendant's explanation and concluded that rather than an innocent bystander, he was the women's partner in a shoplifting scheme. The court held that defendant failed to preserve an issue concerning the jury instructions since he did not object at trial nor complete the appeal record with instructions offered and given. Further, the retail theft statute was constitutional. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel merely because his counsel also represented his codefendant wife. Finally, there was no unjustified gross disparity in defendant's sentence as compared to his wife's sentence to probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for the offense of retail theft.

People v. Upton


No. 5-84-0632


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


151 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 503 N.E.2d 1102; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 1979; 105 Ill. Dec. 96



January 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which convicted her of distribution of look-alike substances in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, § 1404 (1982 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Undercover officers working with an informant sought to purchase controlled substances from defendant. Defendant sold look-alike substances after representing that they were the actual substances. Defendant was convicted of distribution of look-alike substances, in violation of Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para.1404 (1982 supp.). The court initially determined that the look-alike statute was unconstitutional, but that decision was reversed by the Illinois Supreme Court, and the case was remanded for the court to determine: (1) whether instructions defining look-alike substances were misleading and inaccurate; and (2) whether the trial court erred when it refused to instruct the jury on entrapment. The court affirmed, and determined that: (1) jury instructions, although derived from the statute rather than from a pattern jury instruction, were proper because they accurately explained the offense to the jury and did not serve to confuse the jury; and (2) there was no requirement to instruct the jury on the defense of entrapment because even though defendant asserted the defense, no evidence of entrapment was presented and defendant chose to deny that she committed the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court that convicted defendant of distribution of look-alike substances.

Union Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. New Lenox


Nos. 3-86-0072, 3-86-0074 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


152 Ill. App. 3d 919; 505 N.E.2d 1; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 2102; 105 Ill. Dec. 875



January 28, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village and intervenor residents appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which was in favor of plaintiffs, a land trustee and the land trust's beneficial interest owner, on their action challenging application of a village zoning ordinance to their property. The owner cross-appealed denial of its motion for summary judgment on a claim that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The owner applied to the village for a special use permit to build an asphalt plant. The village denied the application, promoting this suit. The owners and the trustee sought declaratory and injunctive relief against the village asking the court to declare the zoning ordinance invalid as it related to their property. They also sought to enjoin the village from interfering with their development and use of the property as an asphalt plant. Judgment was rendered in their favor, prompting the village and the residents to appeal. The owners cross-appealed denial of their motion for summary judgment to declare the ordinance unconstitutional. The court found summary judgment on the constitutional issue should have been granted. The ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because an ordinary person exercising ordinary common sense would have to guess as to whether an asphalt plant was a permitted, special, or prohibited use under the ordinance. Moreover, the ordinance unconstitutionally delegated legislative power to the village board of trustees to determine the status of a proposed use without sufficient criteria.


OUTCOME: The court reversed denial of the owner's motion for summary judgment, granted that motion, and in all other respects affirmed the decision in favor of the owner and the land trust.
