National Bank of Joliet v. County of Will


No. 3-86-0279


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


151 Ill. App. 3d 957; 503 N.E.2d 842; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 1962; 105 Ill. Dec. 2



January 27, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Edward D. Smith, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two landowners and a bank acting as trustee, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which was entered upon a motion for directed verdict filed by defendant county, in plaintiffs' action seeking a declaratory judgment that a zoning ordinance was unconstitutional and void as it applied to the landowners' property and an order enjoining the county from interfering with the use of such property.


OVERVIEW: The landowners bought land and subdivided it for single-family residential development. At the time the landowners bought the property at issue, in the name of the bank, such property was zoned in part for residential development, and the landowners subdivided a portion for such development. The county later adopted a comprehensive amendment to its zoning ordinance which affected plaintiffs' property in such a way as to prohibit further residential development. Plaintiffs brought an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the county, and the trial court entered judgment upon a motion for directed verdict in favor of the county. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court reversed, holding that plaintiffs established by clear and convincing evidence that as applied to the property at issue, the ordinance was unreasonable, arbitrary, and without substantial relationship to the health, safety, morals, or general welfare, and thus, the trial court erred in directing a verdict in favor of the county. The court concluded that the evidence weighed substantially in favor of plaintiffs, including that residential development was compatible with the surrounding property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had been entered upon a motion for directed verdict filed by the county, and remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to proceed as if the finding had not been made in order to allow the trial court to decide the case on the totality of the evidence presented.

People v. Castro


No. 3-86-0392


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


151 Ill. App. 3d 664; 503 N.E.2d 376; 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 1931; 104 Ill. Dec. 819



January 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. Wilbur S. Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) to deny his motion to withdraw his plea of guilty to the offense of delivering more than 15 grams of a controlled substance, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(1) (1985). He also challenged his sentence to the statutory minimum of six years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the offense of delivering more than 15 grams of a controlled substance after his motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds was denied. He filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, alleging that the sentencing scheme of § 401 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401 (1985), was unconstitutional. That motion was denied, prompting this appeal. Defendant argued the progressive sentencing classifications and mandatory minimum jail sentence of § 401 were unconstitutional because they were contrary to the limitation-of-penalties provision of Ill. However, the court found defendant never made a trial demand while he was free on bail, so the 160-day statutory period under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 103-5(b) (1985) within which he had to be brought to trial never began.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both the decision to deny defendant's motion to withdraw his plea of guilty and the sentence imposed.

 

882 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Michael Reese Health Plan


No. 85-2637


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


150 Ill. App. 3d 959; 502 N.E.2d 433; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3269; 104 Ill. Dec. 170



December 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Alan E. Morrill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed defendant health plan from the patients' malpractice action based upon the Voluntary Health Services Plans Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 595 et seq. (1983). The patients claimed the act's exemption from liability for voluntary health services plan corporations violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The patients filed a complaint against the health plan and a doctor for medical malpractice for a failed tubal ligation. The trial court granted the health plan's motion to dismiss, and the patients appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the patient and her child failed to sustain her burden of showing that the classification was unrelated to a legitimate governmental interest. Voluntary health services plans were medical care delivery systems through which medical, hospital, nursing, and related health services were rendered to a subscriber or beneficiary. Generally, the plans ensured the availability of health services for a subscriber population by utilizing a prepayment method of financing and a group practice mode for delivery of services. The court concluded that the legislature had clearly carved out a separate and distinct classification of health care providers, distinguishable from other health care providers because they served the unique function of both insurer and health care provider. The unique organizational structure and regulation of the voluntary health services plan corporation provided a rational basis for immunizing the health plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the health plan from the patients' medical malpractice action. The classification granting immunity from liability to voluntary health services plans was not arbitrary, had a reasonable basis, and had a rational basis upon which to distinguish it from other health care providers.

Muskat v. Sternberg


No. 86-2499


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


151 Ill. App. 3d 304; 502 N.E.2d 1099; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3317; 104 Ill. Dec. 439



December 22, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Alan E. Morrill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a physician, a hospital, and corporations, filed an interlocutory appeal of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiff patient's action with prejudice pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 87 Ill. 2d R. 103(b), for failure to exercise reasonable diligence in obtaining service of process after the expiration of the applicable period of limitations.


OVERVIEW: One day before the expiration of the applicable statute of limitations, the patient filed suit against defendants, alleging an injury from the surgical implantation of a lens in her eye. The patient failed to effectuate service of process upon defendants for two years, and the action was dismissed for want of prosecution. The patient refiled the action pursuant to para. 13-217 of the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-217 (1985) and served defendants with process. Defendants filed respective motions to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion and certified the issue of the apparent conflict between para. 13-217 of the Code and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 87 Ill. 2d R. 103(b) to the court, which reversed and remanded. The court stated that the patient's failure to exercise reasonable diligence to obtain service of process upon defendants after the statute of limitations warranted dismissal with prejudice. The court held that where the patient's original lawsuit was dismissed for want of prosecution and no service of process was attempted, the trial court should have considered the patient's lack of reasonable diligence in obtaining process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which denied defendants' motions to dismiss the patient's action with prejudice, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Strong


Nos. 3-85-0402, 3-86-0253 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


151 Ill. App. 3d 28; 502 N.E.2d 744; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3286; 104 Ill. Dec. 247



December 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) that convicted defendant for unlawful possession with intent to deliver more than 30 grams of a controlled substance, unlawful use of weapons, and from a forfeiture order in favor of the state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the forfeiture was improper, that his convictions should be reversed because the search warrant was invalid, the state did not prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and the prosecutor's allegations were unsupported and highly improper, and that he was improperly sentenced. The court affirmed the trial court's forfeiture order and defendant's conviction for unlawful use of weapons but reversed his conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and remanded the case for a new trial on the possession charge and resentencing on the weapons' charge. The court found that defendant received due process in the timely filed forfeiture proceeding and that a sufficient nexus between the cash and the illegal substances raised the presumption that the cash was forfeitable. The court concluded that the cumulative impact of prosecutorial misconduct could have prejudiced the jury. While the indictment was poorly drafted, it cited the unlawful-use-of-weapons statute under which defendant was charged and sufficiently informed him of the charged violation to both protect him from double jeopardy and enable him to prepare a defense.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence, affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of weapons, and reversed his conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The court remanded the case for a new trial on the possession charge and resentencing on the weapons' charge. The court affirmed the trial court's order of forfeiture.

People v. Arteman


No. 4-86-0364


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


150 Ill. App. 3d 750; 502 N.E.2d 85; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3241; 103 Ill. Dec. 938



December 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. W. Charles Witte, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) after she was convicted of two counts of prostitution, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-14 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a lingerie model. At trial, the State's only witness testified that he had paid to receive masturbatory massages from defendant and to perform oral sex upon her. The State's witness also testified that earlier in the day, before the trial had begun, he had recognized defendant when the witness was sitting outside in the hall. On appeal from her conviction for prostitution, defendant contended that the circuit court erred in admitting the witness's out-of-court identification of defendant on the day of trial and that the admission of the prior identification was prejudicial because the State repeatedly emphasized the witness's credibility in its closing argument. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that the prior out-of-court identification on the day of trial was properly admitted because nothing in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-12 (1983) nor Fed. R. Evid. 801(d)(1)(C) required a very recent prior identification. The State's emphasis of the witness's credibility did not make the admission of the identification erroneous because the prosecutor's comments did not place the office of a state's attorney behind the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

886 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lett v. Klincar


No. 5-85-0803


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


151 Ill. App. 3d 783; 502 N.E.2d 1082; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3367; 104 Ill. Dec. 422



December 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County; the Hon. Carl H. Becker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner, claiming to represent a class of persons, brought an action against defendants, members of the Illinois Prisoner Review Board, in which he sought a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief. He claimed that an amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-3-5(f) was an ex post facto law. The Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) dismissed the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the prisoner's parole hearing, the amended para. 1003-3-5(f) provided that the Prisoner Review Board could set a prisoner's parole hearings three years apart. At the time of the offense, before the amendment, the parole hearings could be set one year apart. The court first held that the trial court properly dismissed the class action portions of the prisoner's complaint because the prisoner had not attempted to meet the prerequisites for maintaining a class action under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-801 (1985). The court stated, however, that the trial court should have allowed the prisoner to proceed individually on his contention that the amendment constituted an ex post facto law. The amendment was retrospective, and the retroactive elimination of the opportunity for an annual parole hearing was disadvantageous to the prisoner. Thus, it met both criteria for an ex post facto law, and the prisoner had stated a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the class action allegations. It reversed the remainder of the trial court's decision and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Gully


No. 5-85-0661


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


151 Ill. App. 3d 795; 502 N.E.2d 1091; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3369; 104 Ill. Dec. 431



December 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. William Starnes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of aggravated kidnapping, armed robbery, and aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to concurrent terms of 25 years for the aggravated criminal sexual assault, 20 years for the armed robbery, and 10 years for the aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Two men pulled a gun on the victim when she was sitting in her car. They entered her car, robbed her, and then drove her to a vacant, dead-end street where they sexually assaulted her before letting her go. The police received a phone call from someone who had information about the crime. After identifying the caller and interviewing him, they included defendant's photograph in a photographic array shown to the victim. She chose defendant's photo. On appeal, the court held that defendant had waived his contention that the criminal-sexual-assault statute was unconstitutionally vague because he did not raise this issue at trial. It further held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. The court found the testimony of the officers concerning the telephone call to the department was not hearsay because the testimony was offered for the limited purpose of explaining the reason the police conducted their investigation as they did. The court held that defendant's acts supported the separate offense of aggravated kidnapping because the victim's asportation was not merely incidental to the commission of the armed robbery and criminal sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

888 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 3-86-0020


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


150 Ill. App. 3d 535; 501 N.E.2d 1347; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3213; 103 Ill. Dec. 809



December 12, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 27, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. Wayne P. Dyer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions by the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois) for criminal trespass to a residence and resisting a peace officer, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 19-4, 31-1 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had lived with the victim in her house until shortly before his arrest. Although the victim permitted defendant to retain his house keys, she changed the front door lock. Defendant, who entered the locked house through a window screen, subsequently was arrested and convicted of criminal trespass to a residence and resisting a peace officer. Affirming the convictions, the court held that the jury reasonably could have concluded that defendant gained unauthorized entry by cutting or tearing the screen and that he knew such entry to be unauthorized. His retention of the keys did not symbolize an invitation to enter the house when he pleased. The victim's testimony on defendant's non-authority to enter was not so improbable as to raise a reasonable doubt as to his guilt. Further, defendant's manner of entry could not reasonably be construed to be pursuant to any invitation that arose from his possession of the keys. The evidence also supported the resisting arrest conviction because defendant backed away and protested; twice refused to put his hands behind his back; and, when officers resorted to force, he responded by holding his arms stiff at his sides and struggling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for criminal trespass to a residence and resisting a peace officer.

 

889 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sheahan


No. 2-85-0317


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


150 Ill. App. 3d 572; 502 N.E.2d 48; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3216; 103 Ill. Dec. 901



December 12, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County; the Hon. Robert J. French, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of criminal contempt of court but mentally ill.


OVERVIEW: When defendant appeared before the trial judge for his arraignment on the charge of battery, he gestured to the trial judge and made threatening comments. The trial judge found defendant in criminal contempt but mentally ill, and found that the mental illness was insufficient to constitute a defense of insanity. Defendant claimed that the judgment was error because the trial court failed to follow the statutorily mandated procedure in finding defendant guilty and to hold a hearing on defendant's sanity. The court reversed the judgment. The court held that the statutes regarding pleas of guilty but mentally ill did not apply because the contempt proceeding was a summary proceeding where no pleas were taken. However, the court did find that a hearing was mandated because contempt required intent, and if there was a question of defendant's mental capacity to form intent, then the elements of contempt were no longer within the trial judge's personal knowledge. The trial judge should have held a hearing on defendant's mental illness and ability to form intent, but because the original charge was dismissed and defendant already served his contempt sentence, remand was not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment finding defendant guilty of criminal contempt but mentally ill.

 

890 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


AXIA, Inc. v. I. C. Harbour Constr. Co.


No. 85-0356


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


150 Ill. App. 3d 645; 501 N.E.2d 1339; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3227; 103 Ill. Dec. 801



December 12, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. William E. Black, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff building owner appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss of defendants, a contractor and an architect, based upon the statute of limitations, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 -- 214(a) (1983). The building owner brought the action to recover damages for breach of contract to construct an office building the building owner, based upon defects in the building constructed.


OVERVIEW: The building owner hired defendants to build an office building, and after its completion, the building began to leak after rain. Under the terms of their contract, the building owner notified defendants of the building's problems and requested that they be corrected. The contractor attempted over time to correct the problems, but was not successful. The building owner brought an action against defendants, alleging breach of contract, and the trial court dismissed the action, holding that the case was time-barred by the two-year statute of limitations, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 -- 214(a) (1983). The building owner alleged that defendants were equitably estopped from raising the statute of limitations for a variety of reasons, including the contractor's ongoing efforts to repair the building and the building owner's reliance on that conduct, the natural effect of which was to forebear legal action. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the architect but reversed the judgment dismissing the contractor. The contractor's conduct in continuing to try to correct the building's problems estopped the contractor from asserting the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the architect based upon the statute of limitations, but reversed the judgment dismissing the contractor. The court held that the contractor's ongoing efforts to repair the building and plaintiff's reliance on that conduct, the natural effect of which was to forebear legal action, equitably estopped the contractor from asserting the statute of limitations.

People v. Kail


No. 4-86-0036


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


150 Ill. App. 3d 75; 501 N.E.2d 979; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3156; 103 Ill. Dec. 662



December 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted her of unlawful possession with intent to deliver cannabis.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped while she was riding a bicycle on a business sidewalk because she was suspected of being a prostitute. The officer charged her with failing to have a bell on her bicycle, and when she was unable to provide adequate proof of identification or post bond, she was arrested. After defendant's arrest, she was subjected to an inventory search, during which the cannabis was discovered. On appeal of her conviction, defendant argued that her equal protection and due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment were violated and that a full custodial arrest solely because she was unable to produce adequate proof of identification or pay bond was an unreasonable seizure under the Fourth Amendment. The court reversed defendant's conviction. In so doing, the court found that defendant's equal protection rights were violated because the ordinance requiring a bell on a bicycle was only enforced against her because she was suspected of being a prostitute. The court stated that there was no rational relationship between the class of suspected prostitutes and the state's legitimate interest in enforcing the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for unlawful possession with intent to deliver cannabis.

People v. Gant


Nos. 4-86-0011, 4-86-0311 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and modified in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of unlawful possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance and unlawful possession with intent to manufacture a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance and unlawful possession with intent to manufacture a controlled substance. On appeal, he contended that denial of his motion to suppress evidence was error and the proof of his guilt was insufficient. The court affirmed in part and modified in part and remanded the matter. Based on the evidence, the jury could have applied the inferences of possession arising from control. The court modified the portion of the judgment in respect to the scanners and described guns to provide that such items should have been turned over to defendant if that may have legally been done, or delivered to any designee of defendant who could legally have possessed them.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of unlawful possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance and unlawful possession with intent to manufacture a controlled substance by providing that scanners and guns were required to be turned over to defendant is that could have been legally done, and, as modified, affirmed the judgment. The court remanded the case.

People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 2-85-0985


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


150 Ill. App. 3d 211; 501 N.E.2d 856; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3174; 103 Ill. Dec. 539



December 1, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson D. Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which entered on a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of obscenity, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Police officers executed a search warrant on a bookstore owned by defendant after they received information that there were obscene magazines for sale. The officers took a total of 139 separate magazines and defendant was charged with obscenity with respect to the magazines. Defendant filed a motion to quash the search warrant and suppress the items seized, but such motions were denied. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

Forsberg v. Chicago


Nos. 84-1223, 84-1230, 84-1234, 84-1349 cons.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff boat owners filed four separate actions against defendants, city and city officers, challenging the constitutionality of a boat mooring tax imposed by the city and seeking injunctive and other relief. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the actions on various grounds, denied their motion to amend the complaint and denied their motion for class action certification. The four actions were consolidated on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Boat owners challenged the circuit court's dismissal of their complaints against a city and city officers, denial of their motion to amend, and denial of their motion for class action certification. The appellate court held (1) dismissal of the actions was proper because the boat owners failed to state causes of action in that the city had the authority under its constitution to impose a boat mooring tax, (2) dismissal of the two actions was proper because the boat owners showed no direct injury suffered as a result of the mooring tax and therefore did not have standing to bring the actions, (3) the boat owners' motion to amend pending class certification and motion for class certification were properly denied because a class could not be certified where no cause of action existed.

People v. McCrimmon


No. 85-0656


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


150 Ill. App. 3d 112; 501 N.E.2d 334; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3160; 103 Ill. Dec. 313



November 24, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Patrick J. Dixon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which found him guilty of three counts of unlawful use of weapons by a felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1(a) (Supp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a felony in 1965, and at that time, he was only prohibited from possessing firearms for five years following the conviction. About 19 years later, several months after § 24-1.1(a) became effective, police officers claimed to have seen defendant in actual possession of a revolver and claimed that he had constructive possession of a target pistol which was found in a bedroom where he lived. At trial, defendant claimed a companion owned the guns and denied any connection with the guns. The police never claimed to have seen the target pistol on defendant's person. The jury was instructed that defendant could be found guilty of unlawful use of weapons if he had actual or constructive possession of the guns, and defendant was found guilty of unlawful use of weapons by a felon. The court affirmed, holding that § 24-1.1(a) was not an ex post facto law because defendant's prior conviction was only an element of the offense, and new acts after the passage of § 24-1.1(a) were required to convict defendant. The jury instructions were proper because defendant was factually charged with actual possession of the revolver and constructive possession of the target pistol.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for three counts of the unlawful use of weapons by a felon.

People v. Morissette


No. 84-2901


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


150 Ill. App. 3d 431; 501 N.E.2d 781; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3201; 103 Ill. Dec. 464



November 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2(a) (1983), and armed violence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1983), adjudged him as a habitual criminal, and sentenced him to life imprisonment without parole pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for stealing a taxicab and committing armed robbery against the driver, who identified defendant in a police lineup. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the identification, which was denied, and after a bench trial, defendant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court affirmed and found that defendant was not prejudiced by the pretrial identification procedure because there was nothing unduly suggestive about the lineup and that there were sufficient indicia of reliability in the driver's lineup identification because he had ample opportunity to view defendant during the robbery. While defendant was entitled to representation, he was not entitled to be represented by the attorney of his choice. Defendant, who had been involved in the criminal justice system on several occasions, made an intelligent waiver of his right to counsel, and his Sixth Amendment rights were not violated by the state's failure name an officer as a witness or to produce documents that were not in its possession. The court found that the Act was constitutional and that it did not give the state unbridled discretion in its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's armed-robbery and armed violence convictions and his sentence of natural-life imprisonment without parole.

Adams Apple Distributing Co. v. Zagel


No. 85-2550


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


152 Ill. App. 3d 157; 501 N.E.2d 302; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3374; 103 Ill. Dec. 281



November 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold A. Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owner appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing his action seeking a declaration that § 2 and § 3 of the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 2101 et seq (1985), were unconstitutional and seeking injunctive relief and damages against defendant, the Director of the Illinois Department of Law Enforcement (director), under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: A search was conducted at the business owner's premises pursuant to a search warrant resulting in the seizure of numerous items of alleged drug paraphernalia, which violated § 2(d) of the Act. A criminal complaint was filed against the business owner who filed an action seeking a declaration that § 2 and § 3 were unconstitutional because they were vague. The business owner also sought an injunction and damages. The director filed a motion to dismiss, which was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 2 and § 3 were not unconstitutional because they provided fair notice of the conduct that was forbidden and established guidelines for the department. The fact that the Act did not delineate every conceivable item that fell within its proscription did not render it unconstitutional. Further, the Act's requirement of scienter weighed against a finding of vagueness. The court found that the business owner was not entitled to injunctive relief because he failed to demonstrate the likelihood of a recurrence of the search and because he had an adequate remedy at law under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 108-10, 108-11 (1985) to contest the propriety of the seizure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the business owner's complaint seeking a declaration that provisions of the Act were unconstitutional and seeking an injunction and damages against the director under § 1983.

People v. Gurga


No. 83-2039


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


150 Ill. App. 3d 158; 501 N.E.2d 767; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3167; 103 Ill. Dec. 450



November 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 6, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. Maloney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of murder, attempted murder, and home invasion, though he pleaded guilty by reason of insanity.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that he was not proved sane beyond a reasonable doubt, that the statute regarding the insanity defense was unconstitutional, that the trial court considered inadmissible evidence, and that the trial court should have found him "guilty but mentally ill." The court concluded that the trial court's finding that defendant was legally sane was not so improbable that it should have disturbed it on review. Since the alleged vagueness of the statute did not affect the outcome of the case, the court did not decide whether the lack of a definition of mental disease renders Ill. Crim. Code § 6-2 unconstitutionally vague. The trial court error in allowing a witness to testify regarding defendant's post-arrest silence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the trial court entered sentence on an improper judgment. Although the sentences entered by the trial court remained available to that court upon a judgment of guilty but mentally ill under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-6(a) (1981), the court could not determine whether the trial court would have entered those sentences had it entered the proper judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order.

O'Connor v. Pinto Trucking Service, Inc.


No. 85-3241


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


149 Ill. App. 3d 911; 501 N.E.2d 263; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3126; 103 Ill. Dec. 242



November 18, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Samuel S. Berger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a trailer lessee, a leasing corporation, and a truck driver, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed defendant manufacturer from a suit filed by plaintiffs, a decedent's wife and his estate, for the wrongful death of the decedent after the manufacturer settled with plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when his car crashed into the rear of a semitrailer parked along a road. The trailer lessee leased the trailer from the leasing corporation and the truck driver was the person who parked the trailer along the road. The primary allegations of plaintiffs' complaint concerned inadequate lighting on the street, inadequate lighting on the parked trailer, and improper placement of the bumper on the rear of the trailer. On appeal, the trailer lessee, the leasing corporation, and the truck driver argued that the settlement between the manufacturer and plaintiffs was invalid. Upon review, the court found that the argument was without merit. In light of the status of the lawsuit and pleadings, and of the ensuing negotiations, the settlement did not appear disproportionate. The trailer lessee, the leasing corporation, and the truck driver failed to prove an absence of good faith in the settlement by clear and convincing evidence. The fact that the settlement also compromised other counts, entirely separate and apart from the products liability count of the complaint, showed that there was no basis upon which to disturb the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the manufacturer from plaintiffs' suit for the wrongful death of the decedent.

 

901 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Foggy


No. 3-86-0213


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


149 Ill. App. 3d 599; 500 N.E.2d 1026; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3086; 102 Ill. Dec. 925



November 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. John Donald O'Shea, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction in the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) for sexual assault. He contended that the privilege afforded for confidential communications between the rape victim and the rape crisis counselor under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-802.1 (1985) unconstitutionally impaired his due process rights to confront witnesses against him.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction for sexual assault, defendant contended on appeal that his due process rights were violated because he was not allowed to cross-examine the victim's rape counselor regarding the victim's statements that could have been exculpatory or could have impeached the victim's testimony. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the absolute privilege of confidentiality granted by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-802.1 (1985) was not unconstitutional. The statute was specifically amended to eliminate in camera disclosure, thus converting the conditional privilege into an absolute privilege, and it provided a penalty for breach of confidentiality. The court noted that the statute was enacted with the express purpose of promoting the prosecution of sex offenders, and that the relationship of a rape counselor and victim was similar to that of an attorney and client in that the communication was the first step in promoting the pursuit of justice. Among the primary services of the rape counselor was to support the victim in pursuing the prosecution of the perpetrator.


OUTCOME: In affirming defendant's conviction for sexual assault, the court held that the absolute privilege of confidentiality between the victim and the rape counselor, which was granted by statute, was not unconstitutional.

Concannon v. Illinois Bell Tel. Co.


No. 85-3016


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


149 Ill. App. 3d 517; 501 N.E.2d 183; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3073; 103 Ill. Dec. 162



November 10, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), which declared that gross receipts from the transmission of interstate messages originating or terminating within the corporate limits of a city were not subject to the city messages tax ordinance in an action against appellee telephone company alleging that the telephone company failed to report or remit messages taxes on interstate messages.


OVERVIEW: The citizen brought an action against the telephone company alleging that the telephone company failed to report or remit messages taxes on interstate messages as required under the messages tax ordinance of the city. The trial court held that gross receipts from the transmission of interstate messages originating or terminating within the corporate limits of a city were not subject to the city messages tax ordinance, and the citizen appealed, arguing that the plain language of the ordinance required the telephone company to report and remit a percentage of its gross receipts from the transmission of interstate messages to the city as a messages tax. The court ruled that the tax was an occupation tax, imposed upon all persons engaged in the business of transmitting messages by means of electricity. Further, the court held that the city could not lawfully impose an occupation tax on the transmission of interstate messages. The court affirmed the order of the trial court, concluding that the city could not enact an occupation tax on telephone messages without specific legislative approval.


OUTCOME: The order declaring that the telephone company's gross receipts from the transmission of interstate messages were not subject to the city messages tax ordinance was affirmed.

People v. Orr


No. 82-2069


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


149 Ill. App. 3d 348; 500 N.E.2d 665; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3052; 102 Ill. Dec. 772



November 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James J. Heyda, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of one count of aggravated arson and three counts of arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 20/1.1(a)(1) and 20/1(a) (1981). The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms of 25 years for aggravated arson and 7 years for each arson conviction. The trial court denied defendant's motions for a mistrial and for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Forty stitches were required to treat defendant's wound after his former girlfriend attacked him with a razor blade. The arsons occurred five days after the razor blade incident. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in admitting evidence, in denying defendant's motions for a mistrial and for a new trial, and in permitting the State to make erroneous and prejudicial closing argument statements. The court vacated defendant's conviction for aggravated arson because the statute was previously declared unconstitutional. Because the State failed to inform defendant of its intention to introduce exculpatory evidence, the court held that the trial court committed reversible error by admitting the evidence and denying defendant's motion for a mistrial. Defendant's girlfriend testified that, five days before the arson, defendant threatened to set fire to her house. The state did not inform defense counsel of its intent to introduce the statement into evidence. The prosecutorial discovery misconduct was grounds for a mistrial. The trial court further erred in permitting witnesses to restate their prior out-of-court consistent statements and to comment on defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for aggravated arson, reversed defendant's convictions and sentences for arson, and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the simple arson charges.

People v. Sephus


No. 4-86-0067


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


150 Ill. App. 3d 272; 501 N.E.2d 175; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3183; 103 Ill. Dec. 154



November 5, 1986, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Edward B. Dittmeyer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) entered judgment upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12--16(c)(1) (1984 Supp.). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After entering the home of an acquaintance, defendant allegedly fondled the breasts and genitals of the acquaintance's eldest daughter. Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual assault, two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, and residential burglary. The state amended the information to dismiss the charge of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The jury found defendant not guilty of residential burglary, but convicted him on the remaining charges. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting the victim's mother's testimony as to what the victim told her. Although the trial court erred in admitting the mother's testimony as to what the victim told her, the error was harmless because defendant's guilt was overwhelmingly established. Moreover, the statutes concerning sexual offenses were not unconstitutional merely because the prosecutor possessed a certain amount of discretion in determining with which offense defendant was to be charged.

People v. Shannon


No. 85-1898


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


149 Ill. App. 3d 525; 501 N.E.2d 166; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3074; 103 Ill. Dec. 145



October 30, 1986, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Cornelius J. Houtsma, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and appeal dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on the People's charges of attempted murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4 (1983) and armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and armed violence. He was sentenced to a term of eight years on the attempted murder conviction, but no sentence was entered on the armed violence conviction. Defendant sought review of his convictions and the court affirmed. First, the court rejected defendant's claim that his rights were violated by the People's destruction of certain evidence. Second, the court found that police had probable cause to arrest defendant because he was in a car that matched a description of that involved in a shooting incident and because he matched the victim's description of the shooter. Third, the court held that defendant did not show that statements made by him while in custody were involuntary. Fourth, the court held that a delay of 29 hours between defendant's arrest and arraignment was not unreasonable. Fifth, the court dismissed defendant's appeal of the armed violence conviction because there was no sentence and, thus, no final judgment. Finally, the court said that there was overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for attempted murder and armed violence.

In re Marriage of Leff


Nos. 2-85-0777, 2-85-0953, 2-86-0031, 2-86-0157 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


148 Ill. App. 3d 792; 499 N.E.2d 1042; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2975; 101 Ill. Dec. 262; 102 Ill. Dec. 262



October 29, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. George W. Pease, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) entered a judgment granting appellant ex-wife's petition for legal separation filed in response to the petition for dissolution filed by appellee ex-husband, ordered the sale and division of marital property, and awarded custody and maintenance. The ex-wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband filed a petition for dissolution of marriage. The ex-wife filed a petition for legal separation in response. The trial court granted the legal separation, awarding custody, maintenance, and dividing the marital property. On appeal, the ex-wife claimed that the trial court did not have the authority to divide property interests in a proceeding for legal separation, and that the awards of custody and maintenance were erroneous. The court found (1) that the trial court had the authority to divide assets in a legal separation action, especially when the ex-wife actively contested the marital or nonmarital status and values and requested an apportionment the property, (2) that the value of the business with its income potential was considered in apportioning the parties' assets and in determining maintenance and child support, (3) that the ex-wife's claim that the home was a gift to her from the ex-husband was not clear and convincing and did not rebut the statutory presumption in favor of marital property, and (4) that the conciliation report was admissible, the child's stated was not controlling, and placement with the ex-wife was not in the child's best interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of legal separation in favor of the ex-wife and the award of custody in favor of the ex-husband, the award of maintenance to the ex-wife, and the division, distribution, and order for the sale of property.

Citizens for Preservation of Knox County, Inc. v. Department of Mines & Minerals


No. 3-85-0697


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


149 Ill. App. 3d 261; 500 N.E.2d 75; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3040; 102 Ill. Dec. 453



October 29, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Knox County; the Hon. Daniel J. Roberts, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens group sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Knox County (Illinois), which granted the motion by defendants, Department of Mines and Minerals (department) and coal company, to dismiss for lack of standing the citizens group's action to challenge the permit issued to the coal company.


OVERVIEW: The citizens group was a nonprofit organization involved in the enforcement of the Federal Surface Mining Act Control and Reclamation Act of 1977 (federal act), 30 U.S.C.S. § 1201 et seq. (1982). The coal company filed a verified application with the department for a coal disturbance permit on certain lands, pursuant to the Surface Coal Mining Land Conservation and Reclamation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 96 1/2, para. 7901.01 et seq. (1983), adopted in accordance with the federal act. After a public hearing, the department granted the permit to the coal company. Subsequently, a departmental administrative review was conducted, and a hearing officer ruled that the citizens group was not a "party with an interest" that could contest the permit grant. The citizens group then filed a complaint for administrative review in the lower court, which granted the department and coal company's motion to dismiss the action. The court affirmed the judgment by holding that the citizens group did not have standing to contest the permit grant because it was not a "party with an interest," because it did not allege any direct or particular financial interest that was affected by the permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which granted the department and coal company's motion to dismiss for lack of standing the citizens group's action to challenge the permit issued to the coal company.

People v. James


No. 4-86-0225


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 536; 499 N.E.2d 1036; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2946; 102 Ill. Dec. 256; 64 A.L.R.4th 1083



October 28, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. James A. Knecht, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) that found him guilty of the offense of retail theft over $ 150.00, a Class 3 felony in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16A--3(a), 16A--10(3), and sentenced defendant to two years incarceration.


OVERVIEW: The lower court convicted defendant of retail theft over $ 150.00, a Class 3 felony in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16A--3(a), 16A--10(3), and sentenced defendant to two years incarceration. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. Defendant claimed the conviction was improper because it violated his equal protection rights since his conviction for retail theft carried a stiffer penalty then if he had been convicted of ordinary theft. He claimed it was unconstitutional to punish the offenses as felonies using different property-value thresholds. The court found that there was a rational basis for the distinction and that no equal protection rights were violated. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the disparity in punishment violated due-process protections because the legislature could reasonably conclude that there was a greater detriment to the state's economy, along with a greater opportunity for committing the offense of retail theft as opposed to simple theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that found defendant guilty of the offense of retail theft over $ 150.00 and sentenced defendant to two years incarceration.

Blackwood v. Rusk


No. 3-86-0023


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


148 Ill. App. 3d 868; 500 N.E.2d 69; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2982; 102 Ill. Dec. 447



October 28, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. Conway L. Spanton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers appealed the orders of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) that (1) dismissed two counts of their complaint against defendant sellers alleging breach of implied warranty of habitability as time-barred, and (2) denied their motion to reconsider the dismissal. The purchasers argued that the applicable statute of limitations was Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214 (1983).


OVERVIEW: The sellers built a house in 1977 and sold it to the purchasers in 1979. In 1984 the purchasers were advised that cracks in the walls and foundation were due to certain defects in the property's foundation. The purchasers sued the sellers in 1985, alleging breach of implied warranty of habitability and failure of consideration. The trial court dismissed the breach of warranty counts, finding that they were time-barred under para. 13-205. The trial court also ruled that para. 13-214 was unconstitutional. The purchasers appealed, and the court reversed, holding that para. 214 was constitutional and applied to the purchasers' claims arising out of the negligent design and construction of the house. Under para. 13-214 the limitation period was two years from discovery of the relevant act or omission with a maximum limitation period of 12 years from the date of omission. The provision applied to negligent design and construction that occurred prior to its November 29, 1979, effective date. The purchasers' complaint contained allegations sufficient to state a cause of action within the limitation periods prescribed in para. 13-214.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the purchasers' claims against the sellers for breach of implied warranty of habitability and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Server

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 888; 499 N.E.2d 1019; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2986; 102 Ill. Dec. 239



October 28, 1986, Filed

The court concluded that the aggravated criminal sexual abuse statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(c)(1), and the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(b)(1), were not unconstitutionally vague where they were clearly discernable and defined. The court noted the legislature was not bound by the common understanding and use of terms.

912 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Farmer


No. 4-86-0239


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 723; 499 N.E.2d 710; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2967; 102 Ill. Dec. 153



October 23, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Douglas County; the Hon. Frank W. Lincoln, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois), which dismissed his post-conviction petition filed pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, acting pro se, entered a negotiated plea of guilty to one count of armed robbery. He subsequently filed a post-conviction petition alleging that he was denied assistance of counsel and that he was mentally incompetent at the time of his guilty plea. The trial court dismissed the petition as patently without merit under § 122-2.1 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 122-2.1 (1985). Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the dismissal. Case law precedent holding that § 122-2.1 did not conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) remained the law. Because § 122-8 of the Act was added in an attempt to afford a petitioner even greater protections under the Act, it was not an indispensable component without which the statutory scheme could not have operated. The trial court was still required to consider a petition and initially determine whether the substantive matters raised were frivolous. Thus, § 122-2.1 was severable from § 122-8, and its validity was upheld despite the unconstitutionality of § 122-8. There was no indication that defendant was not lucid or did not understand the proceedings when he entered his plea. Thus, there was no error in dismissing the petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

913 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Chitwood


No. 4-86-0073


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 730; 499 N.E.2d 992; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2968; 102 Ill. Dec. 212



October 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Robert W. Cook, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) defendant was convicted of three counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para.12-16(a)(1) (1985). He was sentenced to seven years' imprisonment and appealed, arguing that § 12-16(a)(1) of the Criminal Code of 1961 was unconstitutional, that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing, and that errors were committed during trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the felony of aggravated criminal sexual abuse under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para.12-16 (a)(1) (1985), and alleged that the statute was unconstitutional because the same offense when committed by use of force was a misdemeanor. In holding the statute constitutional, the court held that the legislature rationally determined that the threat of the use of force with a dangerous weapon had a greater potential for harm than the actual use of force absent any weapon. After noting that the versions of what happened told by defendant and the victim were exactly contrary to each other, the court stated that the testimony of one witness, if positive and credible, was sufficient to sustain a conviction even though the accused contradicted the witness. There was sufficient evidence to allow the jury to determine the credibility issues against defendant. Opinion testimony of which defendant complained was a continuation of a line of questioning which defendant initiated, and he could not complain of its admission. The court held that an allegation of ineffective counsel could not be based upon speculation, and that defendant had received effective assistance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for three counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

People v. James


No. 83-1323


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


149 Ill. App. 3d 214; 500 N.E.2d 474; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3035; 102 Ill. Dec. 581



October 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Stephen Schiller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of murder, rape, and robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's arrest was based solely upon implicating statements that codefendant made subsequent to his own arrest. When the trial court quashed codefendant's arrest and suppressed his confession for lack of probable cause, the state entered a nolle prosequi and discharged him. The court reversed and held that the admission of defendant's confession violated his Fourth Amendment right to be secure against unreasonable search and seizure. Because codefendant's suppressed confession was insufficient to establish probable cause to arrest defendant the court reasoned that defendant's own confession should have been suppressed as a fruit of the poisonous tree. The court also determined that a good-faith invalid arrest warrant for codefendant could not support a determination that defendant's warrantless arrest was in good faith because the good-faith modification of the exclusionary rule did not apply to warrantless arrests. Contrary to the state's assertion, no intervening events attenuated or otherwise purged the taint of defendant's illegal arrest.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for murder, rape, and robbery was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new trial.

Bryski v. Chicago


No. 2-85-0140


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


148 Ill. App. 3d 556; 499 N.E.2d 162; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2948; 101 Ill. Dec. 795



October 15, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed their class action complaint against appellees, city and airport proprietors, in a case that sought to recover damages that arose from the operation of the airport.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a class action lawsuit against appellees and alleged that the airport caused excessive noise, vibration, and air pollution. Appellants argued that the airport deprived them of the use and enjoyment of their property, injured their physical and mental health, amounted to a taking for public use of their private property, and constituted a continuing nuisance. Appellees moved to dismiss the complaint on the ground that federal law preempted appellants' claims for nuisance and trespass. The lower court dismissed appellants' complaint. Appellants challenged the lower court judgment and argued that federal law did not preempt the nuisance or trespass claims. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because appellants were barred from pursuing the nuisance and trespass claims. The court determined that since federal laws and regulations preempted local control of aircraft flights, appellees could not be charged with creating a nuisance to the extent they complied with such federal laws and regulations. The court held that appellants failed to allege that appellees violated federal regulations in the operation of the airport.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that dismissed appellants' class action lawsuit.

People v. Intercoastal Realty, Inc.


No. 84-1079


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 964; 501 N.E.2d 1305; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2996; 103 Ill. Dec. 767



October 15, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. McDonnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, realty company and its president, appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of criminal housing management in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 23-5.1 (1981) and reckless conduct, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-5 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The evidence presented at trial established that the real estate company was the company that was responsible for the maintenance and repair of a certain property in Chicago. The first building inspector for the city testified that he inspected the building and found pickets missing from a second-floor landing, water standing four inches deep in the basement, and broken plaster and peeling paint in some of the upstairs apartments. A few months later, a second inspector found rotten wood on the rear porches, peeling paint, broken windows, and garbage infested with rats. On appeal, defendants contended that the criminal-housing-management statute was void for vagueness and that the informations did not sufficiently inform them of the nature and elements of the offenses. The court affirmed the convictions and found that the Illinois criminal housing management statute was constitutional. The court also found that the informations were sufficient because defendants could glean from the charging document the accusations that, at a particular time and at a particular location, they permitted the property to become or remain deteriorated to a point where it endangered the occupants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of criminal housing management and reckless conduct.

 

917 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Capporelli


No. 85-1623


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 1048; 502 N.E.2d 11; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 3006; 103 Ill. Dec. 864



October 14, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ronald J. Crane, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which had convicted him of driving a motor vehicle while the alcohol concentration in his blood was more than .10, and driving while his license was suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving a motor vehicle while the alcohol concentration in his blood was more than .10 , and driving while his license was suspended. He was found not guilty of driving while under the influence of alcohol. He contended that the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion for severance and other contentions. The court affirmed and held that defendant failed to establish sufficient grounds for severance. The mere apprehension that joinder may have resulted in prejudice, without a showing that such apprehensions were well founded, was an insufficient ground for severance. Thus, mere speculation by a jury of possible past convictions of defendant was not sufficient to establish prejudice. The court held further that § 11 -- 501(a)(1) of the Illinois Vehicle Code states a single offense, and defendant cannot claim that he was charged with a hybrid of two offenses. Rather, the amended complaint merely described the manner in which the state intended to show that defendant's alcohol concentration was .10 or more. Failure to admit testimony as to the improvements on an Intoxilyzer machine did not constitute prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of driving a motor vehicle while the alcohol concentration in his blood was more than .10, and driving while his license was suspended.

 

918 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lehman v. Stephens


No. 4-86-0041


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 538; 499 N.E.2d 103; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2947; 101 Ill. Dec. 736



October 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which grated appellees, hospital, physician, department of children and family services, and a child protective worker's, motions to dismiss the parents complaint seeking damages after their minor child was admitted to the hospital on a suspicion of abuse and neglect.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed a complaint seeking damages after their minor son was admitted to the hospital for two days for observation and on a suspicion of abuse and neglect. The suit concerns the actions of the physician, who made a report of possible abuse or neglect to the department of children and family services (DCFS), and the child-protective worker, who acted to take official temporary protective custody of the child. The hospital and the physician filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, raising the immunity from civil liability afforded under the Illinois Abused and Neglected Child Reporting Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 23, para. 2051 et seq. DCFS and the child protective worker also filed a motion to dismiss, asserting that exclusive jurisdiction of the matter rested in the Court of Claims. The trial court of Champaign County granted both motions, and the parents appealed. The court held that the Act § 5, which provided for temporary protective custody was not unconstitutional. The court also found that the good faith immunity provided for mandated and permitted report under the Act was clearly justified and was in no way inconsistent with the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the parents' complaint.

People v. Cooper


No. 84-2726


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 412; 499 N.E.2d 599; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2928; 102 Ill. Dec. 42



October 7, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Howard M. Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, aggravated kidnapping, and two counts of armed robbery. He was sentenced to concurrent terms of 100 to 200 years form murder, 15 years for aggravated kidnapping, and 30 years for each of the armed robbery convictions. Defendant filed for post-conviction relief, alleging that the sentences were excessive and that prison authorities had miscalculated the time for his parole hearing. The trial court denied his petition without an evidentiary hearing. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that on a hearing on the state's motion to dismiss, the parties presented their positions in two hearings, therefore Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.38, para. 122-2.1(a) was not applicable and reversal or remandment was unwarranted. The court held that there was no evidence that appellate counsel's decision to not raise certain issues on appeal was erroneous or constituted incompetence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.

 

920 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. O'Neal


No. 4-86-0242


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


148 Ill. App. 3d 87; 499 N.E.2d 83; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2891; 101 Ill. Dec. 83; 101 Ill. Dec. 716



October 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Jerry L. Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which dismissed his post-conviction petition pursuant to the provisions of the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of cannabis and possession with intent to deliver. He was sentenced to incarceration. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief and alleged that he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel because of a conflict of interest between himself and a codefendant, and because of incompetence of counsel. The circuit court entered an order dismissing the post-conviction petition without conducting a hearing, and found that the petition was patently without merit. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant's contention that a conflict of interest on the part of his trial counsel led to ineffective assistance of counsel amounted to mere speculation. No actual conflict was established. The evidence of defendant's guilt was very strong, and the outcome of defendant's trial was not affected by defense counsel's failure to respond to improper remarks by the prosecution. Defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced in any way by the manner in which his defense was conducted, or that there was a reasonable probability that the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of defendant's post-conviction petition as being patently without merit.

 

921 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Combs v. Board of Education


No. 2-85-0559


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


147 Ill. App. 3d 1092; 498 N.E.2d 806; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2873; 101 Ill. Dec. 482



September 29, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. William C. Block, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which upheld his discharge by defendant board of education, from his position as a tenured public school teacher. The teacher argued that his due process rights were violated by the discharge proceedings under § 24-12 of the Illinois School Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 24-12 (1983), and that the decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was discharged pursuant to the provisions of § 24-12 of the Illinois School Code. The circuit court upheld the dismissal, and the court affirmed on appeal. The court held that the teacher's due process rights were not violated because he had been afforded the opportunity to be heard prior to suspension without pay. The decision to dismiss the teacher was not void for lack of jurisdiction. The hearing officer had authority to remove or dismiss the teacher pursuant to § 24-12, and the correct preponderance-of-the-evidence standard was applied. Finally, the court concluded that the decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The evidence showed that the teacher could not maintain order in his classroom, that students were involved in fights in the classroom, and that students were climbing out of windows of the classroom. Teachers also testified as to the frequent noise and regular disorder in the classroom. The teacher failed to remedy the situation over the course of the school year. Thus, the court could not conclude that the board's decision was unreasonable or arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which upheld the teacher's discharge.
