Hammerman v. Illinois State Toll Highway Authority


No. 85-0987


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 259; 498 N.E.2d 795; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2906; 101 Ill. Dec. 471



September 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. David Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, bondholder and corporation, challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the bondholder's action that claimed that appellee highway authority improperly administered the state's tollway system.


OVERVIEW: The individual bondholder filed a class action and asserted that the highway authority its duties regarding the payment terms of bonds that it issued. The corporation filed an intervening class action and claimed that certain tollway users were unconstitutionally double-charged for their use of the highways. However, the highway authority contended that a bondholder settlement in another case rendered the individual bondholder's claim moot. On review, the court dismissed the individual bondholder's appeal. The court held that whether the individual bondholder was bound by the settlement was irrelevant because state law rendered the individual's claims as to the impropriety of the payment terms moot. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against the corporation and held that that actions, such as the one at issue, which challenged the amount of tolls, were impermissible in the absence of a showing of bad faith, fraud, or malice.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the individual bondholder's appeal as moot and affirmed the trial court's judgment against the corporation's challenge.

 

923 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


York v. Wilmette


Nos. 85-2252, 85-2258 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 108; 498 N.E.2d 712; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2894; 101 Ill. Dec. 388



September 25, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the validity of the grant by appellee town of a special use permit to appellee developer to build an apartment building for housing the elderly in an area zoned for townhouses.


OVERVIEW: The landowners sought a declaration that the special use permit granted to the developer was invalid and an injunction preventing the developer from constructing the building. The trial court upheld the validity of the permit, finding that the property was suitable for use of elderly housing as the area was predominantly residential, with retail and commercial uses, and that the promotion of the public health, safety, and welfare outweighed the destruction of property values and the hardship imposed on individual property owners. On appeal, the court affirmed. It found that the homeowners did not satisfy their burden of proving by clear and convincing evidence that the special use of housing for the elderly bore no substantial relation to the public welfare. At best, they showed that a difference of opinion existed concerning the reasonableness of the special use, which was insufficient to compel a finding that the special use was unconstitutional. Further, the variations the homeowners referred to in the special use permit were simply exceptions to zoning code requirements. As such, the ordinance granting a special use with exceptions to the developer was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which upheld the validity of the special use permit granted to the developer and denied the homeowner's request for an injunction preventing the developer from building an apartment building for housing the elderly.

 

924 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Snowden


No. 5-84-0299


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


147 Ill. App. 3d 763; 498 N.E.2d 612; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2836; 101 Ill. Dec. 288



September 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which conducted a bench trial and found him guilty of but mentally ill of five counts of home invasion, seven counts of rape, two counts of burglary, five counts of deviate sexual assault, two counts of battery and one count of attempted rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of various offenses and appealed, claiming that the circuit court erroneously applied the amended statute effective January 1, 1984, in finding him guilty but mentally ill under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6-2 (1983), so as to violate the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws, U.S. Const., art. I, § 10, and additionally challenging the sufficiency of the evidence of defendant's sanity at the time of the offenses. The court affirmed, finding there was no reversible error because the circuit trial court found that the State had proved defendant's sanity beyond a reasonable doubt as required by the law in effect at the time the offense were committed. The presentation of evidence at trial as to sanity proceeded as under the old law, with defendant first raising the issue of insanity by the introduction of evidence to overcome the presumption of sanity and the State then presenting rebuttal testimony to prove defendant's sanity beyond a reasonable doubt. Any error in the circuit court's application of the amended insanity statute was harmless. The circuit court's determination of defendant's sanity was supported by surrounding circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

People v. Whitfield


No. 4-86-0051


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


147 Ill. App. 3d 675; 498 N.E.2d 262; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2824; 101 Ill. Dec. 80



September 15, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which revoked the defendant's conditional discharge after finding the defendant harassed his ex-wife in violation of an order of protection under the Illinois Domestic Violence Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2301-1 et seq. (1983).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition to revoke defendant's conditional release after defendant was alleged to have followed his wife in his car in violation of a domestic violence act order of protection. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that harassment occurred when an individual knowingly caused his victim to suffer undue distress and the individual knew of the order of protection; thus, defendant's act of following his wife home from work in violation of the order that he pled guilty to constituted harassment. The court found that the Illinois Domestic Violence Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2301-1 et seq. (1983), was not unconstitutionally vague because the terms surrounding the word harass in the Act delineated the type of conduct that was prohibited and the Act only prohibited those actions that were done with the intent to cause harm in violation of a domestic violence order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court revoking defendant's conditional discharge.

In re Marriage of Cook


No. 3-85-0627


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


147 Ill. App. 3d 134; 497 N.E.2d 1029; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2760; 100 Ill. Dec. 760



September 8, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Henry County; the Hon. Susan B. Gende, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois), which modified a child support order and ordered her to pay $ 55 per week to the respondent father.


OVERVIEW: When the parties divorced the mother was given custody of the minor child. The mother was also ordered to pay all child-support expenses. The mother filed a petition for child support. The father filed a petition for modification and sought custody of the child. The father was then ordered to pay $ 35 per week for child support. Custody of the child was given to the father on November 26, 1984, but the issue of child support was not decided at that time. A temporary order was filed which directed the mother to pay $ 17.50 per week child support. The trial court denied the mother's request to rule Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 505 unconstitutional and ordered her to pay $ 55 per week child support retroactive to January 11, 1985. The mother appealed. The court reversed and determined that the trial court had abused its discretion when it increased the amount of child support. The court questioned whether a finding of equal support by both parents was a true representation of an analysis of the financial needs and resources of both parents. The court noted that the father's income was 60 percent higher than the mother's income and that he had only been ordered to pay $ 35 per week.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the modification of child support in favor of the mother and remanded to the trial court for reconsideration.

Galesburg Eby-Brown Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 3-85-0709


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


147 Ill. App. 3d 137; 497 N.E.2d 874; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2761; 100 Ill. Dec. 696



September 8, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. L. E. Ellison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cigarette distributor sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which affirmed an administrative decision of appellee state department of revenue that held that delivery of certain of the distributor's cigarettes occurred in the Illinois and that such a transaction constituted a taxable transaction under the Cigarette Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 453 et seq. (1983).


OVERVIEW: The distributor dealt with the delivery of cigarettes in the Illinois and Iowa. It purchased rolls of tax stamps from both states and affixed the proper tax stamp of the state in which the cigarettes were to be sold. Concerning Iowa-stamped cigarettes, the distributor sold and delivered some to retailers whose warehouses were located in Illinois yet retailed the cigarettes only in Iowa. The department assessed the distributor tax and penalties for the sale of Iowa-stamped cigarettes, ruling that in addition to the Iowa tax stamp, the distributor was required to purchase and affix an Illinois tax stamp to each pack. All of the cigarettes bearing the Iowa tax were retailed in Iowa and none were nor could be retailed in Illinois. The trial court affirmed this decision. On appeal, the court held that that the imposition of the Illinois cigarette stamp tax on Iowa-stamped cigarettes destined for sale in Iowa was an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, and resulted in double taxation of Iowa-bound cigarettes contrary to the legislative intent of the Cigarette Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 453 et seq. (1983).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and this cause was remanded with directions that said court enter an order vacating the department's deficiency assessment.

 

928 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


No. 3-85-0722


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


147 Ill. App. 3d 129; 497 N.E.2d 861; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2758; 100 Ill. Dec. 683



September 4, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted defendant upon his guilty plea of felony retail theft, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16A-3(a) (1985), and denied defendant's motion to vacate his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied equal protection and due process when he was convicted of a Class 3 felony for retail theft of merchandise valued at under $ 300, when the taking of the same property under the theft statute would constitute only a Class A misdemeanor. On review the court found no error. Defendant claimed that individuals charged under the ordinary theft or the retail theft statute were similarly situated, that the current statutory scheme was arbitrary and irrational, that it was not reasonably designed to remedy the evil at which it was directed, and that the legislature only inadvertently failed to correspondingly amend the retail theft statute. The court held that the retail-theft statute was constitutionally enacted to respond to the specific nature of theft in retail establishments. Due process did not require identical felony-value levels in the different types of theft and there was a reasonable basis for the felony-value levels in the instant statutory scheme. The felony-level differences between retail theft and ordinary theft were products of the legislature's prerogative to respond to the specific nature of theft in certain establishments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

929 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


United States Steel Corporation-South Works v. Industrial Com.


No. 1-85-1867WC


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Industrial Commission Division


147 Ill. App. 3d 402; 499 N.E.2d 60; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2792; 101 Ill. Dec. 693



August 27, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employee's widow and children, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which set aside the decision of the Industrial Commission denying appellee employer's request that the employee's life insurance be set off against the amount of death benefits payable to him under § 4(i) of the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.4(i) (1983).


OVERVIEW: The employee died after being doused by molten steel at the employer's plant. The employee was covered by a group life insurance policy that was a fringe benefit under an agreement between the employer and the union. The widow and the children filed a claim with the Industrial Commission and were awarded death benefits, burial expenses, and attorney fees. The widow and the children contended that the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974 (ERISA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001 et seq. (1982) preempted § 4(i) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.4(i) (1983). On appeal, the court reversed, holding that because the employer did not made an election to provide life insurance coverage or to apply those benefits as an offset to the employee's death benefits under the plain meaning of the § 4(i), the employee was not entitled to a setoff of the benefits. The court found that § 4(i) was not pre-empted by ERISA because § 4(i) did not prohibit something which was otherwise lawful under federal law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court which set aside the decision of the industrial commission and allowed the employer to set off the employee's life insurance benefits against the death benefits payable under the Workers' Compensation Act.

 

930 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Burmeister


No. 85-596


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


147 Ill. App. 3d 218; 497 N.E.2d 1212; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2773; 100 Ill. Dec. 850



August 26, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County; the Hon. David A. Englund, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count of criminal sexual assault and two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse. On each count, defendant was sentenced to concurrent four-year periods of probation and was fined.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of one count of criminal sexual assault and two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in connection with his fondling of his teenage stepdaughter. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent four-year periods of probation, and as a condition of his probation, defendant was ordered to serve concurrent 120-day terms of imprisonment followed by concurrent 150-day terms of periodic imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed the sexual assault conviction, vacated one of the sexual abuse convictions, and vacated the 150-day period imprisonment term. The court held that the broad definition of the term "penetration" in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-12(f) (1985) did not render the statute unreasonable and arbitrary. The court further held that the circuit court had not abused its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for a mistrial. The court also held that one of the sexual abuse convictions involved the same act as the sexual assault conviction, so that sexual abuse conviction could not stand. Finally, the court held that the 150-day periodic imprisonment term violated Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005- 7-1(c) (1985).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and modified in part and vacated in part a judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendant of one count of criminal sexual assault and two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse. On each count, defendant was sentenced to concurrent four-year periods of probation and was fined.

Zebulon Enterprises, Inc. v. County of Du Page


No. 2-85-0454


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


146 Ill. App. 3d 515; 496 N.E.2d 1256; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2655; 100 Ill. Dec. 191



August 21, 1986, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment for appellee corporation in a declaratory judgment action regarding a special-use-permit requirement.


OVERVIEW: The corporation operated an adult book and video store in the county. The store included 29 booths where patrons could watch sexually explicit videotapes on coin-operated television sets. The county charged the corporation with violating its comprehensive zoning ordinance by operating the "mini-theaters" without first acquiring a special-use permit from the county board. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the corporation could continue its business under the "grandfather" provision of the ordinance as amended.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court entering summary judgment for the corporation in a suit challenging the county's zoning ordinance was affirmed.

 

932 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Foster & Kleiser v. Chicago


No. 85-3612


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 928; 497 N.E.2d 459; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2717; 100 Ill. Dec. 481



August 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff advertising company received permits from defendant city to erect two electric signs. After the signs were erected, the city revoked the permits. The city appealed a ruling of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that the permits were valid and ripened into property rights. The advertising company cross appealed the denial of injunctive relief and the holding that the permits were properly revoked.


OVERVIEW: The advertising company sought and received city permission to attach signs to a historic structure. After the signs were erected, the city revoked the permits. In affirming a judgment denying injunctive relief and holding that the permits were properly revoked, the court held that there was no constitutional violation in the ordinance revoking the permits, so the Immunity Act (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para 2-104 (1985)) precluded any liability on the part of the city. The ordinance language sufficiently informed those in the adverting company' position of the requirements for satisfying the landmark ordinance. The advertising company knew landmark structures were present at the intersections, but failed to obtain necessary landmark commission approval. The city convincingly argued that the advertising company violated several ordinances, thus preventing it from acquiring vested property rights in the permits. Finally, the court held that the permits issued were permissive in nature, and could have been withdrawn at any time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found that the permits were properly revoked and that the advertising company had to remove the sign structures. The judgment that the advertising company acquired a property interest in the permits and was entitled to an award of damages was reversed.

 

933 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Gordon


No. 85-0568


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 898; 497 N.E.2d 442; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2713; 100 Ill. Dec. 464



August 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Daniel J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which rendered judgment for defendant homeowners, who were issued a citation for violating an ordinance which prohibited the use of "For Sale" signs on residences, and held that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners were issued citations for violating the municipal code banning outdoor advertising signs in certain residential districts. On a motion to dismiss, the homeowners alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it restricted their first amendment right to commercial free speech and that it was impermissibly vague and overbroad. The trial court held that the ordinance was not vague but infringed on homeowners' constitutionally guaranteed right to freedom of speech without a commensurate reason. The city appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the city failed to produce any evidence that the regulation of commercial speech served its substantial interest in improving traffic safety and the appearance of the city. The court noted that city erroneously assumed that the proscription of "For Sale" signs would prevent "white flight" by reducing public awareness of potential realty sales and thereby decreasing public concern over selling. But even assuming arguendo that the city's underlying objectives in banning "For Sale" signs were proper, it could not rely upon any assumptions but rather had to prove that the ordinance directly affected its interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment finding that the city's ordinance against the use of "For Sale" signs on residences was unconstitutional.

 

934 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Brazen v. Finley


No. 84-2926


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 750; 497 N.E.2d 1013; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2692; 100 Ill. Dec. 744



August 15, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition for the issuance of a writ of mandamus requiring defendant, circuit court clerk (clerk), to accept the filing of a complaint for process without the requisite affidavit of compliance mandated by Cook (Ill.) Cir. Ct., R. 0.7. The attorney had attempted to file a petition for dissolution of marriage without the required affidavit.


OVERVIEW: Rule 0.7 provided that the unethical solicitation of employment by attorneys and the payment of commissions, living expenses, or other gratuities in connection with employment was prohibited. It required attorneys representing clients in personal injury and domestic relations cases to submit an affidavit of compliance indicating the factual circumstances under which they had obtained their employment. The attorney contended that Rule 0.7 was invalid because it was contrary to the limitations imposed by constitutional and statutory law. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case. The court determined that Rule 0.7 exceeded the authority of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(a) and Ill. Const. art. VI, § 7(c) (1970). The court explained that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21 authorized the circuit court to adopt rules governing matters of pleading, practice, and procedure and that the range of Cook (Ill.) Cir. Ct., Rule 0.7 went far beyond Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(c)'s authority by purporting to monitor attorney-client employment arrangements and by requiring disclosure of an attorney's compliance with ethical obligations as a condition of access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had denied the attorney's petition for a writ of mandamus and remanded the cause with directions to issue the writ of mandamus.

 

935 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 2-85-0739


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


146 Ill. App. 3d 1; 496 N.E.2d 740; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2582; 99 Ill. Dec. 879



August 11, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bookseller sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois) convicting it of obscenity in connection with the sale of magazines to an undercover police officer in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1983) and imposing a fine.


OVERVIEW: At its trial, the bookseller attempted to introduce into evidence ordinances from five Illinois municipalities which regulated zoning for adult theatres, bookstores, and nightclubs, but the trial court refused to admit such ordinances. Defendant contended this exclusion constituted error on the trial court's part because the ordinances were admissible as evidence of the degree of public acceptance of sexually explicit material pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(4) (1983) and were relevant evidence of a statewide community standard. The court rejected that contention, holding that the admission of evidence was within the sound discretion of the trial court judge and that there was no clear showing that he had abused that discretion. Further, the court observed that the ordinances were not intended to be an acknowledgement by the municipalities that had adopted them of the public acceptance of materials deemed obscene. The fact the jury failed to accept testimony from a defense expert regarding a survey of statewide community standards did not mean the jurors did not apply a community standard to finding the bookseller guilty of obscenity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Dukes


No. 85-0465


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 790; 497 N.E.2d 351; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2698; 100 Ill. Dec. 373



August 7, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Lawrence Passarella, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1 (1981), and aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1.1(a)(1) (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were observed at the scene of an alleged arson shortly before the fire was discovered and were seen running from the building. Defendants were convicted of arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1 (1981), and aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1.1(a)(1) (1981). Defendants appealed and the court affirmed their convictions for arson and reversed their convictions for aggravated arson. The court found that no witnesses actually saw defendants start the fire. The evidence against defendants was entirely circumstantial. The reasonable hypothesis of innocence standard applied, and no reasonable hypothesis of innocence arose from the evidence. Defendants had been found guilty of arson beyond a reasonable doubt. However, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1.1(a)(1) (1981), was unconstitutional because the statute, as written, swept too broadly by punishing innocent as well as culpable conduct in setting fires.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendants for arson and reversed their convictions for aggravated arson. The sentences imposed on the aggravated-arson convictions were vacated.

 

937 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henigan


No. 85-0334


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 168; 497 N.E.2d 134; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2607; 100 Ill. Dec. 254



July 29, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. DiVito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of unlawful use of firearms by a felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1(a) after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant claimed that § 24-1.1(a) was an unconstitutional deprivation of his right to due process, and that the State failed to prove the corpus delicti aliunde his statement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a victim after the victim menaced defendant with a knife. There was conflicting testimony as to whether the gun had been purchased by defendant, when it had been purchased, or if the gun belonged to someone else. Defendant claimed that § 24-1.1(a) was an unconstitutional, arbitrary, and unreasonable exercise of the State's police power, which violated his right to due process by depriving him of his affirmative defenses of necessity and self-defense. The court affirmed. Self-defense could be raised when evidence was presented that defendant reasonably believed that imminent danger existed. Necessity could be asserted when defendant claimed that he did not cause the situation and that his conduct was necessary to avoid greater injury than that, which could reasonably have resulted from his conduct. Defendant was not precluded from raising the affirmative defenses to a charge they could properly be used to rebut. However, neither defense could be raised against the charge of knowing possession of a firearm by a felon because the restriction against felons was a reasonable exercise of the State's police power.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Gibbs v. Estate of Dolan


No. 85-2299


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 203; 496 N.E.2d 1126; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2611; 100 Ill. Dec. 61



July 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Frank M. Siracusa, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimants challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled their claim against appellee estate was time barred under § 18-3 of the Illinois Probate Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 18-3. The claimants contended that the Act's notice by publication provisions violated due process requirements and that the local daily law bulletin was not a secular newspaper of general circulation.


OVERVIEW: The claimants filed a claim against the estate after the expiration of the six-month statutory claim period, seeking to recover the purchase price of a motor home pursuant to the revocation-of-acceptance provisions of the Uniform Commercial Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 26, para. 2-608 (1983). After the trial court ruled the disputed claim was time barred, the claimants sought review of the trial court's findings that para. 18-3 was not unconstitutional on its face or as applied, that the local daily law bulletin was a secular newspaper of general circulation, and that their claim had not been timely filed. The court on appeal affirmed the trial court's ruling based on its determination that (1) due process did not require the estate representative to notify the claimants of the impending expiration of the limitations period for filing their estate claim; (2) para. 18-13 was neither facially invalid nor as applied to the claimants, and did not deprive the claimants of their property without requisite due process; and (3) the trial court correctly found that the local daily law bulletin was a secular newspaper of general circulation as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 100, para. 5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Enis


No. 2-84-0733


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


145 Ill. App. 3d 753; 495 N.E.2d 1319; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2533; 99 Ill. Dec. 584



July 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Richard C. Christian and the Hon. Charles F. Scott, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted petitioner department's application to find the parents unfit and to terminate their parental rights over their infant daughter. The parents claimed that § 1(D)(f) of the Illinois Adoption Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(f) (1983), violated due process.


OVERVIEW: Respondent parents had twice been found to have abused their infant daughter, under § 4-8 of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, paras. 704-708 (1983). Petitioner department filed an action to declare the parents unfit and to terminate their parental rights pursuant to § 1(D)(f) of the Illinois Adoption Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(f) (1983). The department offered no evidence other than the two prior orders, and the parents offered no evidence. The department's application was granted and the parents appealed on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) the statute required merely a showing that there had been two prior findings of abuse; (2) abuse had not been proved by clear and convincing evidence at either of the juvenile proceedings or at the termination proceeding; (3) the statutes, in their requirement that abuse be proved merely by a preponderance of the evidence, deprived the parents if due process of law; and (4) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(f) (1983), was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order that granted petitioner department's application to terminate the parental rights of respondent parents in their minor child was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Witherell v. Weimer


No. 3-84-0759


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


148 Ill. App. 3d 32; 499 N.E.2d 46; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2885; 101 Ill. Dec. 679



July 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. John Corman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in a medical malpractice action appealed a reduction by the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois) in a jury award against defendant doctors, who appealed the verdict against them.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought damages from the doctors for malpractice. In reversing a judgment for plaintiff, the court held that the jury was improperly instructed on the issue of causation, even though the parties had not objected to the instruction. Under the instruction given, the doctors were deprived of having their defense as to causation considered by the jury. The court also reversed the determination that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1205 (1983), which restricted medical malpractice recovery to items not reimbursed, was unconstitutional. The section did not hinder plaintiff's right to a full recovery for damages. Equity dictated that the case be remanded to give the doctors the opportunity to prove alleged negligence on plaintiff's part. The doctors were not prejudiced by pharmacological testimony of an unlicensed expert who learned from and taught in the same school of medicine, as his practical knowledge was gained under similar circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against the doctors in plaintiff's medical malpractice action, and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Johnson


No. 5-84-0782


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


146 Ill. App. 3d 640; 497 N.E.2d 308; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2194; 100 Ill. Dec. 330



July 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Patrick J. Fleming, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated indecent behavior with a child in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-4.1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated indecent behavior with a child after sexually assaulting his five-year-old stepdaughter. The stepdaughter was permitted to testify by videotape with defendant in a different room where he could see the child but she could not see him. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling allowing the testimony by videotape. The court held that the testimony was not violative of Ill Sup. Ct. R. 414(a), 206(e); 87 Ill. 2d. R. 414(a), 206(e), which dealt with the availability of witnesses and videotaped depositions respectively. The court held that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to confront a witness was not absolute and could be compromised upon proper showing of necessity and opportunity for cross-examination. The opportunity for cross-examination was met even though defendant was in a separate room from his counsel during the deposition because the trial court had taken steps to make sure that he was able to communicate with his counsel as needed. The separation did not affect defendant's right to effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated indecent liberties with a child.

People v. Wallace


No. 84-1095


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


145 Ill. App. 3d 247; 495 N.E.2d 665; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2470; 99 Ill. Dec. 218



July 10, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Bernard E. Drew, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to 20 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual assault. He was convicted based on evidence that he had forced his way into the complainant's home by grabbing her by the arm as she tried to enter and thereafter compelled her to engage in sexual intercourse with him. He was sentenced to 20 years of imprisonment. On appeal, he argued that there was insufficient evidence of the bodily harm required to elevate criminal sexual assault to aggravated criminal sexual assault, that the trial judge should have instructed the jurors on the meaning of the phrase "bodily harm," and that the trial judge improperly treated his rape charge in another state as an aggravating factor at sentencing. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding the bruising on the complainant's arm sufficient to qualify as bodily harm, and that defendant's jury instruction claim was waived. The court reversed as to sentencing, however, inasmuch as a mere arrest could not be treated as an aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant for aggravated criminal sexual assault was affirmed. His sentence, however, was vacated, and his case was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 85-0504


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


145 Ill. App. 3d 1054; 495 N.E.2d 1292; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2577; 99 Ill. Dec. 557



July 9, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County; the Hon. Wilson Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which convicted it of three counts of obscenity involving the sale of certain magazines seized during a search pursuant to a warrant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in an amended information with ten counts of obscenity involving the sale of certain magazines seized during a search pursuant to a warrant. Following a mistrial after the jury was unable to reach a verdict, defendant was then tried in a jury trial on only three counts and was found guilty of all three counts of obscenity. Defendant sought review, contending that the issuing judge had insufficient facts to establish probable cause and that the search warrant did not sufficiently particularize the items to be seized and should have been quashed by the trial court as a general warrant. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that the search warrant was constitutionally sound because the items to be seized were particularly described in the most feasible way possible. The court further held that the judicial officer issuing the search warrant was not required to view the material to be seized in order to establish probable cause, as long as the supporting affidavits were specific and were not merely conclusional. The court also held that the issuing judge need not determine whether the materials in question were obscene beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of all three counts of obscenity.

People v. Capsel


No. 3-85-0510


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 1057; 496 N.E.2d 10; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2438; 99 Ill. Dec. 664



July 8, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 12, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. Frank X. Yackley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed form the judgment of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois) convicting him of unlawful use of firearms by a felon under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1 (1985). Defendant contended that para. 24-1.1 was so unreasonable as to violate both Federal and State due process. He also contended that he was denied due process when he was prosecuted under para. 24-1.1 rather than Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-3.1 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The charges were based upon defendant's knowing possession of a shotgun, a sawed-off baseball-bat bludgeon, and three pool-cue sections. In 1982, defendant had been convicted of the felony of unlawful possession of a controlled substance. In affirming the conviction by the trial court, the court held that the facts did not support a finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1 (1985) was unconstitutional. Defendant was convicted of a felony less than three years before the charged offenses. Even if the statute was considered overbroad, as applied under the circumstances it was not unconstitutional. The court also rejected defendant's argument that he was denied equal protection and due process as his possession of a shot gun was prosecuted under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1 rather than under section Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-3.1. The statutory scheme did not violate equal protection, provided no undue discretion to the prosecution, and did not invalidly delegate authority. Defendant's firearms prosecution involved no deprivation of due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of unlawful use of firearms by a felon.

Nelson v. Hix


No. 85-0447


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


146 Ill. App. 3d 486; 496 N.E.2d 1052; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2651; 99 Ill. Dec. 960

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the administrator of the estate of a deceased wife, a Canada resident, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which applied the law of Illinois and dismissed the administrator's complaint against defendant husband, also a Canada resident, in a personal injury action based on a car accident in Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The wife and husband were visiting relatives in Illinois when their car struck a second car and the wife, who was a passenger, was injured. They filed an action against the second driver; the husband settled with that driver, and the wife amended her complaint to add the husband as a defendant. She died of cancer while the action was pending. The administrator sought damages based on the Wrongful Death Act and the Survival Act. The trial court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 152, § 65(3)(a) (1980), which permitted tort actions between spouses, controlled. People v. Wilson


No. 84-2095


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


146 Ill. App. 3d 567; 499 N.E.2d 972; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2663; 102 Ill. Dec. 192



July 3, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John W. Crilly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 122-1 et seq. (1985) (act). Defendant contended that the act provided that the trial court had to determine the frivolity or lack of merit of the petition before appointing counsel, which prejudiced defendant.


OVERVIEW: A trial court convicted defendant of murder and armed robbery. Defendant filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief and claimed that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because his lawyer did not make an effort to check alibi evidence and witnesses. Defendant requested a hearing and counsel. More than 30 days later and without appointing counsel a different trial court denied the petition without stating factual findings because defendant's claim set forth no grounds for legal relief. The court found that the 30-day requirement of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 122-2.1(a) was directory rather than mandatory. However, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were not frivolous or patently without merit. Moreover, the court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 122-2.1, the rule that required trial court's to make their frivolity ruling before it appointed counsel during post-conviction proceedings, conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) and violated the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the procedure did not provide defendant with meaningful access to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied defendant post-conviction relief. The court found that a statutory procedure wherein the trial court made a finding of whether a post-conviction petition was frivolous before it appointed counsel did not provide meaningful, adequate, and effective access to the courts. The court held that the procedure conflicted with state supreme court rules and violated notions of due process.

Messina v. Chicago


No. 85-1615


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


145 Ill. App. 3d 549; 495 N.E.2d 1228; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2515; 99 Ill. Dec. 493



June 30, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George A. Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a complaint and an amended complaint in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for a declaratory judgment that he was discharged from his probationary position with defendant employer, a city, in violation of article IX, § 3, of the Personnel Rules of the City of Chicago. The employee appealed from the dismissal of his lawsuit due to his failure to state a cause of action upon which relief could have been granted.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged from his position as a probationary employee in the employer's department of public works because he allowed a disparaging comment to remain in cement that was finished by the employee. The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that dismissed the second count of the amended complaint because the employer's personnel rules and ordinance were proper exercises of its home rule power. Thus, the employer was not bound by any conflicting personnel standards in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-1-14 (1985). The court held that the trial court erred when it dismissed the remainder of the complaint because the employee alleged that the employer's personnel rules did not authorize it to discipline the employee by suspension and then to discipline him a second time for the same misconduct. Although the employee was on probation and his employment was terminable without cause, the employer could not have terminated the employee unless the employer followed its own procedures. The court held that the amended complaint did not allege a federal due process claim and that a claim for attorney fees was not ripe.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the trial court. The court remanded the case to give the employer an opportunity to demonstrate whether any other ordinance or rule authorized the suspension and subsequent discharge of the employee for a single act of misconduct.

Nicpon v. Nicpon


No. 85-2271


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


145 Ill. App. 3d 464; 495 N.E.2d 1193; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2500; 99 Ill. Dec. 458



June 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed a personal injury action she filed against defendant husband. The trial court held that the action was barred by the Illinois Interspousal-Immunity Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1001 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The wife, through her guardian, filed an action for personal injuries she sustained in an automobile accident allegedly caused by the wilful and wanton misconduct of her husband. The action was dismissed on the grounds that it was barred by the Illinois Interspousal-Immunity Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1001 (1985), which barred spouses from suing each other for non-intentional tort injuries. On appeal, the wife claimed that the statute was an unconstitutional violation of equal protection under the federal and state constitutions. The court held that para. 1001 did not burden the marital relationship so directly and substantially as to infringe the fundamental right to marry. The court concluded that the decision to bring suit against one's spouse did not strategically advance the privacy and family interests found to be fundamentally important, nor did para. 1001 constitute a direct legal obstacle to marriage or significantly discourage it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Petrillo v. Syntex Laboratories, Inc.


No. 85-604


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


148 Ill. App. 3d 581; 499 N.E.2d 952; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2952; 102 Ill. Dec. 172



June 26, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Brian L. Crowe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defense attorney refused to comply with an order which barred him from private, ex parte conferences with appellee claimants' treating physicians in the claimants' product liability action against defendant corporation. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order which found the defense attorney in direct contempt of court and fined him $ 1. The defense attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: A defense counsel was found in contempt of court after he refused to comply with an order which barred him from private, ex parte conferences with the treating physicians of claimants in a product liability action against a corporation. The defense counsel appealed and asserted that the conferences should be permitted on the grounds that the claimants waived their physician-patient privilege when they filed the lawsuit and prohibition of the conferences violated the defense counsel's freedom of speech rights under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that prohibition of ex parte conferences was supported by public policy from the medical code of ethics and fiduciary patient-physician relationship, the discovery process, and the physician-patient privilege under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, para. 8 -- 802. The court held that the order was not violative of freedom of speech rights or an unreasonable time, place, and manner restriction because the state's interest in the confidential and fiduciary relationship outweighed the freedom of speech rights and the discovery process provided an ample alternative to defense counsel to obtain the information he sought.


OUTCOME: The order which found the defense attorney in contempt of court was affirmed.

People v. Hengl


No. 3-85-0698


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 405; 494 N.E.2d 937; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2359; 98 Ill. Dec. 815



June 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. L. E. Ellison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion to withdraw his plea of guilty to charges of attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault after a sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: The victim stated that defendant forced his way into her car. While the car was stopped, defendant forced the victim between the seats and tore her clothes off. Defendant could not, however, force her legs apart. The victim's screams finally attracted someone's attention, and she received help. Defendant escaped from the car. Defendant pleaded guilty to attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault. After the sentencing hearing, the trial court denied defendant's motion to withdraw his plea. Affirming, the court held that the trial judge properly considered the victim's impact statement that was included in the presentence report. The court found that the impact statement in the presentence report did have to follow the preparation requirements of sentencing-hearing statements under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-4-1(a)(6) (1985). The court held that the sentence was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion based on the finding that defendant's conduct caused or threatened physical harm. The court found that "bodily harm" as defined by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(a)(2) (1984) was not inherent in the use of force found in criminal sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

951 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Goldstein v. Mitchell


No. 2-85-0125


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


144 Ill. App. 3d 474; 494 N.E.2d 914; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2367; 98 Ill. Dec. 792



June 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. William D. Block, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, landowner and tenant, appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, drainage district board of commissioners (board) and commissioner of the drainage district, in plaintiffs' action challenging the election process and the voting provisions under the Illinois Drainage Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 42, para. 4-5 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought their action against defendants challenging various provisions in the Code after the landowner was not elected to the board and the tenant was not permitted to vote during the election. The parties filed motions for summary judgment, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that because the purpose of the drainage district was to manage erosion and flooding problems in the drainage district and because the Code had a disproportionate effect on the class that was allowed to vote because of the location of their property, the one-person, one-vote rule was not applicable. Thus, the voting plan set forth in § 4-5 did not violate equal protection under either the Illinois Constitution or the United States Constitution. The court also held that the Code adequately defined a landowner and was not vague and, further, that the landowner and the tenant did not have standing to raise the issue that the Code was unconstitutionally vague because they had not suffered any injury. Finally, the court held that the improprieties during the election did not constitute a violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment in favor of defendants in plaintiffs' action challenging the voting provisions of the Code.

 

952 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Traffic Court Driver Improv. Educational Foundation v. Peoria Journal Star, Inc.


No. 3-85-0455


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 555; 494 N.E.2d 939; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2376; 98 Ill. Dec. 817



June 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Dennis K. Cashman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foundation sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which dismissed the foundation's claims against defendants, the media, chief judge, state's attorney, and state officials, for defamation, conspiracy to interfere with a business relationship, and violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Three articles appeared in the newspaper that criticized the foundation's driver improvement program. The articles contained statements that the foundation misrepresented the program's affiliation with the state, that the program's director misrepresented his credentials, that a remark was made in a driving improvement class that the Illinois judicial system was corrupt, and that the chief judge and state's attorney were withdrawing their support for the program. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the defamation, conspiracy to interfere with a business relationship, and § 1983 case because the chief judge's statements were made in his capacity as chief judge, so he was entitled to judicial immunity. The reasonable expectation of continued referrals based upon past performance was not a property interest entitled to due process protection. While there was a conspiracy, the result of the conspiracy was not tortious, so the foundation's § 1983 claim was not actionable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the foundation's claims against the media, chief judge, state's attorney, and state officials for defamation, conspiracy to interfere with a business relationship, and violations § 1983.

National Realty & Inv. Co. v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 2-85-0200


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


144 Ill. App. 3d 541; 494 N.E.2d 924; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2375; 98 Ill. Dec. 802



June 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert D. McLaren, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which confirmed a decision by appellee Department of Revenue that yearly installments from the sale of a hotel by taxpayer were taxable income under the Illinois Tax Act.


OVERVIEW: The department sent the taxpayer a notice of deficiency after determining that the taxpayer was not entitled to a deduction for gains realized on a sale of a hotel. The taxpayer filed a claim for refund due and when the department denied the claim, he filed a protest. After a hearing, the department denied refunds and assessed deficiencies. The trial court upheld the department's decision. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that installments from the sale of the hotel that were received after the enactment of the Illinois Income Tax Act were properly taxed even though the sale occurred nine years prior to the effective date of the statute where the gain was actually realized when the payment was received. The court noted that the receipt of payment was the taxable event upon which the tax was levied and that the tax was not directed at payments received before the date of the Act. The court found that the denial of the valuation-limitation deduction under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2-203 to a corporation was not unconstitutional on the basis that it was discriminatory where the taxpayer failed to show that there was an unreasonable or arbitrary classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment which found that yearly installments from the sale of a hotel by the taxpayer were taxable income.

 

954 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Monmouth v. Galesburg Printing & Pub. Co.


No. 3-85-0515


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 224; 494 N.E.2d 896; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2337; 98 Ill. Dec. 774



June 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Warren County; the Hon. Francis P. Murphy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Warren County (Illinois) that dismissed its action for declaratory judgment and injunction against appellee newspaper in a dispute over the publication of names, ages, and addresses of victims of crimes that occurred in the city. The newspaper cross-appealed the trial court's judgment that held Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 116, para. 207(b)(v) (1985) to have been constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city challenged the trial court's dismissal of its complaint for declaratory judgment and injunction against the newspaper to prevent publication of the names, ages, and addresses of crime victims. The newspapers challenged the trial court's judgment as to the constitutionality of the Freedom of Information Act (FOIA). The court affirmed and first addressed the question of whether FOIA exempted the publication of information about crime victims. The newspaper asserted that the information entitled to the exemption from publication had to have been a clearly unwarranted invasion of the victim's privacy. The court held that the legislative intent of FOIA was that the public had a right to know what the government was doing, and that any exemptions were limited. The court held that the city's position on a blanket exemption was not consistent with legislative intent. The court held that FOIA constituted prior restraint on the newspaper's ability to gather news that was not related to a compelling governmental interest. The court found that a case-by-case approach could have been used to protect crime victims from an unwarranted invasion of privacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the legislative intent of FOIA was that the public had a right to know what government was doing, and that the blanket exemption imposed a prior restraint on the newspaper's ability to gather news that was not related to a compelling governmental interest.

Park Forest v. Thomason


No. 85-2717


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


145 Ill. App. 3d 327; 495 N.E.2d 1036; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2482; 99 Ill. Dec. 301



June 12, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Marvin E. Gavin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to vacate his plea of guilty of driving under the influence of liquor in violation of a village ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence of liquor in violation of the village ordinance, which provided for a fine of not less than $ 150 nor more than $ 500, but did not provide for or authorize a jail sentence. Defendant filed a motion to vacate his plea of guilty on the basis that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The village appealed the trial court's grant of defendant's motion. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, par. 11-501(c) (1983), which provided that every person convicted of violating it should have been guilty of a Class A misdemeanor, evidenced a statutory scheme to remove from home rule units as well as other municipalities the discretion of providing for Class A misdemeanor treatment in their local ordinances for drunken drivers. The court held that the ordinance was invalid for failing to comply with the mandate of the Illinois Vehicle Code. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting defendant's motion to vacate his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

956 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Crawford


No. 85-1820


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


145 Ill. App. 3d 318; 495 N.E.2d 1025; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2481; 99 Ill. Dec. 290



June 11, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John A. McElligott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of unlawful use of a firearm by a felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24--1.1 (!984 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had previously been convicted of voluntary manslaughter, was convicted of unlawful use of a firearm by a felon after police observed defendant standing outside his residence with a revolver in the waistband of his pants. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. On appeal, defendant contended that § 24--1.1 was unconstitutional. Enactment of § 24--1.1 was a reasonable use of the state's police power. The standard for determining the legislature's proper exercise of the police power was whether the statute was reasonably designed to remedy the evil which the legislature had determined to be a threat to the public health, safety, and general welfare. The legislature was vested with wide discretion in determining what the public interest required and what means were needed to promote and protect that interest. The purpose of § 24--1.1 was to protect the health and safety of the public by deterring possession of weapons by convicted felons, and this was a proper exercise of the police power. The court further found that the prohibition against use and possession of weapons by felons did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of a firearm by a felon.

 

957 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilson


No. 4-85-0759


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


144 Ill. App. 3d 290; 494 N.E.2d 849; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2347; 98 Ill. Dec. 727



June 10, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. John R. DeLaMar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which placed her on conditional discharge for the offense of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1983) and subjected her to various conditions including the payment of costs and a fine.


OVERVIEW: In addition to a general fine, defendant had to make small payments to the Traffic and Criminal Conviction Surcharge Fund of the State Treasury, to Champaign County to finance its court system, to the Drivers Education Fund, and to the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund. She contended that the legislation purporting to authorize the assessments was unconstitutional. The court disagreed. First, the court rejected defendant's argument that the charges for the Traffic and Criminal Conviction Surcharge Fund and for Champaign County to finance its court system were taxes that violated the provisions of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2. The legislation authorizing the charge for the Traffic and Criminal Conviction Surcharge Fund clearly indicated that it was a penal fine and not a tax. Further, the fee to pay for operation of the county court system was imposed as a penalty for violating the law. Finally, the legislation providing for additional fines and penalties to be paid into the Drivers Education Fund and the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund was valid. The legislature had substantial discretion in setting the nature and the extent of penalties for criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

958 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Tobin v. McClure


No. 3-85-0548


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 33; 493 N.E.2d 1215; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2304; 98 Ill. Dec. 194



June 5, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. Daniel W. Gould, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant challenged a judgment from the Kankakee County Circuit Court (Illinois), which awarded her only part of her apartment security deposit and court costs in a dispute with defendant landlords, who claimed that the nail holes the tenant spackled would require repainting the entire apartment and that the nail holes were not part of normal wear and tear. The tenant also sought punitive damages and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The tenant had an apartment on an oral month-to-month lease and paid a security deposit, and she alleged that she left it in good condition, minus normal wear and tear. The trial judge found that the walls needed repainting and subtracted the painter's estimate from the deposit, awarding the tenant the rest plus court costs. On review, the court found the judgment against the manifest weight of the evidence, as the landlords knew about the nail holes before the tenant left but promised the full deposit, and there was no evidence of damage other than normal wear and tear. The court asserted that nail holes were normal wear and tear and should not have been taken from the deposit. The court disagreed that aggregation should extend to landlords owning unrelated structures which, in the aggregate, were 10 or more units, as there was a substantial penalty for landlords who did not comply with the law, too much for small landlords who lacked the large landlord's administrative resources, and harm caused by a dilatory large landlord could greatly exceed any by an isolated small landlord. The court modified the judgment to award the full deposit with court costs and otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment, awarding the tenant her full security deposit plus court costs, and affirming as modified.

People v. Huber


No. 4-85-0724


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


144 Ill. App. 3d 195; 494 N.E.2d 770; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2333; 98 Ill. Dec. 648



June 5, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County; the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol and failure to reduce speed to avoid an accident. Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which, after a jury had convicted him of reckless homicide under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-3(b)(2) (1983), imposed an extended-term sentence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 1005-8-1(a), 1005-8-2(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle collided with another, killing three people, two of whom were under 12 years of age. The trial court sentenced defendant to an extended sentence pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(3)(i) (1983). Defendant asserted that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing the sentence because the purpose of an extended sentence was to deter criminal conduct and his conduct was not intentional. The court noted that defendant's assertion was essentially that reckless conduct could not be deterred. The court affirmed the judgment. The court based its rejection of defendant's argument on the fact that, by the definition of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 4-6 (1983), recklessness included the conscious disregard of a substantial and unjustifiable risk that a result would follow from one's actions. Further, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2 did not require intent, but applied to any felony. Defendant's conviction was a class four felony. The court noted that a reviewing court should not ordinarily substitute its judgment regarding sentencing for that of the better-situated sentencing court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Church permitted her to inspect her records with the exception of three letters which church withheld on the advice of its attorney. Consumers Gas Co. v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 5-86-0044


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


144 Ill. App. 3d 229; 493 N.E.2d 1148; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2338; 98 Ill. Dec. 127



May 30, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Illinois Commerce Commission.



DISPOSITION: Motions denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public utility petitioned for direct review of an administrative decision issued by appellee Illinois Commerce Commission (commission) in a utility rate case. The public utility filed a motion to stay the commission's order and for an expedited appeal, pursuant to Section 10-201, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 10-201 (1985), of the Public Utilities Act and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 335, 87 Ill. 2d R. 335. The court issued its decision.


OVERVIEW: The court denied both of the public utility's motions. The court held that (1) under the separation of powers doctrine, § 10-201 was an improper legislative intrusion into the area of appellate practice by attempting to regulate the method for perfecting a direct appeal of an administrative decision, and, to the extent that its provisions regarding direct appeals of administrative decisions, stays on appeal, and expedited hearings conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 335, 87 Ill. 2d R. 335, it was unconstitutional; and (2) the public utility failed to provide the court with a question of substance on appeal because it did not allege that the commission acted in an arbitrary or capricious manner in reaching its decision, or that the decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence, or that there was a likelihood of success on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the public utility's motion to stay the commission's order pending resolution of its appeal and denied the public utility's motion to expedite the appeal.
