North Sheffield, Inc. v. Chicago


No. 85-1650


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


144 Ill. App. 3d 913; 494 N.E.2d 711; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2417; 98 Ill. Dec. 589



May 30, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found the Chicago Alcoholic Beverage Tax Ordinance (ordinance), codified at Chicago Mun. Code § 200.5 et seq. (1984), to be in violation of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, pertaining to uniformity on the subjects of taxation, and therefore unconstitutional, void, and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that imposed a tax upon the purchase of alcoholic beverages that were immediately consumed upon the premises where they were purchased. The ordinance did not impose the tax upon the purchase of alcoholic beverages consumed off the premises where they were purchased. Plaintiff alcohol beverage distributors filed an action to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional and to enjoin its enforcement, contending that it was in violation of art. IX, § 2 because it created an arbitrary and unreasonable classification in defining the persons and transactions subject to the tax. The trial court found the ordinance unconstitutional and the city appealed. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that there was no rational basis for the distinction in imposing a tax upon an alcoholic beverage immediately consumed on the premises while not imposing the tax for the purchase of the same alcoholic beverage for the sole reason that it was to be consumed off the premises. The court concluded that the distinction was arbitrary and bore no reasonable relationship to the revenue raising purpose of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the city ordinance imposing a tax upon the consumption of alcohol on the premises where it was purchased was unconstitutional, void, and unenforceable.

 

963 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wolfe


Nos. 84-0921, 84-1097 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


144 Ill. App. 3d 843; 494 N.E.2d 670; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2409; 98 Ill. Dec. 548



May 27, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder and armed robbery, arguing that the trial court abused its discretion in allowing each of them a total of only six peremptory challenges during voir dire examination and in refusing to sever their cases from one another.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were found guilty of murder and armed robbery. On appeal, they claimed that the trial court abused its discretion in allowing each of them a total of only six peremptory challenges during voir dire examination of prospective jurors and in refusing to sever their cases from one another. In affirming, the court held that the antagonism which existed at trial was not the result of inconsistent defenses, but rather, concerned codefendants' pretrial statements, in which each asserted that the other was responsible for the shootings. The jury was properly instructed, however, to only use each defendant's statement against the defendant who made that confession. Accordingly, no severance was required. Also, while the court did not approve of several of the State's comments, the alleged errors were, for the most part, either invited reply to improper comments in defendants' closing arguments or the provoked response to arguments raised by defendants during trial. Further, in light of the evidence presented, defendants failed to demonstrate that the alleged errors unduly influenced the jury so as to constitute a material factor in their convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

964 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mason


No. 84-2802


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


145 Ill. App. 3d 218; 494 N.E.2d 1176; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2466; 98 Ill. Dec. 849



May 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her pro se petition for post-conviction relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 --2.1 (1985), prior to the appointment of counsel on the grounds that it was frivolous or patently without merit.


OVERVIEW: After defendant had already pursued appeals of her convictions, she filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court dismissed the petition pursuant to § 122 --2.1 as frivolous and without merit. Defendant appealed the dismissal, arguing that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) and the due process and equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The court reversed the dismissal, holding that defendant's equal protection rights were not violated because there was no disparate treatment between indigent and nonindigent post-conviction petitioners. However, the statute did violate the doctrine of separation of powers in that it directly conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c), which required the appointment of counsel at the appellate level for an indigent post-conviction petitioner. Further, the statute violated defendant's due process rights because it denied her adequate, effective, and meaningful access to the courts by allowing a dismissal on the merits, and the consequential application of res judicata, prior to the appointment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment dismissing defendant's pro se petition for post-conviction relief prior to the appointment of counsel.

County of Peoria v. Capitelli


No. 3-85-0278


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


144 Ill. App. 3d 14; 494 N.E.2d 155; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2300; 98 Ill. Dec. 228



May 22, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 15, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Jackson P. Newlin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), of allowing his cat to run at large in violation of Peoria County, Ill., Code § 5-19, enacted by plaintiff Peoria County.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that: (1) the county as a non-home-rule unit of government lacked the authority to enact the ordinance under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6 (1970), (2) attorneys for the city lacked the requisite authority to prosecute violations of the ordinance for the county under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 10 (1970), and (3) prosecution of county ordinance violations by city attorneys was a conflict of interest and violated the Code of Professional Responsibility. The court rejected defendant's first argument because the counties were given the express power to establish animal pounds and to dispose of stray animals under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 128 et seq. (1985), which concerned pet dogs and cats, and other animals. The grant of authority to dispose of stray animals contained the implied authority to regulate stray animals by less drastic means, such as fines, as provided by the Peoria County ordinance. The court found pursuant to the terms of the Peoria intergovernmental agreement, the attorneys for the city possessed the requisite authority to prosecute defendant, and there was no violation of the Code of professional Responsibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Eckman v. Board of Trustees


No. 2-85-0259


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


143 Ill. App. 3d 757; 493 N.E.2d 671; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2254; 97 Ill. Dec. 864



May 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. John L. Nickels, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which reversed the board's decision to reduce plaintiff claimant's disability pension benefits in an amount equal to workers' compensation benefits that he was to receive and ruled in favor of the claimant.


OVERVIEW: On review, the board argued that the trial court erred in finding that its interpretation and application of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 3 -- 114.5 (1985) was unconstitutional, that the board's action in reducing plaintiff's disability pension benefits did not constitute an administrative decision subject to review, and that the board's action, if subject to administrative review, was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court affirmed. The court found that, based on the language of the statute and the fact that the board determined the injury under consideration by it was not work related, the trial court was correct in concluding that the injury for which the claimant received his pension benefits and the injury for which he received his workers' compensation benefits did not constitute the same injury. The court concluded that the board's decision to reduce the claimant's non-duty-related pension benefits by the amount of his work-related workers' compensation benefits was clearly against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the board's decision to reduce the benefits paid to the claimant was affirmed.

People v. Le Shoure


No. 4-85-0628


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


143 Ill. App. 3d 839; 493 N.E.2d 687; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2265; 97 Ill. Dec. 880



May 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and modified in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) entered a judgment for forfeiture, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of various narcotics offenses. Subsequently, the state filed a petition in the circuit court requesting forfeiture of various items of personal property and weapons and ammunition seized from defendants' house at the time of defendants' arrest for the crimes charged. The court affirmed all aspects of the judgment appealed except in regard to forfeiture of firearms and ammunition. It reversed the judgment in regard to items of firearms and ammunition which were mentioned only in the separate petition of March 5th concerning firearms and ammunition. Pursuant to the court's power under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 366(a)(5) the judgment was modified to provide that (1) as to any such items which were not sold, they be turned over to any designee of defendant who was not prohibited from possessing such items; and (2) the proceeds of any of such items that were sold be turned over to defendant. The case was remanded to make any rulings necessary to carry out the court's directions in regard to the items listed only in the aforesaid separate petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed except in regard to the firearms and ammunition. The judgment was modified and remanded.

 

968 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wellington v. Chicago


No. 85-577


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


144 Ill. App. 3d 774; 494 N.E.2d 603; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2403; 98 Ill. Dec. 481



May 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Harold A. Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cabdrivers sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the cabdrivers' action that alleged that the Chicago transaction tax ordinance, Municipal Code of Chicago, ch. 200.1, sec. 2.A.1. (1981), was an invalid occupation tax under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6 as it applied to the cabdrivers, who leased their taxicabs.


OVERVIEW: The cabdrivers leased their taxicabs and were required to pay a tax under ch. 200.1, § 2A.1 for the lease of property. They sought to have the law declared an unconstitutional occupation tax under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6, but the trial court held that it was a constitutional transaction tax. On appeal, the court affirmed because the transaction tax was not designed to impose a tax upon the occupation of being a cabdriver, so it was not an occupation tax. The tax was one which some cabdrivers had to pay incidental to their occupation. The practical operation and effect test was not appropriate because the disputed tax was not a service tax. Also, the essence of the lease was the lease of personal property, the taxicab, not the taxi license, the trademarks, or the tradename. Thus, the leases were essentially leases of tangible personal property. The court also upheld Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11- 42-6 (1985) because home rule units should not be denied pre-1970 municipal powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which dismissed the cabdrivers' action that alleged that the Chicago transaction tax ordinance was an invalid occupation tax under the Illinois Constitution as it applied to the cabdrivers, who leased their taxicabs.

Bobber Auto Truck Plaza v. Department of Revenue


No. 5-85-0387


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


143 Ill. App. 3d 614; 493 N.E.2d 404; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2235; 97 Ill. Dec. 741



May 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County; the Hon. Edward C. Eberspacher, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Illinois Department of Revenue, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois) that reversed a decision by the Department denying the taxpayer's claim for credit or refund for the overpayment of retailers' occupation tax and municipal retailers' occupation tax that it made over several tax years.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer operated a truck stop where it sold fuel. The taxpayer's accountant realized that the taxpayer had paid retailers' occupation tax and municipal retailers' occupation tax on amounts from fuel sales, which included federal excise tax. The accountant corrected its method of tax calculation and applied to the Department for credits on the taxes. The Department denied the claim, finding that the taxpayer "intended" to collect the excess tax and had not refunded the excess amounts to its customers. The trial court took judicial notice of fuel prices in the area at the time and ruled that the taxpayer bore the economic burden of the excess tax. On appeal, the court ruled that the trial judge erred by taking judicial notice of the fuel prices and that it should have remanded for a determination of that issue, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 3-111(7) (1983). Nonetheless, the uncontradicted evidence established that the taxpayer did not compute the amount of tax applicable to a given fuel sale until after its customers had paid for their fuel. Thus, the excess taxes were not passed on to the taxpayer's customers, and it was thus entitled to a credit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

970 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Southland News Co. v. People


No. 85-0211


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


143 Ill. App. 3d 971; 493 N.E.2d 398; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2280; 97 Ill. Dec. 735



May 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Robert J. French, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drive-in theater owner challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that affirmed a decision of a county commission in favor of appellee state. The county commission ruled that the theater owner had violated the county's theater licensing ordinance that regulated the showing of sexually explicit scenes. The theater owner was fined and the theater owner's license was suspended for 30 days.


OVERVIEW: The theater owner contended that the county ordinance was unconstitutional on its face because it required a theater operator to covenant not to show constitutionally protected movies if they were viewable from certain specified locations. On appeal, the court ruled that the license suspension imposed a prior restraint on the theater owner's freedom of speech without adequate safeguards and it was, therefore, unconstitutional. The portion of the judgment which affirmed the license suspension was reversed. However, the portion of the circuit court's judgment that affirmed the fines assessed against the theater owner was affirmed. The decision of the county commission was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The county presented the testimony of police officers and people who resided near the theater to the effect that on the dates in question they observed, from the locations specified in the ordinance, sexually explicit scenes. That testimony was sufficient to sustain the county commission's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of the state insofar as it affirmed the fines assessed against the theater owner. The portion of the judgment which affirmed the suspension of the theater owner's license was reversed.

People v. Clark

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) entered upon a jury verdict convicting him of several crimes including two murders. Defendant, who was 14 years of age when the crimes were committed, challenged the constitutionality of the procedures used under § 2 -- 7(3) of the Juvenile Court Act to try him as an adult, and the life sentence imposed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The trial court at the transfer hearing determined that it was not in the best interests of defendant and the public to proceed with the juvenile proceedings against him. Defendant was convicted of home invasion, and criminal sexual assault, as well as the two murders. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentencing of defendant. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702 -- 7(3) (1983) in transferring defendant to be tried as an adult. The court found that there was strong evidence that defendant was involved in the charged offenses, and the security of the public required that he be held in custody for a period extending beyond the age of minority. The court rejected defendant's contention that the mandatory life imprisonment imposed on him under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 8 --1(a)(1)(c) (1983) violated his due process rights. The court further held that the lack of a provision in the sentencing statute to include the trial court's consideration of evidence in mitigation did not violate defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amends. People v. Evans


No. 5-84-0734


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


143 Ill. App. 3d 236; 492 N.E.2d 1036; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2187; 97 Ill. Dec. 377



May 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. Snyder Howell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and modified in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for unlawful possession of a controlled substance and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a controlled substance and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. He was sentenced on the latter charge to 25 years' imprisonment, and a $ 3500 "street value fine" was imposed. On appeal, the court was convinced that the evidence was sufficient to exclude every reasonable theory of defendant's innocence and prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. However, in sentencing, the court found that the trial court's emphasis on defendant's lack of remorse was misplaced, given that defendant continued to maintain his innocence. Furthermore, the amount of the controlled substance was relevant to the seriousness of the offense, and the 35.1 grams of cocaine found was only slightly in excess of the minimum required to make the offense a Class X felony as opposed to a Class 1 felony. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing such a harsh sentence upon defendant. The court also determined that the statute authorizing a "street value fine" was not unconstitutionally vague, and defendant was entitled to credit toward his fine for jail timer served prior to sentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of a controlled substance and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver was affirmed. The sentence of imprisonment was reduced, and the cause remanded with directions to amend the mittimus to reflect a 10-year term of incarceration and to award defendant a credit towards his fine.

 

973 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Holloway


No. 84-2895


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


143 Ill. App. 3d 735; 493 N.E.2d 89; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2252; 97 Ill. Dec. 607



May 8, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. Mannion, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of soliciting for a prostitute, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-15(a)(1) (1983), for which he was sentenced to one year's conditional discharge. Defendant challenged the resulting judgment.


OVERVIEW: The only issue addressed on appeal was defendant's claim that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-15(a)(1) (1983) only prohibited actions of a person, typically a middleman, in seeking customers for a prostitute. Thus, even crediting the State's evidence that defendant attempted to solicit a prostitute for his own use, defendant argued that he did not violate § 11-15(a)(1). Before addressing § 11-15(a)(1)'s meaning, the court rejected the State's claim that defendant had waived the issue because he did not raise it in the trial court, ruling that because his claim challenged the subject matter jurisdiction of the trial court, it could be raised for the first time on appeal. With respect to the meaning of § 11-15(a)(1), the court declared that it was necessary to look to the statute as a whole, and because it was subject to differing interpretations, it was helpful to review its legislative history. Moreover, because it was a criminal statute, its provisions were strictly construed. Applying these principles, the court concluded that § 11-15(a)(1) was limited to the acts of a third person in soliciting customers for a prostitute and thus, did not prohibit defendant's actions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

People ex rel. Hartigan v. Moore


No. 84-2305


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


143 Ill. App. 3d 410; 493 N.E.2d 85; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2209; 97 Ill. Dec. 603; 90 A.L.R.4th 1093; 1986-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P67,154



May 7, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth C. Prince, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Government appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) order that dismissed the civil penalty action for failure to state a cause of action and expiration of the statute of limitations, and which denied the government's motion to amend the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The government brought civil action for bid rigging and conspiracy to conduct an unreasonable restraint of trade. The trial court dismissed the complaint because the statute of limitations had run and failure to state a cause of action. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred when it concluded the statute of limitations began to run when the rigged bids were submitted. The illegal act charged in the complaint was conspiracy to fix prices that continued at least until the defendants transferred a payment. This action was filed within the four-year limitations period and therefore was not time barred. It appeared from the nature of the proposed amendments that the inadequacies in pleadings found by the trial judge were curable, so dismissal was reversed. Regarding a prior discovery order, the court further found that the attorney general was not prohibited from using pre-complaint subpoenaed deposition material.


OUTCOME: Dismissal based on the statute of limitations was in error because the wrong date was used. As the inadequacies in the pleadings found by the trial judge were curable, dismissal was reversed and the case remanded.

Hoffman v. Nustra


Nos. 2-85-0012, 2-85-0032, 2-85-0036 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


143 Ill. App. 3d 259; 492 N.E.2d 981; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2190; 97 Ill. Dec. 322



May 5, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Laurence Inglis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a class action against defendants, a county and county officials, to challenge the collection of real estate transfer tax by the county. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) denied the taxpayers' motions for leave to amend their complaint, denied the intervenor taxpayer's petition to intervene as a class representative, and granted intervenor attorney general's petition to intervene. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the issues were: (1) whether the forgiveness statute, Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 120, para. 1001 (1985), was unconstitutional; (2) whether the taxpayers' proposed constitutional challenges and prayers for disgorgement were barred by stare decisis, res judicata, equitable considerations, or mitigating factors; (3) whether the trial court abused its discretion in denying the taxpayers' motions for leave to amend their complaint and for summary judgment; and (4) whether the trial court abused its discretion in denying the intervenor taxpayer's petition to intervene. The court held that: (1) there was no need to reach the issue of the constitutionality of the forgiveness statute; (2) the denial of the taxpayers' request to amend their complaint was not an abuse of discretion because timeliness and prejudice to the county were factors which the trial court may have considered; (3) the dismissal of the initial complaint was proper under the doctrine of stare decisis; and (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the intervenor taxpayer leave to intervene because the state attorney general was able to represent the public interest and the state department of revenue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgments denying the taxpayers' motions for leave to amend their complaint, dismissing their complaint, denying the intervenor taxpayer's petition to intervene as a class representative, and granting intervenor attorney general's petition to intervene.

People v. Elliott


No. 4-85-0520


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


143 Ill. App. 3d 72; 492 N.E.2d 946; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2167; 97 Ill. Dec. 287



May 1, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. John R. DeLaMar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, found him guilty of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(2) (1983). Defendant was sentenced to incarceration and fined.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction for driving while under the influence of alcohol, defendant raised the issues of whether the jury was correctly instructed on the law applicable to the evidence regarding defendant's blood-alcohol level based on the results of a chemical analysis of his breath and whether defendant was proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that instructions regarding inferences and presumptions related to the blood-alcohol testing were appropriate. The jury had been properly instructed as to its duties, the charge made against defendant, the presumption of innocence, the issues, and the burdens of proof. Also, the blood-alcohol content was not the only evidence submitted by the State concerning defendant's driving while under the influence. The arresting and backup officers' corroborating testimony was entirely adequate to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty. There was sufficient evidence to allow the jury to find defendant guilty. The officers' testimony, the blood-alcohol test, and defendant's admission that he had been drinking were sufficient to support the conviction beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Blaisdell v. Blaisdell


No. 84-3088


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


142 Ill. App. 3d 1034; 492 N.E.2d 622; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2147; 97 Ill. Dec. 186



April 29, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Barbara J. Disko, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee ex wife filed suit against appellant ex husband to obtain a modification of a child-support order. Finding that the ex wife had shown a substantial change in circumstance, the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) ordered an increase in monthly child-support payments pursuant to § 505(a) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 505(a). The ex husband appealed the trial court's order.


OVERVIEW: The ex husband argued that § 505(a) violated various provisions of the Federal and State Constitutions. The ex husband's constitutional challenge was based on the erroneous assumption that, under § 505(a), courts were mandated to follow literally the schedule for child support. In rejecting the ex husband's argument that § 505(a) violated the separation-of-powers requirement of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1, or Ill. Const. art. IV, § 1, the court held that the child support guidelines involved application of substantive law and were not an incursion into the power of the judiciary. The court further held that § 505(a) was consistent with constitutional standards in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 in that it was a general law that operated equally among divorced parents. The court found that the procedural protections afforded to the ex husband in the trial court far exceeded any which were constitutionally required and, therefore, § 505(a) did not deprive the ex husband of procedural due process under both the Federal and State Constitutions. Moreover, the court ruled that § 505(a) did not deprive the ex husband of equal protection of law under the Federal and Illinois Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted the ex wife's request for modification of the child-support order.

Kaniuk v. Safeco Ins. Co.


No. 85-396


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


142 Ill. App. 3d 1070; 492 N.E.2d 592; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2152; 97 Ill. Dec. 156



April 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Cornelius F. Dore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee insurer's motion to dismiss count III of the insured's complaint.


OVERVIEW: The insured sued the insurer and alleged that the insurer refused to pay a valid claim on a policy of fire insurance. In one of the counts, the insured sought exemplary damages of one million dollars for the insurer's bad-faith conduct. The insurer moved to dismiss the count, and the trial court granted the motion. The insured challenged the decision, and argued that the statute deprived them of their right to trial by jury to determine the proper amount of punitive damages. The court affirmed the decision, and held that under the statute the trial court alone was to determine the proper measure of punitive damages, within the given limits pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 73, para. 767. However, where punitive damages may be assessed, they were allowed in the nature of punishment and as a warning and example to deter a defendant from committing like offenses in the future. Therefore, the insured could not complain of any deprivation of their rights when punitive damages were assessed by a court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the insurer's motion to dismiss.

Sweis v. Chicago


No. 84-2485


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint challenging the validity under Ill. Rev. The court held that there was no due process violation because the city had a rational basis for differential taxation in the area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the citizens' complaint, which challenged the validity of the city's ordinance creating a special service tax area and its tax levy ordinances to fund the operation of a public parking facility.

People v. Pride


No. 85-190


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


144 Ill. App. 3d 612; 494 N.E.2d 509; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2385; 98 Ill. Dec. 387



April 2, 1986, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Massey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of voluntary manslaughter and armed violence that was predicated upon voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to a term of 17 1/2 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of murder and two counts of armed violence. Defendant entered a guilty plea to voluntary manslaughter and armed violence that was based upon voluntary manslaughter. The circuit court sentenced defendant on the greater offense of armed violence. The court affirmed defendant's voluntary manslaughter conviction, vacated his armed violence conviction, and remanded the action for resentencing. The crime of armed violence was not to have been predicated upon voluntary manslaughter. Even though Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) provided that there was no appeal from a guilty plea unless defendant filed a motion to withdraw his plea and to vacate the judgment in the trial court, the argument that a criminal charge was void could have been raised at any time regardless of whether it was properly preserved for review. The State conceded that defendant's argument was correct on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for voluntary manslaughter, vacated defendant's plea of guilty to armed violence that was based on voluntary manslaughter, and remanded the action to the circuit court for resentencing on voluntary manslaughter.

 

981 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bormet


No. 84-0587


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


142 Ill. App. 3d 422; 491 N.E.2d 1281; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2077; 96 Ill. Dec. 821



March 31, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Martin E. McDonough, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on the state's charge of deceptive practice for knowingly issuing a check without sufficient funds in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17-1(B)(d) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of deceptive practice for knowingly issuing a check without sufficient funds in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17-1(B)(d) (1983). Defendant sought review of his conviction, arguing that the state had not met its burden of proving guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court reversed. The court found that defendant gave the seller a check to cover the cost of goods and that there were sufficient funds in defendant's account to cover the check when written. The court further found that defendant's conviction was based on an inference of intent to defraud. The court held the inference inapplicable in this case. The court said that an inference of guilt could have been drawn from proven facts if there was a rational connection between the proven fact and the inferred fact, the inferred fact more likely than not flowed from the proven fact, and the inference was supported by corroborating evidence. The court found that the state had not produced any corroborating evidence that supported the inference of intent. Therefore, the court said, the inference itself could not have supported the conclusion that defendant intended to defraud the seller.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction on the state's charge of deceptive practice for knowingly issuing a check without sufficient funds.

People v. Price

OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief without specifying its findings of fact and conclusions of law. The court affirmed the dismissal and held that, under § 122-2.1 (Ill. Rev. Further, the challenged provisions of § 122-2.1 were deemed constitutional based on prior cases in which the same provisions were examined in light of the constitutional mandates of separation of powers, equal protection, and due process. Further, defendant's challenge to that portion of the statute that required assignment of a trial judge not associated with the original proceeding was not preserved for appeal. Finally, appointment of counsel at the post-conviction stage was not mandatory where the petition was dismissed as being frivolous or without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

People v. Hope


No. 3-85-0242


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


142 Ill. App. 3d 171; 491 N.E.2d 785; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2043; 96 Ill. Dec. 506



March 27, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of attempted murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and armed violence, and sentenced him to concurrent terms of 30 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) his conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault required reversal because the sex assault law of which his offense was a part was so unreasonable in its definitions and applications as to violate the due process clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions; (2) he should not have been convicted of attempted murder; and (3) the trial court did not grant him the proper number of days against his sentence. Upon review, the court held that defendant should not have been convicted of armed violence, and that the trial court did not grant defendant the proper number of days against his sentence. The fact that defendant stabbed the victim four times in rapid succession, that there were no intervening acts or events, that there was a single victim, and that all of the stabbings occurred at the same location led to the conclusion that defendant's conduct gave rise to only one offense. Defendant should not have been convicted of both attempted murder and armed violence.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for armed violence, affirmed his convictions and sentences for attempted murder and aggravated criminal sexual assault, and gave defendant 44 days credit time against each of his two remaining concurrent terms of 30 years imprisonment.

People v. Brown


No. 5-84-0287


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


142 Ill. App. 3d 139; 491 N.E.2d 486; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2037; 96 Ill. Dec. 440



March 24, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. William H. South, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which summarily dismissed the defendant's pro se petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (Supp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of murder and filed a petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (Supp. 1984), claiming denial of his constitutional rights through ineffective assistance of counsel at both the trial and appellate levels. The trial court summarily dismissed the defendant's petition. The defendant appealed, contending that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (Supp. 1984) was unconstitutional because it allowed summary dismissal of post-conviction petitions deemed "frivolous" or "patently without merit" prior to appointment of counsel. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded with directions, and held that the defendant was denied adequate representation by counsel and that the trial court's summary dismissal of the defendant's post-conviction petition in violation of the mandatory 30-day rule of para. 122-2.1 was void. The defendant's attorney candidly admitted that she had been unable to comply, prior to dismissal of the defendant's pro se petition, with her obligation to properly investigate and present claims for post-conviction relief. The trial court's order of dismissal was untimely under para. 122-2.1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the defendant's pro se petition for post-conviction relief, and remanded with directions to order the defendant's petition docketed for further consideration.

 

985 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Gasoline Dealers Asso. v. Chicago


No. 85-0988


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 976; 491 N.E.2d 112; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2008; 96 Ill. Dec. 298



March 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an association and various service stations and others, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their suit against appellees, a city, its department of revenue, and its director of revenue, which challenged the constitutionality of an ordinance that imposed a seven cent tax on the sale of leaded gasoline in the city.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted the Chicago Leaded Gasoline Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 200.9 (1984), which imposed a seven cent tax on the sale of leaded gasoline in Chicago. Appellants brought an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against the city, the department, and its director challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the suit. In affirming on appeal, the court held that: (1) the ordinance was unambiguously a taxing measure with the purpose of raising revenue, it did not govern the time, place, or manner of the sale of leaded gasoline, and the penalties and fines imposed for failure to comply did not convert the ordinance into a regulatory measure; (2) as the ordinance was not a regulatory measure regulating clean air, no federal preemption occurred; (3) the tax uniformly applied to all purchasers of leaded gas and thus did not violate the uniformity provision of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970); (4) discouraging the sales of leaded gas was a rational basis for imposing the tax; and (5) that environmental matters were of statewide concern did not prohibit Chicago, a home rule city, from enacting a consumer tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which dismissed appellants' suit.

In re D.T.


No. 84-1329


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 1036; 490 N.E.2d 1361; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2014; 96 Ill. Dec. 156



March 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Vincent Bentivenga, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a, juvenile, challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of and sentenced him for involuntary manslaughter under the Juvenile Court Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(6)(a) (1983).


OVERVIEW: A defendant, who was a juvenile, was accused of murder. Under the Juvenile Court Act (Act), defendant was automatically tried as an adult. After a bench trial, the court found defendant guilty of involuntary manslaughter. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(6)(c) provided that when a juvenile who was tried as an adult was convicted of a lesser offense, the trial court had discretion to sentence defendant under the Act or under general criminal statutes. The trial court sentenced defendant under general Illinois criminal law. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed and held that the state's reference to defendant's prior criminal history in the grand jury proceedings was not error because grand juries did not have the same technical rules concerning evidence as trials did. The state did not misinform the grand jurors about the legal standard for murder. The Act's distinction between treating defendants of a certain age as adults was not a violation of defendant's equal protection and due process rights. The trial court demonstrated that it considered the factors set out in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(3)(a) when it sentenced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for involuntary manslaughter.

Fuller v. Kusper


No. 86-0556


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 1074; 491 N.E.2d 87; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2018; 96 Ill. Dec. 273



March 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed an order of defendants, the officers of the county electoral board, which found the candidate ineligible to be named on a ballot.


OVERVIEW: The candidate collected over 12,000 signatures to be named on a ballot for sheriff, and filed over 8,000. The county officers electoral board disqualified over 3,000 votes, and found that the remaining votes were insufficient under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-10(c) (1983) to get the candidate on the ballot. The trial court affirmed the board's decision. On appeal, the candidate challenged para. 7-10(c) on constitutional grounds. The court found that para. 7-10(c) did not violate equal protection because the State had a valid interest in limiting ballot access to serious candidates, a minimum signature requirement was a constitutional means to do so, and the statute applied equally to all people seeking to run for sheriff. The fact that those seeking to run for judge had lower signature requirements did not violate equal protection. Further, the requirement that the candidate collect one-half of one percent of the qualified electors of his party cast at the last general election in his county was not so onerous a burden as to deny the candidate's first amendment and due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the board's finding of the candidate's ineligibility.

People v. Hall


No. 2-85-0231


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


143 Ill. App. 3d 766; 491 N.E.2d 757; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 2255; 96 Ill. Dec. 478



March 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 6, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John W. Nielsen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a conviction and sentence from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois). Defendant was convicted of the offense of obscenity, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11--20(a)(1) (1983), as a result of the sale of an allegedly obscene magazine. He was sentenced to 140 days' imprisonment and a fine of $ 1,000.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant guilty of obscenity. The court imposed a sentence of imprisonment and a fine. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) defendant's public opinion evidence regarding community standards regarding sexually explicit material did not require the state to do more to sustain a conviction than introduce the allegedly obscene magazine into evidence because the survey did not ask whether the magazine in question was acceptable regarding obscene materials; (2) the trial court properly refused to tender defendant's instruction on community standards because it singled them out as the most important evidence in the case and it was argumentative; (3) the trial court properly permitted the state to cross-examine defendant's expert psychiatric witness or any error in the cross-examination was harmless; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing incarceration on defendant; and (5) the Illinois obscenity statute was constitutional. The court concluded that the state met its burden in proving defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of obscenity and that the jury's determination of his guilt was correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for obscenity as a result of the sale of an obscene magazine.

People v. Jenkins


No. 4-85-0331


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


141 Ill. App. 3d 602; 490 N.E.2d 953; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1949; 95 Ill. Dec. 861



March 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Woodford County; the Hon. Richard M. Baner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Woodford County (Illinois), which accepted the guilty plea of defendant and convicted him of home invasion and residential burglary. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the indictment, he contended that the plea was not voluntary, he argued that the burglary statute was unconstitutional, and defendant challenged the sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the home of an elderly victim and assaulted her, although defendant did not plead guilty to sexual assault. Defendant contended that the indictment was insufficient because it did not contain an allegation that he used force. Defendant's challenge to the voluntariness of the plea was raised because he claimed he was not told that the victim would testify at sentencing. Defendant contended that the circuit court improperly relied on prejudicial and hearsay evidence of other crimes or bad conduct in sentencing. On appeal, the court affirmed in large part. The challenge to the indictment was waived by the voluntary guilty plea. Further, defendant stipulated to an amended indictment that added the use of force language. Defendant waived the voluntariness issue by the failure to raise it below. The constitutionality of the burglary statute was upheld in case law. The sentencing issue failed because the circuit court was not confined to the evidence at the guilty plea, and further, any error was harmless. However, defendant was improperly ordered to pay restitution because the circuit court did not admonish him on the issue.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed in part and vacated in part. They were affirmed in all respects except for the restitution aspect of the sentence, which was vacated.

People v. Beavers


No. 3-85-0285


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


141 Ill. App. 3d 790; 491 N.E.2d 438; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1977; 96 Ill. Dec. 392



March 6, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing April 17, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of delivery of a controlled substance and the possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant alleged entrapment, the propriety and constitutionality of a fine, the improper valuation of cocaine, and the ordering of restitution to a policing agency.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in cocaine sales with her ex-husband. The ex-husband contacted the Metropolitan Area Narcotics Squad (MANS) because of alleged concern about the children. MANS began an investigation. Defendant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance and the possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. She contended that a MANS agent and her ex-husband entrapped her into dealing drugs. On appeal, the court held that the entrapment defense failed because defendant's alleged fear and reluctance to deal drugs were not controlling when she independently gave the agent drugs on several occasions. Defendant used cocaine and had knowledge of drug terminology and equipment. The mandatory fine of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 9 -- 1.1 (1983) was not repealed by implication. Further, the statute was constitutional even if it contained no provisions related to a defendant's financial situation. The agent properly established the street value of the cocaine. However, defendant was actually convicted of a lesser amount, and the fine was reduced. Whether the circuit court could have ordered restitution to MANS was waived by the failure to object.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but modified the sentence by reducing the fine.

Street v. Hubert


No. 85-0615


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 871; 491 N.E.2d 29; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1989; 96 Ill. Dec. 215



March 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff natural mother appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her action against defendant adoptive parents to set aside the adoption decree and to enforce the terms of an oral agreement allegedly made between the parties prior to the adoption.


OVERVIEW: The natural mother gave her four year old child to her parents in adoption with an oral agreement that she would be given visitation and, eventually, the child. Six years later, she brought an action to enforce the oral agreement or to annul the adoption. The trial court dismissed her action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court retroactively applied the 12-month statute of limitations of the amendment to the adoption statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1513 (1983), and found that the mother's action was time-barred. The mother urged the court to begin the time tolling when she discovered the adoptive parents were not going to honor the oral agreement. The court found the purpose of the adoption act was to promote stable family relationships free from unnecessary intrusion and this purpose would be frustrated by applying the discovery rule. The court held the mother was not denied due process because the statute of limitations was reasonably related to the state's interest. The court refused to consider the constitutionality of the adoption act because it did not affect the mother because her action was time-barred. The court found the oral agreement to be unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the natural mother's action to annul the adoption or to enforce an oral agreement.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff farmer taxpayers challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois), which granted motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, the supervisor of assessments and the Chairman of the Board of Review of Henry County, in the farmers' § 1983 action because the farmers had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Nine farmer taxpayers properly perfected their objections to an assessment and responded to the application of the tax collector to sell land on which taxes were delinquent. They brought a class action, alleging that defendants deprived them of rights, privileges, or immunities secured by the Constitution under § 1983. The trial court dismissed their complaint as premature. On appeal, the court determined that the farmer taxpayers needed to seek protection of their federal rights by state remedies when those remedies were plain, adequate, and complete. The court found that Illinois principles of administrative and judicial review were a plain, speedy, and efficient remedy. The court also concluded that the case did not involve the absence of power of the defendants to do the act charged nor any unique situation of the farmers justifying equitable relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court decision that dismissed the farmers' § 1983 action.

People v. Patroff

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), for selling obscene materials.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer went into a bookstore. The store required a "browsing" fee, which the officer paid to defendant, who was working there. When defendant saw the officer dictating into a tape recorder, defendant asked the officer to leave. Based on his observations, the officer obtained a search warrant. A search was conducted, and defendant was charged and convicted of selling obscene materials. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 was not unconstitutional because the definition of "prurient" interest was a shameful or morbid interest in nudity, sex, or excretion, not a normal sexual curiosity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling obscene materials.

People v. Palmer


Nos. 84-718, 84-719 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 234; 490 N.E.2d 154; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1900; 95 Ill. Dec. 681



February 27, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael P. Toomin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted defendant of aggravated arson under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1), (3) (1983) and aggravated battery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(a) (1983), following a bench trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1983) of the aggravated arson statute was unconstitutional and that the trial court abused its discretion by allowing his attorney to represent him while under a per se conflict of interest, thus depriving him of his right to effective assistance of counsel. The court reversed and remanded defendant's convictions and sentences based on a state supreme court decision that held that § 20-1.1(a)(3) was unconstitutional and violated due process because it was overbroad and punished innocent as well as culpable conduct in setting fires. The court applied the reasoning of the supreme court decision and determined that § 20-1.1(a)(1) of the aggravated arson statute was also unconstitutional. In so ruling, the court held that culpable intent was not inherent in the very act of setting a fire or using explosives in a building, knowing that persons are present therein. However, under § 20-1.1(a)(1), as under § 20-1.1(a)(3), an innocent person who committed such acts could be convicted of a Class X felony. The court also concluded that defense counsel had a potential conflict of interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated arson and aggravated battery and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Porter


No. 84-1800


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


141 Ill. App. 3d 208; 490 N.E.2d 47; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1897; 95 Ill. Dec. 574



February 18, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. William Cousins, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the denial of his post-conviction appeal by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant's convictions for attempted murder, two counts of aggravated battery and armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8 -- 4, 12 -- 4(a), 12 -- 4(b)(1), 33A -- 2 (1979) were affirmed pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 23, 87 Ill. 2d R. 23. Subsequently, his county public defender withdrew as counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pro se filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which was dismissed as frivolous. On appeal, the court affirmed because defendant did not overcome the strong presumption that the applicable statute, § 122 -- 2.1 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963 (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 --2(a) (1983 Supp.) was constitutional. The court found that the circuit court was not required to include written findings of fact and conclusions of law in it's decision despite the Code's use of the word "shall" because the context and statutory purposes required the statute to be permissive. Otherwise the statute would violate separation of powers principles by intruding on the court's exercise of judicial discretion. The court found that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c), 87 Ill. 2d R. 651(c) did not apply because that rule required the appointment of counsel in post-conviction matters only in the appellate court. The Code did not violate the doctrine of equal protection because defendant was not similarly situated to someone pursuing a direct appeal and did not violate defendant's due process rights because the state was not required to provide counsel on discretionary appeals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing defendant's post-conviction appeal.

People v. David


No. 84-0803


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


141 Ill. App. 3d 243; 489 N.E.2d 1124; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1901; 95 Ill. Dec. 396



February 14, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which, following a jury trial, found defendant guilty of unlawful possession with the intent to deliver 200 grams or more of a substance containing a derivative of barbituric acid, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(5) (1981), and sentenced him to a term of 30 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a search of his house produced Phenobarbital tablets and a large sum of cash. Defendant did not appear at his trial, and he was found guilty, in absentia, of unlawful possession with the intent to deliver 200 grams or more of a substance containing a derivative of barbituric acid and sentenced in absentia. Later, defendant appeared and appealed. The court affirmed and held, inter alia, that: (1) defendant's motion for a Franks hearing was insufficient on its face; (2) the trial court had a substantial basis for concluding that probable cause existed for a search of defendant's house and garage; (3) defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt; (4) defendant, having chosen not to question a person in court and available to testify, could not then claim he was denied his right to confront that person; (5) defendant's volunteered statements were not barred by the Fifth Amendment, and their admissibility was not affected by Miranda; (6) the prosecutor did not intend or calculate to call the jury's attention to defendant's failure to testify; and (7) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to the maximum 30-year term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found defendant guilty of unlawful possession with the intent to deliver 200 grams or more of a substance containing a derivative of barbituric acid and sentenced defendant to a term of 30 years' imprisonment.

 

997 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


County of Kane v. Carlson


Nos. 85-0228, 85-0230 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


140 Ill. App. 3d 814; 489 N.E.2d 467; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1783; 95 Ill. Dec. 246



February 7, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county brought an action in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) seeking a declaratory judgment and an injunction restraining defendant Illinois State Labor Relations Board (Board) from proceeding on a petition by defendant union requesting a representation election for deputy circuit clerks. After the injunction was granted, the Board and union appealed; and the circuit clerk cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The union representing deputy circuit clerks filed a representation petition with the Board, and the county obtained an injunction preventing the Board from proceeding on the petition. In reversing the injunction, the court held that the county's claim that "appointees" were not "employees" for purposes of the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act (PLRA) (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 1601 et seq. (1984 Supp.) was without support in the statute. The legislature intended the term "employee" to include persons appointed to positions. The offices of the chief judge and circuit clerk could only have been deemed to be authorities of the State of Illinois, and insofar as they acted as employers in their official capacities they were persons acting within the scope of their authority on behalf of the state in dealing with its employees. Therefore, to the extent that the chief judge or circuit clerk might have been employers of the deputy circuit clerks, they were public employers and the deputy circuit clerks public employees under the PLRA. The court concluded that the PLRA was valid on its face and that any separation of powers defect in the statute would only occur in its application.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the injunction dissolved. On the court's own motion, the cause was certified to the Supreme Court of Illinois as involving questions of such importance that they should be decided by that court.

Calhoon v. Communications Systems Constr., Inc.


No. 5-85-0242


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


140 Ill. App. 3d 1012; 489 N.E.2d 23; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1808; 95 Ill. Dec. 71



February 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County; the Hon. James R. Williamson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners and defendant cable company appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois), which entered judgment for the property owners in their trespass suit against the cable company and ordered that the cable company raise its cable line over the property owners' land.


OVERVIEW: The cable company constructed cable lines across the property owners' land despite learning that it had no easement to do so. The property owners filed a trespass suit seeking damages and removal of the cable company's equipment. The lower court awarded damages to the property owners, refused to order the removal of the equipment, and ordered the cable company to raise its lines. Both parties appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part. The court determined that although it was satisfied that the cost of removing the equipment from the land was great and that the benefit to the property owners of doing so was small, the cable company's encroachment upon the land was intentional. The court found that the cable company admitted it had no right to be on the property owners' land, the property owners protested early on in the construction, and the cable company persisted in completing the very structure it subsequently claimed was too expensive to move. The court also concluded that, contrary to the cable company's claims, injunctive relief against illegal appropriation of property could not be defeated by any claim that the public interest required it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment awarding damages to property owners' for the cable company's intentional encroachment upon their land and reversed and remanded the judgment in so far as it did not require the cable company to remove the equipment from the land.

People v. Wright


No. 84-2754


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


140 Ill. App. 3d 576; 488 N.E.2d 1344; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1746; 95 Ill. Dec. 1



January 28, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. Divito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and one count of unlawful use of weapons. The trial court sentenced defendant to a period of six years incarceration on the possession with intent to deliver finding and two years incarceration on the unlawful use of weapons finding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, unlawful use of weapons, and bribery. Over defense counsel's objections, three officers testified about various weapons and ammunition seized during the search of defendant's apartment. The items of evidence were kept at the state's table during its case in chief. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, holding that: (1) the trial court did not err in admitting the guns and ammunition into evidence because the evidence was properly offered by the state to establish the motive for defendant's alleged bribe; (2) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(7) (1983) was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant was charged with conduct to which the statute clearly applied; and (3) the trial court did not err when, in answer to a jury question during deliberations, it responded that possession of a shotgun with a barrel less than 18 inches in length was sufficient to convict for unlawful use of a weapon, even without specific knowledge that the barrel was in fact less than 18 inches because § 24-1(a)(7) did not require that defendant in fact knew the shotgun's barrel measured less than 18 inches.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and unlawful use of weapons and the sentences imposed for his convictions.

People v. Jackson


No. 85-0088


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


140 Ill. App. 3d 318; 488 N.E.2d 1056; 1986 Ill. App. LEXIS 1716; 94 Ill. Dec. 809



January 24, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. Harris H. Agnew, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted him of residential burglary and sentenced him to an extended term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The complainant had testified that a camera, some photographic film, a portable television, a police scanner, a microwave oven, and a telephone had been taken from her residence. Defendant was stopped the evening of the burglary in response to a radio broadcast about a suspect vehicle in the burglary. It was during that stop that defendant fled into an open field, only to be apprehended at a later date. The police found a camera and film in the car that matched the items reportedly missing from the complainant's home. On review, the court noted that defendant's flight tended to show his consciousness of guilt that was corroborative evidence to support his conviction. The court further found that contrary to defendant's contention, the prosecutor's comments on the credibility of certain witnesses was permissible when the comments were drawn from facts in evidence or when the comments constituted reasonable inferences drawn from those facts. In affirming, the court concluded by finding no error in the imposition of an extended term of imprisonment, noting that the trial judge had properly considered the relevant factors before imposition of such a sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.
